عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے ان میں سے کسی ایک کی طرف سے واقع کرناممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے وہ مامور ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ اور یہ بھی ممکن نہیں کہ اس کے بعد نائب اس کو ایک کی طرف سے کر دے۔ بر خلاف اس کے جب اپنے والدین کی طرف سے حج کیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اس حج کو والدین میں سے کسی ایک کے واسطے کر دے۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنے عمل کا ثواب ایک کے واسطے ہدیہ کرنے میں متبرع ہے یا دونوں کے واسطے ہدیہ کر دے۔ پس وہ حج کے سبب ثواب واقع ہونے کے بعد اپنے اختیار پر ہے۔ اور یہاں نائب بحکم آمر کرتا ہے۔ اور حال یہ کہ نائب نے دونوں موکلوں کے حکم کی مخالفت کی۔ اس لئے یہ حج نائب کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، ایک شخص کو دو شخصوں نے وکیل بنایا کہ وہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے حج کرے۔ پس اس وکیل نے دونوں کی طرف سے ایک حج کا احرام باندھا یعنی دونوں میں سے کسی کے واسطے متعین کئے بغیر افعال حج شروع کر دیئے تو یہ حج حاجی وکیل ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا ۔ اور دونوں موکلوں نے جتنا جتنا خرچ دیا ہے ہر ایک کے لئے اس کے خرچہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس مسئلہ کی جو دلیل بیان فرمائی ہے بظاہر دلیل اور مدلول کے درمیان مطابقت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ مدلول تو یہ ہے کہ حج حاجی یعنی وکیل کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا۔ اور موکلوں کے لئے نفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اور دلیل میں کہا ہے کہ حج آمریعنی موکلوں کی طرف سے واقع ہوتا ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی مطابقت نہیں ہے۔ صاحب نہایہ نے فرمایا کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی بیان کردہ دلیل اس حکم کی ہے جو کتاب میں مذکور نہیں ہے۔ اور تقدیر کلام یہ ہے کہ حاجی یعنی وکیل دونوں امر کرنے والوں کے لئے خرچہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اس نے دونوں کے امر کی مخالفت کی ہے اور خرچہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوگا ۔ اگر آمریعنی مؤکل کے امر کی موافقت کی ہو اس لئے کہ اس وقت حج آمر ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ حتی کہ حاجی وکیل فریضہ حج سے سبکدوش نہیں ہو سکے گا ۔ اور یہاں صورت یہ ہے کہ اس نے آمر کی مخالفت کی سے ابدانج آمر کی طرف سے واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ مامور یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ صاحب عنایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دلیل اور مدلول کے درمیان مطابقت حاصل ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ یہی حج من وجہ تو حاجی یعنی وکیل کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا۔ اور من وجہ دونوں امر کرنے والوں کی طرف۔ اول کی دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ دونوں امر کرنے والوں میں سے ہر ایک نے اس بات کا امر کیا تھا کہ بغیر کسی کو شریک کئے اس حج کو خالص اس کے لئے کر دے پس جب وکیل حاجی نے دونوں کی طرف سے نیت کی تو اس نے ہر ایک کے امیر کی مخالفت کی اور جب امر کرنے والوں کے امر کی مخالفت کی تو یہ فعل آمر کی طرف سے واقع نہ ہوگا بلکہ مامور یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا۔ اور حاجی مخالفت آمرین کی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے اس مال کا ضامن ہوگا جو انہوں نے خرچ کے لئے اس کو دیا تھا۔ اور چونکہ ان دونوں میں سے کسی کو کسی پر ترجیح نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ بھی ممکن نہیں ہے کہ اس حج کو ان میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے ٹھہرا دے اور نہ ترجیح بلا مرحج کا الزام آئے گا۔ اسلئے یہ حج بجائے آمر کے مامور یعنی حاجی ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ اور اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ حج تو مامور ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوا مگر بعد میں ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے کر دے۔ جیسے والدین کی طرف سے کسی نے حج کیا پھر کسی ایک کے لئے کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ چونکہ والدین نے نہ تو اس کو حج کرنے کا امر کیا ہے اور نہ خرچہ دیا ہے بلکہ یہ شخص متبرع ہے اور متبرع کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اپنے عمل کا ثواب ایک کے لئے کر دے یا دونوں کے لئے ۔ پس وہ ثواب کا سبب یعنی حج واقع ہونے کے بعد اپنے اختیار پر باقی رہے گا۔ اور یہاں وکیل حج کرتا ہے آمر کے حکم سے اور اس نے دونوں موکلوں وں کی مخالفت کی تو یہ حج وکیل یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا نہ کہ مؤکل اور آمر کی طرف سے۔ اور ثانی یعنی اس کی دلیل کہ حج آمر کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا یہ ہے کہ حاجی اپنے اس حج سے اگر اپنے ذمہ کے حج فرض کو ادا کرنے کی نیت کرلے تو یہ فریضہ حج سے سبکدوش نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ یہ نج ما مور یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع نہیں ہوا بلکہ آمر یہ حج گا کی طرف سے واقع ہوا ہے۔ حج نفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا بشرطیکہ دونوں موکلوں وں کے مال سے خرچ کیا ہو ويضمن النفقة إن أنفَقَ مِنْ مَالِهِمَا لأَنَّهُ صَرَفَ نَفَقَةَ الأمر إلى حَحِ نَفْسِهِ ترجمہ اور وہ نفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا بشرطیکہ دونوں موکلوں وں کے مال سے خرچ کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس نے موکلوں کا مال اپنے ذاتی آج کے لئے صرف کیا ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
He said: And whoever two men command him to perform Hajj on behalf of each of them, and he pronounces talbiyah for one Hajj for both of them, then it is for the pilgrim (the deputy) and he guarantees the expenses, because the Hajj occurs on behalf of the commander, such that the pilgrim does not exit from the obligatory Hajj of Islam. And each of them commanded him to make the Hajj exclusively for him without partnership, and it is not possible to make it occur for one of them due to lack of priority, so it occurs for the commanded person (the deputy). And it is not possible for him to make it for one of them after that, contrary to when he performs Hajj on behalf of his parents, for then he has the option to make it for one of them, because he is a volunteer in giving the reward of his deed to one of them or both of them, so he remains with his choice after it occurs as a cause for reward. And here he acts by the command of the commander, and he has opposed their command, so it occurs for him.
Source pages p. 518

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on a specific case of delegated Hajj (Hajj al-Niyabah). The passage opens with the ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah: if two persons appoint a single deputy to perform Hajj on behalf of each, and the deputy pronounces talbiyah for one Hajj intending it for both, then the Hajj is considered to be for the deputy himself, and he is liable to return the expenses given by both principals. The reasoning provided is that the deputy was commanded by each principal to perform an exclusive Hajj for that principal alone. Since he combined the two commands into one action, he disobeyed both. Moreover, there is no priority to assign the Hajj to one over the other, nor can he later assign it to one arbitrarily without evidence. Therefore, the Hajj falls to the deputy himself. The proof cited is that if the deputy had performed this Hajj intending his own obligatory Hajj, he would not be discharged from it, indicating that the action is attributed to the deputy, not to the principals. The text then distinguishes this case from the voluntary performance of Hajj for one's parents. In the parents' case, the deputy is a volunteer (mutabarri‘) who has not been commanded or paid; he may later assign the reward to either parent at his discretion because he retains ownership of the reward. In the commanded case, the deputy acts under a binding command and has violated it, so he loses the ability to direct the act to either principal. The commentary by Ashraf al-Hidayah further clarifies that the apparent contradiction in the proof is resolved by noting that the Hajj has a dual aspect: from one perspective, it is for the deputy (due to disobedience), and from another, it is for the principals (since if he intended his own Hajj it would not suffice). The final ruling remains that the Hajj is for the deputy, but the reasoning confirms that the act would have been for the principals had the deputy complied. The condition for liability of expenses is that the deputy spent the principals' money on this Hajj; if he used his own money, he is not liable for return but may still owe something? The text explicitly says he guarantees the expenses if he spent from their wealth, because he used their funds for his own pilgrimage.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The verbal declaration of intention for Hajj or Umrah, typically 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk', which initiates the state of ihram.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Financial expenses provided by the principals to the deputy for the journey and rituals of Hajj.
ضامن (damin): Legally responsible to return the equivalent amount of money spent, because the funds were used for an unauthorized purpose.
مامور (ma'mur): The person commanded to perform the act; in this passage, the deputy who was ordered by the principals.
آمر (amir): The person giving the command; the principal who hires or appoints the deputy for Hajj.
متبرع (mutabarri'): One who performs an act of worship voluntarily, without being obligated or compensated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what is the status of a Hajj performed by a deputy who was appointed by two principals to perform separate Hajj for each, but instead performs one Hajj for both?
A) The Hajj is valid for both principals.
B) The Hajj is for the deputy himself, and he must return the expenses.
C) The Hajj is invalid, and a dam is due.
D) The deputy may later choose which principal it is for.

Key Takeaway
Disobeying a specific command and using the principal's funds for a combined act makes the act belong to the deputy, not the principal.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
12 min
Ruling on Deputy Performing Hajj for Two Principals with Unspecified Intention
Explains the ruling when a deputy performs Hajj for two unspecified principals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a deputy performs Hajj for two unspecified principals and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding specification after ambiguous ihram.

Core Idea
A deputy who performs Hajj for two principals without specification acts for himself; ambiguity in ihram can be rectified by specification before actions.

This lesson delves into a nuanced scenario in Hanafi fiqh: a deputy (wakil) appointed by two principals (muwakkil) to perform Hajj. The source text examines what happens when the deputy's intention is ambiguous—either intending for both simultaneously or for one unspecified—and whether subsequent specification before completing the Hajj actions can remedy the ambiguity. We will unpack the general ruling, the underlying reasoning, and an important intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and general ruling
Read the initial part of the passage where the deputy performs Hajj for two principals without specifying. Note that he opposes both commands, so the Hajj is valid but counts for himself, and he must repay expenses.
2
Examine the sub-case of ambiguous ihram
Focus on the section beginning with 'وإن أبهَمَ الإحرام'. Understand that the deputy ties ihram intending for one of two principals without naming which. The passage then discusses whether specification before completing the actions (tawaf, sa'y) can change the attribution.
3
Understand Abu Yusuf's position (qiyas)
Abu Yusuf argues that even if the deputy specifies before actions, the Hajj remains for himself. His analogy (qiyas) compares it to an agent buying a slave for an unspecified principal—the purchase is for the agent. The key illa is that the deputy was commanded to specify from the start, and ambiguity is opposition.
4
Understand the istihsan position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
The majority view relies on istihsan: ihram is a means, not an end; specification before the actions corrects the ambiguity. Unlike a volunteer who can assign reward after the fact, the deputy's act is conditional on his mandate, but specification within the window of actions is acceptable.
The passage distinguishes between ambiguity of the person (who deserves the Hajj) and ambiguity of the type of pilgrimage (Hajj vs. Umrah) where the deputy has free choice.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: specification before completing the Hajj actions is valid, and the Hajj counts for the specified principal. The thamarah al-khilaf is that Abu Yusuf would require the deputy to repeat the Hajj for the principal, while the majority allows the specification to suffice.

کتاب الحج
نے دونوں کے امر کی مخالفت کی ہے اور خرچہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوگا ۔ اگر آمر یعنی مؤکل کے امر کی موافقت کی ہو اس لئے کہ اس وقت حج آمر ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ حتی کہ حاجی وکیل فریضہ حج سے سبکدوش نہیں ہو سکے گا ۔ اور یہاں صورت یہ ہے کہ اس نے آمر کی مخالفت کی سے ابدانج آمر کی طرف سے واقع نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ مامور یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔
صاحب عنایہ کہتے ہیں کہ دلیل اور مدلول کے درمیان مطابقت حاصل ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ یہی حج من وجہ تو حاجی یعنی وکیل کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا۔ اور من وجہ دونوں امر کرنے والوں کی طرف سے۔ اول کی دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ دونوں امر کرنے والوں میں سے ہر ایک نے اس بات کا امر کیا تھا کہ بغیر کسی کو شریک کئے اس حج کو خالص اس کے لئے کر دے پس جب وکیل حاجی نے دونوں کی طرف سے نیت کی تو اس نے ہر ایک کے امیر کی مخالفت کی اور جب امر کرنے والوں کے امر کی مخالفت کی تو یہ فعل آمر کی طرف سے واقع نہ ہوگا بلکہ مامور یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع ہو گا۔ اور حاجی مخالفت آمرین کی وجہ سے ان دونوں کے اس مال کا ضامن ہوگا جو انہوں نے خرچ کے لئے اس کو دیا تھا۔ اور چونکہ ان دونوں میں سے کسی کو کسی پر ترجیح نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ بھی ممکن نہیں ہے کہ اس حج کو ان میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے ٹھہرا دے اور نہ ترجیح بلا مرحج کا الزام آئے گا۔ اسلئے یہ حج بجائے آمر کے مامور یعنی حاجی ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ اور اگر کوئی یہ کہے کہ حج تو مامور ہی کی طرف سے واقع ہوا مگر بعد میں ان دونوں میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے کر دے۔ جیسے والدین کی طرف سے کسی نے حج کیا پھر کسی ایک کے لئے کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ چونکہ والدین نے نہ تو اس کو حج کرنے کا امر کیا ہے اور نہ خرچہ دیا ہے بلکہ یہ شخص متبرع ہے اور متبرع کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اپنے عمل کا ثواب ایک کے لئے کر دے یا دونوں کے لئے ۔ پس وہ ثواب کا سبب یعنی حج واقع ہونے کے بعد اپنے اختیار پر باقی رہے گا۔ اور یہاں وکیل حج کرتا ہے آمر کے حکم سے اور اس نے دونوں موکلوں کی مخالفت کی تو یہ حج وکیل یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا نہ کہ مؤکل اور آمر کی طرف سے۔ اور ثانی یعنی اس کی دلیل کہ حج آمر کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا یہ ہے کہ حاجی اپنے اس حج سے اگر اپنے ذمہ کے حج فرض کو ادا کرنے کی نیت کرلے تو یہ فریضہ حج سے سبکدوش نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ یہ حج مامور یعنی حاجی کی طرف سے واقع نہیں ہوا بلکہ آمر کی طرف سے واقع ہوا ہے۔
ويضمن النفقة إن أنفَقَ مِنْ مَالِهِمَا لأَنَّهُ صَرَفَ نَفَقَةَ الأمر إلى حَجِّ نَفْسِهِ
ترجمہ اور وہ نفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا بشرطیکہ دونوں موکلوں کے مال سے خرچ کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس نے موکلوں کا مال اپنے ذاتی حج کے لئے صرف کیا ہے۔
تشریح واضح ہے۔
وَإِن أَنهَمَ الإحرام بأن نوى عن أحدهما غيرَ عَيْنِ فَإِن مَضى على ذلك صار مخالفا لِعَدَمِ الْأُولَوِيَّةِ وَإِنْ عَيَّنَ أحَدَهُمَا قَبْلُ الْمَضى فكذلك عِندَ أَبِى يُوسُفَ وَهُوَ الْقِياسُ لأَنَّهُ مامور با لتعبير والأَنْهَامُ يُخَالِفُهُ فَيَقَعُ عَنْ نَفْسِهِ بِخِلافِ ما إذا لم يُعيّن حجّة أو عُمْرَةً حَيْثُ كَانَ لَهُ أَنْ يُعَينَ مَا شَاء لأن السيرة هناك مجهول وههنا المجهول مَنْ لَهُ الْحَقَّ وَجَهُ الإِسْتِحْسَان أَنَّ الْإِحْرَامَ شُرِع وسيلة إلى الأفعال لا مقصودا بنفْسِهِ وَالْمُنهم يُصْلِحُ وَسِيْلَةً بِوَاسِطَةِ التَّعْيِينِ فَاكْتُفِى بِهِ شَرَطًا بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا أَدَّى الأفعال عَلَى الْإِنْهَام لأنَّ الْمُوَدى لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّعْلِينَ فَصَارَ مُخَالِفًا
ترجمہ اور اگر وکیل نے احرام کو مبہم رکھا ہو بایں طور کہ ان دونوں موکلوں میں سے ایک غیر معین کی نیت کی ہے۔ پس اگر وہ اسی مبہم نیت پر گذر گیا تو بھی وکیل عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے اپنے موکلوں کا مخالف ہو گیا۔ اور اگر افعال ادا کرنے سے پہلے ان دونوں میں سے ایک متعین کر دیا تو ابو یوسف کے نزدیک یہی حکم ہے اور یہی قیاس ہے۔ کیونکہ وکیل تو معین کرنے پر مامور ہے اور مبہم کرنا اس کے مخالف ہے ۔ اس لئے یہ حج بھی خود اسی کی طرف سے واقع ہوگا۔ برخلاف اس کے جب اس نے حج یا عمرہ متعین نہیں کیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ جس کو چاہے متعین کرے۔ کیونکہ وہاں جو چیز اپنے اوپر لازم کی وہ مجہول ہے اور یہاں وہ شخص مجبول ہے جس کو حق ہے۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ احرام تو افعال حج ادا کرنے کا وسیلہ ہو کر مشروع ہوا ہے خود مقصود نہیں ہے۔ اور احرام مبہم بھی وسیلہ ہوسکتا ہے بواسطه تعیین کے۔ خاک شرط ہونے میں احرام مبہم کے ساتھ اکتفاء کر لیا گیا ہے۔ برخلاف ایسی صورت کے کہ جب ابہام کی حالت پر افعال ادا کر چکا۔ کیونکہ جو چیز ادا ہو چکی، تعیین کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی تو مخالف ہوا ۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وکیل نے احرام نہ خا مثالان اونوں مونگوں میں ایک نہ معین کی طرف سے حج ادا کرنے کی نیت کی ۔ ہوں اگر وکیل نے اس مبہم نیت کے ساتھ افعال نبی اور لے تو بھی میاں ندور نے اپنے موکلوں کی مالات ہیں۔ کیونکہ حج پورا ہونے کے بعد ران و کسی کے واسطے معین نہیں کر سکتا ورنہ تو تری با امرت کا انتبام آئے گا۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بہت ، کیل ہی کی طرف سے شمار ہوگا موگلوں کی طرف سے شمار نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر افعال حج ادا کرنے سے پہلے اس نے کسی ایک متعین کر لیا تو بھی ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حکم نہیں ہوتا کہ ج وکیل کی طرف سے ادا ہونہ کہ موکل کی طرف سے اور قیاس بھی یہی ہے لیکن استحسانا تعیین میں ہے اور یہی طرفین کا قول ہے۔ قیاس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ وکیل اس بات پر مامور ہے کہ وہ معین موکلوں کی طرف سے حج ادا کرے لیکن اس نے ابتداء اس کو جسم رکھا اور ابیا معین کے خلاف سے تو گویا وکیل نے موکلوں کی مخالفت کی۔ اور مخالفت آمر کی صورت میں وکیل کی طرف سے ادا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ مؤکل کی طرف سے۔ اس لئے یہ حج بھی خود اسی وکیل کی طرف سے ادا ہو گا ۔ جیسے دو شخصوں نے ایک آدمی کو علامہ خریدنے کا وکیل بنایا اس نے ان دونوں میں سے ایک غیر معین کے لئے غلام خرید لیا تو یہ خرید نا خود ما مور یعنی وکیل کے لئے ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس نے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کے لئے متعین کرنے کا ارادہ کیا تو تعیین صیح نہ ہوگی۔ اسی طرح یہاں بھی ابہام کے بعد متعین کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے اور اگر یہ سوال کیا جائے کہ اگرکسی
Book of Hajj. He opposed the command of both and will not be guarantor of expenses. If he followed the command of the principal, then the Hajj would be on behalf of the principal. Even the deputy would not be discharged from the obligatory Hajj. And here the case is that he opposed the principal, so the Hajj will not be on behalf of the principal but on behalf of the commanded one, i.e., the deputy. Sahib al-‘Inayah says that there is correspondence between the evidence and the conclusion. In this manner, this Hajj, from one aspect, will be on behalf of the deputy, and from another aspect, on behalf of both commanders. The proof of the first is that each of the two commanders had commanded him to perform Hajj exclusively for him without associating anyone. So when the deputy intended for both, he opposed each commander, and when he opposed the command of the commanders, this action will not be on behalf of the commander but on behalf of the commanded one, i.e., the deputy. And the deputy, because of opposing the commanders, will be guarantor of the wealth they gave him for expenses. And since there is no preference of one over the other, it is not possible to assign this Hajj to one of them, and the accusation of preference without a preferrer would arise. Therefore, this Hajj will be on behalf of the commanded one, i.e., the deputy himself. And if someone says that the Hajj occurred on behalf of the commanded one, but later he could assign it to one of them, just as when someone performs Hajj on behalf of parents and later assigns it to one, it is permissible, so here too it should be. The answer is that the parents did not command him to perform Hajj nor give expenses; rather he is a volunteer, and the volunteer has the option to give the reward of his action to one or both. So the cause of reward, i.e., the Hajj, remains under his control after it occurs. But here the deputy performs Hajj by the command of the principal, and he opposed both principals, so this Hajj will be on behalf of the deputy, not the principal. The second proof that the Hajj will be on behalf of the principal is that if the deputy intends to fulfill his own obligatory Hajj with this Hajj, he will not be discharged from the obligatory Hajj. From this, it is known that this Hajj did not occur on behalf of the deputy but on behalf of the principal. And he will be guarantor of expenses if he spent from their wealth because he spent the wealth of the principals on his own Hajj. The explanation is clear. And if he made the ihram ambiguous by intending for one of them unspecified, then if he continues on that, he becomes an opponent due to lack of preference. And if he specifies one of them before continuing, it is the same according to Abu Yusuf, and that is the analogy, because he is commanded to specify, and ambiguity opposes it, so it falls on himself. Unlike when he does not specify Hajj or Umrah, where he has the option to specify whichever he wants because there the matter is unknown, but here the unknown is who has the right. The basis of istihsan is that ihram is prescribed as a means to the actions, not as an end in itself, and ambiguous ihram can be a means through specification, so it is sufficed for the condition. Unlike when he performed the actions on ambiguity, because what has been performed does not accept specification, so he became an opponent. Translation: And if the deputy kept the ihram ambiguous, i.e., he intended one of the two principals unspecified, then if he passed with that ambiguous intention, the deputy became an opponent of his principals due to lack of preference. And if he specified one of them before performing the actions, according to Abu Yusuf the ruling is the same, and this is the analogy. Because the deputy is commanded to specify, and ambiguity opposes it, so this Hajj will also be on his own behalf. Unlike the case when he did not specify Hajj or Umrah, where he has the option to specify whichever he wants, because there what is necessary is unknown, but here the person who has the right is unknown. And the basis of istihsan is that ihram is prescribed as a means to perform the actions of Hajj, not an end itself. And ambiguous ihram can also be a means through specification. So it is sufficed with ambiguous ihram for the condition. Unlike the case when he performed the actions in a state of ambiguity, because what has been performed does not accept specification, so he became an opponent. Explanation: The issue is that if the deputy tied ihram with the intention of performing Hajj for one of two unspecified principals. If the deputy performed the actions with this ambiguous intention, then even then he opposes his principals. Because after completing Hajj, he cannot specify it for anyone, otherwise the accusation of preference without a preferrer would arise. Therefore, in this case too, it will be counted for the deputy, not for the principals. And if he specified one before performing the actions, then according to Abu Yusuf the ruling does not change, that it is performed on behalf of the deputy, not the principal, and analogy is also this. But istihsan permits specification, and this is the saying of the two (i.e., Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The basis of analogy is that the deputy is commanded to perform Hajj on behalf of specified principals, but he initially kept it ambiguous and acted against specification, so he opposed the principals. And in the case of opposing the commander, it is performed on behalf of the deputy, not the principal. So this Hajj will also be performed on behalf of the deputy himself. Just as if two persons appointed someone as agent to buy a slave, and he bought a slave for one of them unspecified, then this purchase is on behalf of the agent himself. And if he intended to specify one of them, the specification will not be valid. Similarly here, specifying after ambiguity is not valid. And if it is asked that if someone...
Source pages p. 519

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi fiqh: a person (wakil) is appointed by two principals (muwakkil) to perform Hajj on their behalf, each desiring exclusivity. The deputy, when performing the Hajj, intends to do it for both simultaneously (or for one unspecified). The ruling is that this Hajj is not valid on behalf of either principal but counts as the deputy's own Hajj, and he becomes liable for the expenses incurred. The text first establishes the general principle: if the deputy follows the command (i.e., performs Hajj for one specific principal), it is credited to that principal. If he violates the command (by intending for both or for an unspecified one), it becomes his own. The reasoning is that he opposed each principal's command, so the act cannot be attributed to them. The author then refutes a potential analogy to a volunteer performing Hajj for parents and later assigning the reward to one: in that case, the volunteer is not commanded and has freedom over the reward; here the deputy is commanded and has no such discretion. The passage then introduces a sub-case: if the deputy made the ihram ambiguous, intending to perform Hajj for one of two principals without specifying which, but before completing the actions (talbiyah, tawaf, sa'y, etc.) he specifies one. Abu Yusuf holds that even with subsequent specification, it remains the deputy's own Hajj (qiyas). The author presents the preferred hanafi position (credited to the two elders, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) based on istihsan: since ihram is a mere means to the actions, specification before completing the acts is valid, and the Hajj becomes for the specified principal. The distinction is made with the case where the deputy does not specify Hajj or Umrah at all—there he has full freedom to choose. The key difference is that here the object (the person) is unknown, not the type of worship. The commentary concludes by emphasizing the practical difference: according to the mufta bihi view, the deputy can validly specify before performing the bulk of Hajj actions.

Key Terms
موكل (muwakkil): The principal who appoints a deputy (wakil) to perform Hajj on his behalf.
وكيل (wakil): The deputy appointed to perform Hajj for another.
إحرام مبهم (ihram mubham): An ihram in which the person on whose behalf the Hajj is intended is unspecified.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here applied by Abu Yusuf to compare the deputy's action to an agent buying unspecified goods.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; here used to validate specification despite initial ambiguity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi school, if a deputy appointed by two principals to perform Hajj ties his ihram intending it for one of them unspecified, but then specifies one before completing the Hajj actions (e.g., before tawaf), what is the ruling?
A) The Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The Hajj counts for the deputy himself, not for either principal.
C) The Hajj counts for the specified principal, because specification before the actions is valid by istihsan.
D) The Hajj counts for both principals equally.

Key Takeaway
Ambiguity in the deputy's intention at ihram can be rectified by specification before completing the Hajj actions, according to the prevailing Hanafi view (istihsan).

Who Bears the Dam for Qiran When an Agent Performs It
Ruling with rational proof on agent's obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who must offer the dam for Hajj al-Qiran when performed by an agent, and explain the rationale based on the blessing of combining the two rites.

Core Idea
The dam for Qiran is a personal thanks for combining Hajj and Umrah, so it falls on the one who actually performs it — the agent.

This passage addresses a specific but important point in Hajj law: when a person appoints an agent to perform Hajj al-Qiran, who must bear the required dam? The source gives a clear ruling based on the nature of the dam as a thanksgiving (shukr) for the blessing of combining the two rites. Understanding this helps clarify the distinction between the physical performer and the one for whom the act is done.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
What is the factual scenario described? A principal orders an agent to perform Qiran on his behalf. What is the ruling? The dam is upon the one who performed the ihram—the agent.
The key phrase: 'فَالدَّمُ عَلَى مَنْ أَحْرَمَ' (the blood is upon the one who performed ihram).
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
What evidence is given? The dam is wajib as a thanks (شكرا) for the blessing Allah granted of combining the two rituals (الجمع بين النسكين).
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): the nature of the dam as 'shukr' ties it to the actual recipient of the blessing.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
Why does the blessing attach to the agent? Because the agent is the one who actually performed the combination. The phrase 'الْمَأْمُورُ هُوَ الْمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ النِّعْمَةِ' (the one ordered is the one specifically favored with this blessing) shows that the act and therefore the blessing belong to the agent.
The agent experienced the actual performance; the principal only ordered it.
4
Identify the broader implication (thamarah)
The passage concludes that this ruling supports a narration from Imam Muhammad that Hajj occurs on behalf of the agent in terms of physical actions. This affirms the principle that the physical acts of Hajj are attributed to the actual performer.
This is consistent with the rule that the agent bears the dam even though the reward may go to the principal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر غیر نے امر کیا کہ اس کی طرف سے قرآن کیا جائے تو دم اس پر ہے جس نے احرام باندھا
قَالَ فَإِنْ أَمَرَهُ غَيْرُهُ أَنْ يَقْرِنَ عَنْهُ فَالدَّمُ عَلَى مَنْ أَحْرَمَ لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ شُكْرًا لِمَا وَفَّقَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنَ الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ النُّسُكَيْنِ وَالْمَأْمُورُ هُوَ الْمُخْتَصُّ بِهَذِهِ النِّعْمَةِ لِأَنَّ الْحَقِيقَةَ الْفِعْلَ مِنْهُ وَهَذِهِ الْمَسْأَلَةُ تَشْهَدُ بِصِحَّةِ الْمَرْوِيِّ عَنْ مُحَمَّدٍ أَنَّ الْحَجَّ يَقَعُ عَنِ الْمَأْمُورِ
ترجمہ کہا کہ اگر عاجز نے دوسر کو حکم کیا کہ میری طرف سے قرآن ادا کر دے تو قربانی اس شخص پر واجب ہوگی جس نے احرام باندھا ہے۔ کیونکہ دم قرآن اس کا شکرانہ ہے کہ اللہ نے اس کو حج و عمرہ جمع کرنے کی توفیق دی ہے۔ اور اس نعمت کے ساتھ مامور یعنی وکیل مختص ہے کیونکہ حقیقی فعل اس کی طرف سے ہے۔ اور یہ مسئلہ شہادت دیتا ہے اس قول کے صحیح ہونے کی جو امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ حج غائب کی طرف سے واقع ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر ایک شخص نے دوسر کو حج قرآن کا حکم کیا تو دم قرآن وکیل پر واجب ہوگا نہ کہ آمر کے مال میں۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ دم قرآن اللہ کی اس نعمت کا شکرانہ ہے کہ خدا نے اس کو حج و عمرہ جمع کرنے کی توفیق عطا کی۔ اور اس نعمت کے ساتھ وکیل مختص ہے۔ کیونکہ حقیقی فعل قرآن اسی سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ البتہ دم قرآن وکیل ہی پر واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ مسئلہ اس بات کی شہادت دیتا ہے
He said: If someone else ordered him to perform Qiran on his behalf, then the blood (sacrifice) is upon the one who performed ihram, because it became obligatory as a thanks for what Allah has granted him of combining the two rituals, and the one ordered is the one who is specifically favored with this blessing, because the actual action is from him. And this issue testifies to the correctness of what is narrated from Muhammad that Hajj occurs on behalf of the one ordered.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This short passage addresses the scenario where a person (the principal) authorizes another (the agent) to perform Hajj al-Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) on his behalf. The question is: who must offer the dam (sacrificial animal) required for Qiran?

The ruling is clear: the dam is obligatory upon the agent (the one who actually performed the ihram), not upon the principal. The reasoning is that the dam for Qiran is an expression of thanks (shukr) for the blessing of combining the two rituals (Hajj and Umrah) in one state of ihram. This blessing is experienced by the person who actually performs the actions—the agent—since he is the one who entered ihram and combined the rites. The principal merely ordered the act; the actual performance and thus the blessing belongs to the agent.

The passage further notes that this ruling supports a narration from Imam Muhammad that Hajj (if performed by a proxy) is considered to be performed by the agent in terms of the physical actions, although the reward (thawab) may go to the principal. The dam is a physical obligation tied to the performer.

Thus, in Hanafi fiqh, when a person appoints another to perform Qiran, the agent must bear the cost of the dam from his own wealth, not from the principal's. This is different from Hajj Ifrad (Hajj only) or Tamattu' where the dam may be on the principal in some cases.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): A type of Hajj where one enters ihram with the intention of both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required as compensation or thanks for certain acts during Hajj, here for Qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person (principal) orders another to perform Hajj al-Qiran on his behalf, who is required to offer the dam?
A) The principal, because he is the one for whom Hajj is performed.
B) The agent, because he actually performed the actions and combined the two rites.
C) Both must contribute equally.
D) No dam is required because it is a proxy Hajj.

Key Takeaway
The dam for Qiran is a personal obligation on the one who actually performs the combination, not on the one who ordered it.

The Agent's Failure to Specify for Whom He Performs Hajj: Between Qiyas and Istihsan
Analyzing the validity of an agent's later specification after performing Hajj ambiguously

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an agent's later specification after performing Hajj in ambiguity, explain the distinction from an individual's case, and apply the concept of istihsan in agency contexts.

Core Idea
An agent's prior disobedience voids later specification; the act is his own.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on an agent (wakīl) who enters ihram without specifying which principal he represents. While an individual can later clarify an ambiguous niyyah, the agent's duty to obey his principal's explicit command changes the ruling. Through a detailed comparison and the use of istihsan, the Hanafi school distinguishes the two scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Observe the analogy proposed: an individual who enters ihram without specifying Hajj or Umrah can later specify before actions. The opponent argues the agent should similarly be able to specify.
2
Note the key difference
The agent was explicitly commanded by each principal to specify for him. His failure to specify is an act of disobedience (mukhālafah). The individual had no such command.
3
Understand the qiyas argument
The opponent draws an analogy (qiyas) between the individual's and agent's cases, claiming similarity in ambiguity. This is the starting point of the discussion.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response via istihsan
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy because of the agent's disobedience. Using istihsan, the school holds that the agent's actions are attributed to himself, not the principal. The distinction is further supported by examples from acknowledgment of debt and wudu for cooling.
5
Apply the ruling
Recall that if an agent performs Hajj without specifying for any principal, the Hajj counts as his own. He cannot later rectify it by specification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نے صرف احرام کا تلبیہ کہا یعنی احرام باندھا اور یہ نیت نہ کی کہ یہ حج کا احرام ہے یا عمرہ کا ہے۔ پھر افعال ادا کرنے سے پہلے اس نے متعین کر لیا تو یہ تعین جائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح اس شخص کو متعین کرنا بھی جائز ہونا چاہئے۔ جس کے لئے وکیل نے حج کیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں موکلوں کی تعیین پر مامور تھا یعنی دونوں موکلوں میں سے ہر ایک نے اسپر مامور کیا تھا کہ حج خاص طور پر میرے لئے کمرے لیکن اس نے مخالفت کی اور متعین نہیں کیا تو اب اس مخالفت کے بعد متعین کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف اس صورت کے جب احترام مہم باندھا اور حج یا عمرہ متعین نہیں کیا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ جس کو چاہے متعین کرے حج کو یا عمرہ کو۔ کیونکہ حج یا عمرہ کے ابہام کی صورت میں جو چیز اس نے اپنے اوپر لازم کی ہے وہ مجبول ہے۔ پس بیان سے اس کو رفع کرنا جائز ہے۔ جیسے زید نے بکر کے واسطے اپنے اوپر کچھ مجبول مال لازم ہونے کا اقرار کیا تو اقرار صحیح ہے اور مقدار مال کی جہالت بیان سے دور کر دے اور وکیل کے احترام کو مبہم کرنے کی صورت میں مجہول وہ شخص ہے جس کا حق ہے جیسے زید نے ہزار درہم اپنے اوپر ایک مجہول حقدار کے لازم کئے تو یہ اقرار صیح نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ جس کا حق ہے وہ مجہول ہے اس فرق کے رہتے ہوئے قیاس درست نہیں ہے۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ احرام خود مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ افعال ادا کرنے کا وسیلہ ہے اور مبہم تعیین کے واسطہ سے وسیلہ ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس شرط ہونے میں احرام مبہم کے ساتھ اکتفاء کرلیا گیا۔ کیونکہ شرط جس طرح بھی پائی جائے کافی ہوتی ہے۔ جیسے وضو نماز کی شرط ہے۔ لیکن اگر کسی نے ٹھنڈک حاصل کرنے کے لئے وضو کیا اور پھر اس سے نماز پڑھے تو جائز ہے۔ برخلاف اس صورت کے جب وکیل نے ایہام کی حالت پر افعال ادا کئے تو اب تعیین نہیں ہو سکتی۔ کیونکہ جو چیز ادا ہو چکی و تعیین کا احتمال نہیں رکھتی۔ ہاں جو ابھی ادا نہیں کی اس میں تعیین کرنا ممکن ہے۔ بہر حال وکیل نے مبہم حالت پر افعال ادا کئے تو اس نے مؤکل کی مخالفت کی اور مؤکل کی مخالفت کی صورت میں فعل وکیل کی طرف سے ادا ہوتا ہے۔
(Someone) merely said the talbiyah of ihram, i.e., entered ihram without intending whether it was for Hajj or Umrah. Then before performing the actions, he specified. This specification is valid. Similarly, it should be permissible for the person for whom the agent performed Hajj to specify. The answer is that here [the agent] was commanded to specify the principals, i.e., each of the two principals commanded him to perform Hajj specifically for him, but he disobeyed and did not specify. So after this disobedience, specification is not valid. Contrary to the case where one ties ihram ambiguously and does not specify Hajj or Umrah; he has the choice to specify whichever he wishes, because in the case of ambiguity, what he obligated upon himself is mujmal (unclear). So removing it by clarification is permissible. Like when Zayd acknowledges that he owes some unspecified property to Bakr, the acknowledgment is valid and the ignorance of amount is removed by explanation. But in the case of the agent's ambiguous ihram, the unknown entity is the person who has the right, like Zayd acknowledging one thousand dirhams owing to an unknown claimant; such acknowledgment is not valid because the right-holder is unknown. Given this difference, the analogy is not correct. The reason for istihsan is that ihram is not intended for itself but is a means to perform the actions, and a means can be achieved through ambiguous specification. Therefore, in being a condition, ambiguous ihram is deemed sufficient because a condition, however found, suffices. Like wudu is a condition for prayer; if someone makes wudu for cooling and then prays with it, it is valid. Contrary to the case when the agent performed actions in the state of ambiguity; then specification is not possible because what has been performed does not admit specification. However, in what has not yet been performed, specification is possible. In any case, the agent performed actions in the ambiguous state, so he disobeyed the principal, and in case of disobedience, the action is performed on behalf of the agent himself.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of an agent (wakeel) appointed by multiple principals to perform Hajj. The agent enters ihram without specifying for which principal, then later attempts to specify after performing some actions. The text first presents a qiyas (analogy) to a person who enters ihram without specifying Hajj or Umrah and later specifies before actions—this is valid. However, the agent's case differs because he was explicitly commanded to specify for each principal; his ambiguity constitutes disobedience. After disobedience, he cannot rectify the situation. The text distinguishes between the two cases using istihsan: ihram is a means, not an end, and ambiguity in a means can be tolerated, but the agent's disobedience changes the ruling. Therefore, the actions performed are attributed to the agent himself, not to the principals. The istihsan is supported by examples from acknowledgment of debt and wudu for cooling.

Key Terms
وکیل (wakīl): Agent appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another
تعیین (ta'yīn): Specification of the person (principal) for whom the act is performed
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference overriding qiyas due to a stronger consideration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When an agent (wakīl) is appointed by two principals to perform Hajj, and he enters ihram without specifying for which principal, then later tries to specify after performing actions, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The specification is valid because ihram is a means and can be ambiguous.
B) The specification is not valid because the agent disobeyed by not specifying initially, and the actions count for himself.
C) The specification is valid only if the principals agree to it later.
D) The specification is valid only if the agent performed all actions before specifying.

Key Takeaway
An agent's later specification is invalid if he performed actions in ambiguity; the Hajj counts for himself due to disobedience.

Dam al-Qiran Falls on the Agent When Commanded by Another
Determining who bears the Qiran sacrifice when someone commands another to perform Qiran on his behalf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the dam of Qiran when an agent performs it on behalf of a commander, and explain the proof based on the concept of shukr (thank-offering).

Core Idea
The Qiran sacrifice is a thank-offering for combining Hajj and Umrah; only the actual performer bears it.

When a person unable to perform Hajj commissions an agent to perform Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) on his behalf, a question arises: who must offer the required sacrificial animal (dam)? Is it the commander (the principal) who requested the act, or the agent who physically performs the rituals? The Hanafi school, as presented in al-Hidayah, rules decisively that the dam is on the agent. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
First, recognize the act: Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram). The ruling: the dam (sacrifice) is wajib on the one who actually enters ihram and performs the rituals—the agent.
The dam is a thank-offering (shukr), not a penalty.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is not a direct text but qiyas based on the nature of the dam. The text states: 'because it became wajib as a thank-offering for what Allah granted him of combining the two rituals.' Identify that the dalil type is qiyas, with the illa being the agent's exclusive experience of the blessing.
The Arabic: لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ شُكْرًا لِمَا وَفَقَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنَ الْجَمْعِ بَيْن النُّسُكَيْنِ
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The dam is a shukr (thanksgiving). Only the agent actually performed the combination and thus received the divine favor. Therefore, the obligation of thanks falls on him, not on the commander who only gave permission.
This reasoning is specific to Hanafi usul; it emphasizes the actual doer over the causer.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab dimension
Note that some other schools may place the dam on the commander because he initiated the obligation. The Hanafi position prioritizes the one who physically acts. This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The text also mentions that this ruling supports Imam Muhammad's view that Hajj falls on the commanded person (principal).
5
Apply to the given scenarios
The passage gives two cases: (1) a single commander; (2) two commanders, one for Hajj and one for Umrah, both permitting Qiran. In both, the ruling is identical: the dam is on the agent. Test your understanding: would the ruling change if the commander did not permit Qiran?
The principle remains consistent: the agent's performance triggers the shukr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر غیر نے امر کیا کہ اس کی طرف سے قرآن کیا جائے تو دم اس پر ہے جس نے احرام باندھا قَالَ فَإِنْ أَمَرَهُ غَيْرَهُ أَنْ يَقْرِنَ عَنْهُ فَالدَّمُ عَلَى مَنْ أَحْرَمَ لِأَنَّهُ وَجَبَ شُكْرًا لِمَا وَفَقَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مِنَ الْجَمْعِ بَيْن النُّسُكَيْنِ وَالْمَامُورُ هُوَ الْمَخْتَصُّ بِهذِهِ النِّعْمَةِ لِأَنَّ الْحَقِيقَةَ الْفِعْل مِنْهُ وَهَذِهِ الْمَسْتَلَةُ تَشْهَدُ بِصِحَةِ الْمَرْوِي عَنْ مُحَمّدٍ أَنَّ الْحَجَّ يَقَعُ عَنِ الْمَامُور ترجمہ کہا کہ اگر عاجز نے دوسر کو حکم کیا کہ میری طرف سے قران ادا کر دے تو قربانی اس شخص پر واجب ہوگی جس نے احرام باندھا ہے۔ کیونکہ دم قران اس کا شکرانہ ہے کہ اللہ نے اس کو حج و عمرہ جمع کرنے کی توفیق دی ہے۔ اور اس نعمت کے ساتھ ماموریعنی وکیل مختص ہے کیونکہ حقیقی نعل اس کی طرف سے ہے۔ اور یہ مسئلہ شہادت دیتا ہے اس قول کے صحیح ہونے کی جو امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ حج غائب کی طرف سے واقع ہوتا ہے۔ - تشریح مسئلہ، اگر ایک شخص نے دوسر کو حج قرآن کا حکم کیا تو دم قرآن وکیل پر واجب ہوگا نہ کہ آمر کے مال میں ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ دم قران اللہ کی اس نعمت کا شکرانہ ہے کہ خدا نے اس کو حج و عمرہ جمع کرنے کی توفیق عطا کی۔ اور اس نعمت کے ساتھ وکیل مختص ہے۔ کیونکہ حقیقی فعل قرآن اسی سے صادر ہوا ہے۔ البز ادم قرآن وکیل ہی پر واجب ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ مسئلہ اس بات کی شہادت دیتا ہے کہ حج مامور کی طرف سے واقع ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے۔ کسی عاجز نے حکم دیا کہ اس کی طرف سے حج ادا کیا جائے اور دوسرے نے کہا کہ اس کی طرف سے عمرہ کیا جائے دونوں نے قران کی اجازت دی تو دم قرآن وکیل پر ہوگا وَ كَذَلِكَ إِنْ أَمَرَهُ وَاحِدٌ بِنْ يَحُجَّ عَنْهُ وَ الْأَخَرُ بِأَن يَعْتَمِر عَنْهُ وَأَذِنَالَهُ بِالْقِرَانِ فَالدَّمُ عَلَيْهِ لِمَا قُلْنَا ترجمہ اور یوں ہی اگر کسی عاجز نے اس کو حکم کیا کہ میری طرف سے حج ادا کر دے۔ اور دوسرے عاجز نے اس کو حکم کیا کہ میری طرف سے عمرہ ادا کر دے اور دونوں موکلوں نے اس کو قرآن کر لینے کی اجازت دی تو دم قرآن وکیل پر ہوگا۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
If someone else commands him to perform Qiran on his behalf, then the dam is on the one who entered ihram. He (the author) said: 'If someone else commands him to perform Qiran on his behalf, then the blood sacrifice is on the one who entered ihram, because it became wajib as a thank-offering for what Allah Almighty granted him of combining the two rituals, and the commanded person (the agent) is the one specifically favored with this bounty because the actual act is from him. And this issue testifies to the correctness of what is narrated from Muhammad that the Hajj falls upon the commanded person.' Translation: He said: If an incapacitated person commands another to perform Qiran on his behalf, the sacrifice is obligatory on the person who entered ihram. Because the dam of Qiran is a thank-offering for the ability that Allah granted him to combine Hajj and Umrah. And this favor is specific to the agent, because the actual act is from him. This issue testifies to the correctness of the narration from Imam Muhammad that Hajj falls upon the commanded person. Explanation: If a person commands another to perform Qiran Hajj, the dam of Qiran is obligatory on the agent, not from the commander's wealth. The proof is that the dam of Qiran is a thank-offering for the bounty of being able to combine Hajj and Umrah, and this bounty is specific to the agent because the actual act of Qiran is performed by him. So the dam is on the agent. The author of al-Hidayah says that this issue testifies that Hajj falls upon the commanded person, as narrated from Imam Muhammad. Similarly, if someone commands him to perform Hajj on his behalf and another commands him to perform Umrah on his behalf, and both permit Qiran, then the dam of Qiran is on the agent. And likewise if one incapacitated person commands him to perform Hajj on his behalf and another commands him to perform Umrah on his behalf, and both principals permit him to do Qiran, then the dam of Qiran is on the agent, for the reason we have stated. Explanation is clear.

Commentary
This passage deals with the Qiran sacrifice (dam) when one person commands another to perform Hajj and Umrah combined (Qiran) on his behalf. The ruling is that the dam is wajib on the agent (the one who actually performs the ihram and the rituals), not on the commander (the principal). The proof is that the dam is a thank-offering for the blessing of being able to combine the two rituals, and this blessing is experienced by the agent, since he is the one who physically performs the acts. The passage also notes that this ruling supports a narration from Imam Muhammad that the Hajj is validly performed on behalf of the commanded person (i.e., the principal), meaning that the reward goes to the principal even though the sacrifice is on the agent. Two scenarios are given: a single commander, and two commanders (one for Hajj, one for Umrah) who both permit Qiran. In both, the dam is on the agent.

Key Terms
قران (qirān): Performing Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (animal) required as a penalty or thank-offering in Hajj
مامور (ma'mūr): The commanded person; here the agent who is commanded to perform Hajj/Umrah

Dam of Qiran Falls on the Agent When Two Principals Authorize Combined Hajj and Umrah
Ruling on dam liability for agent combining two mandates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who bears the dam of qiran when an agent is appointed by two principals for separate hajj and umrah with permission to combine, and explain the reasoning.

Core Idea
The agent bears the dam of qiran because he performs the combined rituals with permission.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj agency: when two different principals appoint the same agent—one for hajj and the other for umrah—and both permit the agent to combine them into a qiran. The key question is who is obligated to offer the sacrificial dam. The text provides a clear ruling from the Hanafi school, which we will unpack and understand.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal actors
Identify the two principals (one commanding hajj, the other umrah) and the single agent. Note that both principals explicitly permit qiran.
2
Confirm the ruling
State the ruling: the dam of qiran is wajib upon the agent (wakil), not on either principal.
The ruling is based on the principle that the agent's act of combining the two rituals makes him liable.
3
Understand the reasoning
The agent physically performs the combined rituals. The dam is a penalty for the act of qiran (combining hajj and umrah). Since the agent is the one who does the combining, he bears the responsibility for its associated obligation.
This aligns with the general Hanafi rule that obligations arising from the agent's actions fall on the agent unless stipulated otherwise.
4
Distinguish from other scenarios
Contrast this with a case where a single principal appoints an agent for qiran—then the dam is on the principal. Here, because two different principals gave separate commands, the agent's combination is effectively his own act, so he bears the dam.
The key difference is that the agent's mandate from each principal is partial; he chooses to combine them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج
کہ حج مامور کی طرف سے واقع ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ امام محمد سے مروی ہے۔
کسی عاجز نے حکم دیا کہ اس کی طرف سے حج ادا کیا جائے اور دوسرے نے کہا کہ اس کی طرف سے عمرہ کیا جائے دونوں نے قران کی اجازت دی تو دم قرآن وکیل پر ہوگا
وَ كَذَلِكَ إِنْ أَمَرَهُ وَاحِدٌ بِنْ يَحُجَّ عَنْهُ وَ الْأَخَرُ بِأَن يَعْتَمِر عَنْهُ وَأَذِنَالَهُ بِالْقِرَانِ فَالدَّمُ عَلَيْهِ لِمَا قُلْنَا ترجمہ اور یوں ہی اگر کسی عاجز نے اس کو حکم کیا کہ میری طرف سے حج ادا کر دے۔ اور دوسرے عاجز نے اس کو حکم کیا کہ میری طرف سے عمرہ ادا کر دے اور دونوں موکلوں نے اس کو قرآن کر لینے کی اجازت دی تو دم قرآن وکیل پر ہوگا۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
Book of Hajj: That the hajj occurs on behalf of the one who is commanded [i.e., the principal], as is narrated from Imam Muhammad. If one incapable person commanded him to perform hajj on his behalf, and another said to perform umrah on his behalf, and both gave permission for qiran, then the dam of qiran is upon the agent (wakil). And likewise, if one person commanded him to perform hajj on his behalf, and another to perform umrah on his behalf, and they permitted him to do qiran, then the dam is upon him for what we have said. Translation: And similarly, if one incapable person commanded him to perform hajj on his behalf, and another incapable person commanded him to perform umrah on his behalf, and both principals permitted him to do qiran, then the dam of qiran is upon the agent, for the reason we have stated. The explanation is clear.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the chapter on Hajj. The issue: two different principals appoint the same agent—one for hajj and the other for umrah—and both allow the agent to combine them as qiran. The question: who bears the required dam? The text rules that the dam is on the agent (wakil), not on either principal. The reason is that the agent performs the act of qiran with the permission of both principals, so the ritual is attributed to him. The dam is a penalty for the act of combining, and since the agent is the one doing it, he must pay it. The text references that this is based on what was previously stated, likely that the agent’s actions are on his own behalf in matters of penalties.

Key Terms
دم قرآن (dam al-qirān): The specified animal sacrifice required for performing combined hajj and umrah (qiran).
وکیل (wakīl): The agent appointed to perform hajj or umrah on behalf of another.
مأمور (ma'mūr): The person who is commanded to perform hajj/umrah; here synonymous with wakil (agent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Both principals equally

Key Takeaway
If two principals separately appoint the same agent for hajj and umrah and both permit qiran, the dam of qiran is wajib upon the agent, not the principals.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Who Bears the Dam of Ihsar? Principal vs Agent in Hajj Delegation
Intra-Hanafi dispute with rational proofs and extension to deceased principal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on liability for dam al-ihsar and apply the mufta bihi ruling to cases involving a living or deceased principal.

Core Idea
The dam of ihsar falls on the one who caused the entry into ihram, not the one who suffers the harm.

When a pilgrim is prevented (ahsara) from completing Hajj, a dam (sacrifice) becomes wajib to exit ihram. But who must pay it? Is it the agent who physically performs the hajj and experiences the harm, or the principal who delegated him? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold the principal liable; Imam Abu Yusuf argues for the agent. This lesson unpacks their proofs and extends the ruling to cases where the principal is deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
State clearly: (a) Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: dam on principal (aamir). (b) Abu Yusuf: dam on agent (haji). Note that both agree on the wajib nature of the dam itself.
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; all three imams are part of the same school.
2
Compare the Dalil (Rational Proofs)
For Abu Hanifa/Muhammad: The principal caused the agent to enter ihram; he must bear the cost of release. For Abu Yusuf: The dam benefits the agent by removing his hardship; he should pay.
Both proofs are aqli (rational). The text does not give a rebuttal from one side to the other.
3
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
According to the majority (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad), the agent is not out-of-pocket; the principal must provide the dam. According to Abu Yusuf, the agent bears the expense.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) follows the majority view (principal liable).
4
Apply to a Deceased Principal
When the principal is deceased and the agent he hired is prevented, the dam is taken from the deceased's estate according to the majority. Abu Yusuf still holds the agent liable.
The text then presents two opinions among later mashayikh on how the dam is paid from the estate.
5
Distinguish Payment from Estate: Silla vs Debt
Some said dam is a silla (gratuity) like unpaid zakat → from one-third of estate. Others said it is a debt owed to the agent → from entire estate. Both opinions are recorded.
This sub-ikhtilaf is among later scholars, not the three founding imams.

Source Text

And the dam of ihsar (prevention) is upon the commander (principal). This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said it is upon the haji (agent) because it became obligatory for tahlil (becoming halal) due to the harm of extended ihram. This harm returns to him, so the dam is upon him. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), that the commander is the one who put him into this responsibility, so upon him is the release. Translation: And the dam of ihsar is binding on the principal, and this is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said that the dam of ihsar is wajib on the haji (agent) because the dam of ihsar became wajib for tahlil so that the harm of long duration of ihram is removed, and this harm returns to the agent, so the dam is also wajib on him. And the proof of the two is that the principal is the one who put the agent into this responsibility, so the one who put him into it is also obligated to release him. Explanation of the issue: If the agent (mamur) is prevented and he becomes halal by sacrificing the dam of ihsar, then this sacrifice is wajib on the principal according to the two, and according to Abu Yusuf it is wajib on the agent. The proof of Abu Yusuf is that the dam of ihsar is wajib for tahlil to remove the harm of extended ihram, and this harm returns to the agent, so the dam is auf ihn. And the proof of the two is that the principal is the one who involved the agent in this responsibility, so whoever involved him is the one who must release him. If he was performing hajj for a deceased person and then was prevented, the dam is in the wealth of the deceased according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. Then it was said that it is from one-third of the wealth of the deceased because it is a silla (gratuitous payment) like zakat and others. And it was said that it is from all of the wealth because it became wajib as a right of the agent (mamur), so it becomes a debt. Translation: Then if he was performing hajj for a specific deceased and then was prevented, the dam of ihsar according to the two is wajib from the wealth of the deceased, contrary to Abu Yusuf. Some elders said that it will be from one-third of the deceased's wealth because it is a silla like zakat and others. And it was said that it will be from the entire estate because it became wajib as a right of the agent and thus became a debt. Explanation of the issue: If a person performs hajj on behalf of a deceased and then is prevented, according to the two the dam of ihsar is from the deceased's estate, and according to Abu Yusuf it is on the agent. Then some mashayikh said that the dam of ihsar is from one-third of the deceased's estate because it is a silla, like zakat and kaffarat are silla. Silla is that which is not in exchange for monetary consideration. Just as if zakat remained due on the deceased in his lifetime and he did not pay it, then zakat is given from one-third, similarly the dam of ihsar is a silla, so it is also given from one-third. And some mashayikh said that the dam of ihsar from the deceased is wajib from the entire estate because the dam of ihsar is a right of the agent against the principal, it becomes a debt on the deceased, and debt is paid from the entire estate.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the dam of ihsar (the sacrifice required when a pilgrim is prevented from completing Hajj). According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the dam is the responsibility of the principal (the person who appointed the agent), because the principal caused the agent to enter the state of ihram and thus must bear the cost of releasing him. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, reasoning that the dam is for the agent's benefit—to remove his own hardship of prolonged ihram—so the agent should pay it. Both sides give rational proofs. The text then extends the discussion to the case where the principal is deceased. The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) holds that the dam is paid from the deceased's estate. However, there is further disagreement among later scholars about whether the dam is deducted from one-third of the estate (treating it as a silla, like zakat that was not paid) or from the entire estate (treating it as a debt). The commentary explains both opinions and the reasoning behind them.

Key Terms
دم احصار (dam al-ihsār): The animal sacrifice required when a pilgrim is prevented (ahsara) from completing Hajj or Umrah, allowing them to exit ihram.
آمر (āmir): The principal who commands the agent to perform hajj; the one who delegates.
صلہ (ṣila): A gratuitous payment or charity not in exchange for something; e.g., zakat, kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The agent
B) The principal
C) Both equally
D) No one, it is waived

Key Takeaway
The dam of ihsar is wajib on the principal (or his estate) according to the majority of the Hanafi school, because causation of responsibility entails liability for release.

Dam of Sexual Intercourse and All Expiatory Dams Are on the Agent
Ruling on liability for expiatory dams for an agent performing Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding the liability for the dam of sexual intercourse during Hajj when performed by an agent, and identify the conditions that affect the agent's liability for expenses.

Core Idea
The agent bears the dam for his own offense; the principal is not liable for sins the agent commits voluntarily.

When a person performs Hajj on behalf of another (as an agent), any prohibited act committed during ihram may incur an expiatory dam. This lesson clarifies that the dam for sexual intercourse, as well as all other expiatory dams, are the responsibility of the agent, not the principal. Furthermore, if the intercourse occurs before standing at Arafat (wuquf), the Hajj becomes invalid and the agent must also compensate the principal for expenses; if after wuquf, the Hajj remains valid and no expense compensation is due, but the dam is still required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agent's liability for dam al-jima'
The text states that the dam for intercourse is upon the agent (al-hajj) because it is a dam for an offense, and the agent committed it voluntarily. Accept this as the baseline ruling: the agent pays from his own wealth.
The term 'al-hajj' here refers to the agent performing the Hajj, not the principal.
2
Distinguish the two temporal scenarios
The passage contrasts intercourse before wuquf and after wuquf. Before wuquf, the Hajj becomes invalid (fasid); after wuquf, it remains valid. Distinguish these two scenarios and note the different consequences for expense liability.
Wuquf at Arafat is the main pillar of Hajj.
3
Understand the consequence of invalidation on expenses
If the Hajj becomes invalid due to intercourse before wuquf, the agent must reimburse the principal for the expenses incurred (nafaqah) because the principal's purpose (a valid Hajj) was not achieved. If the Hajj is valid (after wuquf), no reimbursement is due.
The agent is liable for nafaqah only when the Hajj is invalidated by his own voluntary act.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind the rulings
The text uses rational argument: the agent acted by his own choice (bi ikhtiyar), so he bears the dam and, in the case of invalidation, the expense compensation. The principal is not liable because the sin is the agent's voluntary act.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on personal responsibility.
5
Extend the rule to all expiatory dams
The text explicitly states that all other expiatory dams (for hunting, shaving, etc.) are also upon the agent. The same principle applies: the agent committed the offense voluntarily, so he must pay.
This generalization covers all dam al-jinayat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ دَمُ الْجَمَاعِ عَلَى الْحَاحِ لِأَنَّهُ دَم حِنَايَةٍ وَهُوَ الْجَانِي عَنِ احْتِيَارِ وَيَضَمَن التَّفَقَة مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا جَامَعَ قَبْلَ الوقوف حَتَّى فَسَدَ حَجَّةَ لِأَنَّ الصَّحِيحَ هُوَ الْمَأمُورُ بِهِ بِخِلَافِ ما إذا فاتَهُ الْحَج حَيْثُ لَا يَصْمِنُ النَّفَقَةَ لِأَنَّهُ مَا فَاتَهُ بِاخْتِيَارِهِ أَمَّا إِذَا جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ لَا يَفْسُدُ حَجَّهُ وَلَا يَضمن النَّفَقَةَ لِحُصُولِ مَقْصُودِ الْأَمْرِ وَعَلَيْهِ الدَّمُ فِي مَالِمٍ لِمَا بَيْنَا وَكَذَلِكَ سَائِرَ دِ مَاءَ الْكَفَّارَاتِ عَلَى الْحَاحِ لِمَا قُلْنَا ترجمہ اور جماع کی قربانی اسی حاجی پر واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دم جنایت ہے۔ اور جرم کرنے والا بھی اپنے اختیار سے ہے۔ اور نائب نفقه ( خرچہ ) کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جب نائب نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے جماع کر لیا حتی کہ اس کا حج فاسد ہو گیا کیونکہ جس حج کا اس کو وکیل کیا گیا وہ حج صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے جس صورت میں اسکاج فوت ہو گیا چنا نچہ اس میں نفقہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے اختیار سے فوت نہیں ہوا ہے۔ بہر حال جب نائب نے وقوف عرفہ کے بعد جہان کیا تو اس کا حج فاسد نہ ہوگا۔ اور نہ وہ انفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ موکل کا مقصود حاصل ہو گیا ہے۔ اور وکیل پر اس کے مال میں سے مر جنایت واجب ہوگا۔ اس دلیل کی مہر تے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ اور یوں ہی تمام کفارات کے دم حاجی یعنی وکیل پر واجد میں اس میل کی محبت جو ہم بیان کر چکے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And the dam of intercourse is upon the hajj pilgrim (agent) because it is a dam of offense, and he is the one who committed the sin voluntarily. And he is liable for the expenses (nafaqa). Its meaning: when he had intercourse before standing (wuquf) such that his hajj became invalid, because the correct hajj is the one commanded. Contrary to the case where hajj is missed (fatahu al-hajj) in which he is not liable for expenses because it was not missed by his choice. As for when he had intercourse after wuquf, his hajj does not become invalid and he does not owe expenses because the purpose of the command has been achieved. And upon him is the dam from his own wealth for what we have explained. And similarly all other expiatory dams are upon the hajj pilgrim for what we have said. Translation: And the sacrifice for intercourse is wajib on the same hajj pilgrim (agent) because it is a dam for an offense, and the one who commits the crime is of his own free will. And the agent is liable for the expenses (nafaqa). Its meaning: when the agent had intercourse before wuquf such that his hajj became invalid, because the hajj for which he was appointed is a valid hajj. Contrary to the case where his hajj is missed (fata) in which he is not liable for expenses because it was not missed by his choice. In any case, when the agent had intercourse after wuquf, his hajj does not become invalid and he is not liable for expenses because the purpose of the principal has been achieved. And upon the agent is the dam from his own wealth for the offense, for the reason we have explained. And similarly all expiatory dams are wajib on the hajj pilgrim (agent) for the reason we have stated. The explanation is clear.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding the dam for sexual intercourse (dam al-jima') during Hajj. The text establishes that this dam, as well as all other expiatory dams (like dam for hunting, etc.), are the responsibility of the agent (the person physically performing the Hajj), not the principal. The reasoning: the agent commits the sin voluntarily; it is his own crime. Additionally, if the intercourse occurs before wuquf (standing at Arafat), the hajj becomes invalid (fasad), and the agent must also compensate the principal for the expenses incurred (nafaqa) because the principal did not get a valid hajj. However, if the intercourse occurs after wuquf, the hajj is not invalidated because the main pillar has been performed; thus no expense compensation is due, but the dam is still required. The text also states that all other expiatory dams follow the same rule: the agent pays from his own wealth.

Key Terms
دم جماع (dam al-jimā'): The prescribed sacrificial animal required as expiation for sexual intercourse during the state of ihram in Hajj.
دم جنایت (dam al-jināyah): A dam (sacrifice) required due to a transgression or offense committed during ihram.
نفقہ (nafaqah): Expenses incurred by the agent while performing Hajj; if hajj is invalidated, the agent is liable to repay the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The agent

Key Takeaway
The agent bears all expiatory dams arising from his own voluntary acts during Hajj, and if the Hajj is invalidated before wuquf, he must also compensate the principal for expenses.

Ruling on Dam al-Ihsar from the Deceased's Estate
Dispute on whether dam al-ihsar is from one-third or entire estate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the source of payment for dam al-ihsar and identify the reasoning (silah vs. dayn) behind each position.

Core Idea
Dam al-ihsar is wajib, but its source—one-third or entire estate—is disputed among Hanafi scholars.

When a deputy appointed by the deceased becomes muhsar (prevented from completing Hajj), the dam al-ihsar becomes wajib. But who bears the cost? The classical Hanafi texts record a significant intra-madhhab difference. In this lesson, you will explore the views of Abu Yusuf, the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and later mashayikh, and the reasoning that leads each to a different conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key question
What is the core dispute? Is dam al-ihsar on the deputy or the estate? If estate, from one-third or whole?
2
State the view of Abu Yusuf
He holds the obligation falls on the deputy himself, not the deceased's estate.
3
State the view of the two (Sahibayn)
They hold it is wajib from the deceased's estate, but later scholars differ on the portion.
4
Analyze the reasoning of the mashayikh
One group classifies it as silah (like zakat) → from one-third. The other classifies it as dayn (debt) → from entire estate.
The classification hinges on whether the payment is gratuitous or a financial obligation.
5
Understand the legal basis
The difference rests on the nature of the dam: is it a gratuitous payment (silah) akin to zakat, or a debt (dayn) owed to the deputy?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب ان
اشرف البدایہ میں اردو ہدایہ بند ہو
ترجمہ پس اگر مشخص میت کی طرف سے جی کرتا ہو پھر محصہ، ہو گیا تو ہم انحصار طرفین کے نزدیک میت کے مال میں واجب ہے۔ خلاف ہے ابو یوسف کا۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ وہ میت کے تہائی مال میں سے ہو گا۔ کیونکہ یہ صلہ ہے ز کو توفیہ کے مانند۔ اور کہا که احصار میت کے کل ترکہ سے واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ میل کا فتق بن کر واجب ہوا۔ اس لئے دین ہوگا۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص میت کی طرف سے حج کرتا ہے پھر وہ مصر ہو گیا تو طرفین کے نزدیک نام احصار نیت کے ترکہ میں سے واجب ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک وکیل پر واجب ہوگا ۔ پھر بعض مشائخ نے کہا کہ ام احصارمیت کے تہائی ترکہ میں سے واجب ہو گا ۔ کیونکہ یہ صلہ ہے۔ جیسے زکوۃ اور کفارات صلہ ہیں ۔ صلہ اس کو کہتے ہیں جو مالی عوض کے مقابلہ میں نہ ہو۔ ہاں جس طرح میت پر اگر زندگی میں زکو تم باقی رہ گئی ہو جو اس نے ادا نہیں کی تو زکوۃا تہائی مال میں سے دی جائے گی ۔ اسی نام احصار بھی چونکہ صلہ ہے اس لئے یہ بھی میت کے تہائی مال میں سے دیا جائے گا۔ اور بعض مشان نے فرمایا ہے کہ دم احصار میت سے کل ترکہ سے واجب ہوگا کیونکہ ہم احصار مامور یعنی وکیل کا آمر پر حق واجب ہے گویا یہ آمریعنی میت پر دین اور قرضہ ہے اور قرضہ کی ادائیگی میت کے کل ترکہ سے ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے دم احصار کی ادائیگی بھی میت کے کل ترکہ سے ہوگی ۔
Then if a specified person performs Hajj on behalf of the deceased and then becomes confined, then according to the two sides (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is wajib from the deceased's wealth. Abu Yusuf disagrees. Some scholars said that it will be from one-third of the deceased's wealth because it is a gift (silah) like zakat. And some said that the dam of confinement is wajib from the entire estate because it became obligatory as a right (haqq) and thus is a debt (dayn). Explanation: If someone performs Hajj on behalf of the deceased and then becomes confined, according to the two it is wajib from the deceased's estate. According to Abu Yusuf, it is wajib on the deputy. Then some mashayikh said that the dam of confinement is wajib from one-third of the estate because it is silah like zakat and kaffarat. Silah is that which is not in exchange for a financial compensation. Just as if the deceased had zakat due, it is paid from one-third, similarly dam al-ihsar. Some said it is wajib from the entire estate because the deputy's right is owed by the principal, so it is a debt, and debt is paid from the entire estate.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the source of payment for dam al-ihsar when the deceased's appointed deputy becomes muhsar (confined from completing Hajj). The key question: from which portion of the deceased's estate should the dam be paid? The passage records multiple positions. First, the 'two' (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is wajib from the deceased's wealth generally. Abu Yusuf alone differs, placing the obligation on the deputy himself. Then among later scholars (mashayikh), there are two views: (1) It is like a silah (gratuitous payment) – analogous to zakat and kaffarat – thus payable from one-third of the estate. (2) It is like a debt (dayn) because it is a right owed by the principal to the deputy, so payable from the entire estate. The text explains silah as a payment without financial exchange, contrasting it with debts. The first view likens it to zakat left unpaid by the deceased, which is taken from one-third. The second view argues that since the deputy performed the journey on the principal's command, the dam is a liability on the principal, thus a debt binding on the entire estate. The commentator does not explicitly prefer one view, presenting both as valid positions among the mashayikh.

Key Terms
دم احصار (dam al-ihsar): The blood sacrifice (dam) required when one is prevented (ihsar) from completing Hajj, here referring to the deputy's obligation that becomes due from the deceased's estate.
صلہ (silah): A gratuitous payment not in exchange for any financial return, like zakat and kaffarat.
دین (dayn): A debt or financial obligation owed by the deceased, payable from the entire estate before distribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do some mashayikh argue that dam al-ihsar is taken from one-third of the estate?
A) Because it is a debt (dayn) and debts are from one-third.
B) Because it is a silah (gratuitous payment) like zakat and kaffarat, which are from one-third.
C) Because the deputy chose to become muhsar.
D) Because the deceased made a will for it.

Key Takeaway
The classification of dam al-ihsar as silah or dayn determines whether it is paid from one-third or the entire estate.
