Dam al-Jama' for the Deputy: Personal Liability for Transgression
Ruling that blood of intercourse is on the pilgrim (deputy) with liability for expenses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who is liable for dam al-jama' when a deputy commits intercourse during Hajj and explain why the deputy must also repay expenses if the act occurs before wuquf.

Core Idea
A deputy’s transgression is his own liability — the dam and expenses fall on him, not the principal.

When a deputy performs Hajj, he acts on behalf of another. But what happens when he violates the sanctity of Ihram by sexual intercourse? Does the penalty fall on the deputy or the one who hired him? This passage from Al-Hidayah gives a clear ruling: the deputy bears the dam because he chose to transgress. Moreover, if the act invalidates the Hajj (i.e., before wuquf), he must also refund the expenses. Let's unpack the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the parties
The act is sexual intercourse (jima') during the state of ihram performed by a deputy (na'ib) on behalf of a principal (muwakkil).
The ruling applies specifically to the deputy, not to the principal.
2
State the ruling on the dam
The dam al-jama' (blood sacrifice for intercourse) is wajib upon the deputy personally, from his own property.
This is the core ruling: liability is personal.
3
Extract the proof (dalil)
The passage states: 'because it is a blood of transgression (jinayah), and the transgressor is by choice.' The deputy chose to commit the act, so he bears the penalty.
The illah (effective cause) is the transgression combined with free choice.
4
Distinguish the two scenarios
If intercourse occurs before wuquf (standing at Arafat), the Hajj is invalidated, and the deputy must also repay the principal's expenses (nafaqah). If after wuquf, the Hajj remains valid, and no expense repayment is required, but the dam is still due.
The timing affects expense liability, not the dam obligation.
5
Apply the principle to other expiation bloods
The passage concludes that all dam of expiation (kaffarat) are upon the deputy, not the principal, because the deputy's act is his own transgression.
This is a general rule for any violation during the deputy's Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جماع کا دم حاجی پر ہے
وَ دَمُ الْجَمَاعِ عَلَى الْحَاحِ لِأَنَّهُ دَم حِنَايَةٍ وَهُوَ الْجَانِي عَنِ احْتِيَارِ وَيَضَمَن التَّفَقَة مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا جَامَعَ قَبْلَ الوقوف حَتَّى فَسَدَ حَجَّةَ لِأَنَّ الصَّحِيحَ هُوَ الْمَأمُورُ بِهِ بِخِلَافِ ما إذا فاتَهُ الْحَج حَيْثُ لَا يَصْمِنُ النَّفَقَةَ لِأَنَّهُ مَا فَاتَهُ بِاخْتِيَارِهِ أَمَّا إِذَا جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ لَا يَفْسُدُ حَجَّهُ وَلَا يَضَمِنُ النَّفَقَةَ لِحُصُولِ مَقْصُودِ الْأَمْرِ وَعَلَيْهِ الدَّمُ فِي مَالِمٍ
لِمَا بَيْنَا وَكَذَلِكَ سَائِرَ دِ مَاءَ الْكَفَّارَاتِ عَلَى الْحَاحِ لِمَا قُلْنَا
ترجمہ اور جماع کی قربانی اسی حاجی پر واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دم جنایت ہے۔ اور جرم کرنے والا بھی اپنے اختیار سے ہے۔ اور نائب نفقه ( خرچہ ) کا ضامن ہوگا۔ اس کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جب نائب نے وقوف عرفہ سے پہلے جماع کر لیا حتی کہ اس کا حج فاسد ہو گیا کیونکہ جس حج کا اس کو وکیل کیا گیا وہ حج صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے جس صورت میں اسکاج فوت ہو گیا چنا نچہ اس میں نفقہ کا ضامن نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے اختیار سے فوت نہیں ہوا ہے۔ بہر حال جب نائب نے وقوف عرفہ کے بعد جہان کیا تو اس کا حج فاسد نہ ہوگا۔ اور نہ وہ انفقہ کا ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ موکل کا مقصود حاصل ہو گیا ہے۔ اور وکیل پر اس کے مال میں سے مر جنایت واجب ہوگا۔ اس دلیل کی مہر تے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ اور یوں ہی تمام کفارات کے دم حاجی یعنی وکیل پر واجد میں اس میل کی محبت جو ہم بیان کر چکے۔
The blood of intercourse is on the pilgrim (deputy) because it is a blood of transgression, and the transgressor is by choice. He guarantees the expenses. Meaning: When he has intercourse before standing at Arafat such that his Hajj becomes invalid, because the sound Hajj is what he was commanded to do. Contrary to when the Hajj is missed (not by his choice), he does not guarantee expenses because it was not missed by his choice. As for when he has intercourse after standing, his Hajj does not become invalid and he does not guarantee expenses because the objective of the command has been achieved. Upon him is the dam from his property as we stated. Similarly, all other bloods of expiation are on the pilgrim (deputy) for what we said.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the deputy (na'ib) who commits intercourse during Hajj. The ruling: the dam (blood sacrifice) for intercourse is wajib on the deputy himself, not on the principal. The proof: this is a dam due to transgression (jinayah), and the deputy chose to commit it. Additionally, the deputy must compensate the expenses (nafaqah) spent on the journey if the intercourse occurs before wuquf, because it invalidates his Hajj and thus the principal's command was not fulfilled. If he has intercourse after wuquf, the Hajj is valid (since the main pillar is wuquf), so no dam for invalidation, but he still owes the dam for intercourse itself? Actually, the text says 'upon him is the dam from his property' – this refers to the dam for intercourse (a penalty for the act). The rule distinguishes between before and after wuquf: before wuquf invalidates the Hajj and he must repay expenses; after wuquf, the Hajj is valid and he does not repay expenses, but he still owes the dam for the act of intercourse. The passage concludes that all bloods of expiation (dima' al-kaffarat) are on the pilgrim (deputy), meaning any such penalty falls on the deputy's own wealth, not the principal's.

Key Terms
دم الجماع (dam al-jama'): The blood sacrifice required for committing sexual intercourse during the state of ihram, which is a transgression (jinayah) on the part of the one who does it.
نائب (na'ib): A deputy appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another person (the principal).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a deputy (na'ib) has intercourse after wuquf (standing at Arafat), what is the ruling according to this passage?
A) His Hajj becomes invalid, and he must pay expenses.
B) His Hajj is valid, and he does not guarantee expenses, but he owes the dam from his own property.
C) His Hajj is valid, and no dam is required.
D) The principal must pay the dam from his estate.

Key Takeaway
The deputy is personally liable for any transgression during Hajj; the principal only bears expenses for the valid fulfillment of the command.

Deputy Dying En Route: Hajj Wasiyyah Execution Dispute
Dispute among imams on executing Hajj wasiyyah when deputy dies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi positions on executing a Hajj wasiyyah when the deputy dies en route, and evaluate the qiyas vs. istihsan reasoning for each.

Core Idea
When a Hajj deputy dies en route, the dispute: is the journey void (qiyas) or valid (istihsan) for executing the will?

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and his two disciples disagree on whether the journey of a deceased deputy affects the location and source of funds for executing a Hajj will. Abu Hanifa applies qiyas, treating the journey as void in worldly matters, while the Sahibayn apply istihsan, citing Quran and Hadith that honour the journey. Understanding this dispute illuminates the Hanafi method of balancing textual evidence and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Read the passage and note the three distinct views: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. List each position regarding starting location and source of funds.
Abu Hanifa: start from home, use one-third of remaining estate. Abu Yusuf: start from death place, use remaining of original one-third. Muhammad: start from death place, use remaining of the money given to the first deputy.
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's qiyas
Abu Hanifa analogizes the situation to the hadith 'deeds are cut off except from three' and argues that the journey is void in worldly rulings (like executing a will). Identify the asl (the hadith) and the illa (worldly effect).
The asl is the hadith; the illa is that the journey has no legal effect in worldly matters, so the will must be executed from the original home.
3
Trace the Sahibayn's istihsan
The Sahibayn prefer a different ruling based on Quran 4:100 and a hadith about dying on the path to Hajj. They argue the journey is not void; rather it is rewarded. Identify how these texts override qiyas.
The Quranic verse and hadith directly honour the journey, so istihsan overrides qiyas, making the journey valid for worldly rulings as well.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the journey is void (Abu Hanifa), the second deputy must start from the deceased's home, possibly increasing travel cost. If valid (Sahibayn), start from the place of death, reducing expense.
Also, the source of funds differs: Abu Hanifa uses the remaining one-third of the total estate; Sahibayn use the remaining of what was allocated (with sub-differences).
5
Relate to Hanafi usul
This dispute is a textbook example of qiyas vs. istihsan. In Hanafi usul, istihsan is a preferred method when there is a stronger textual basis (like a Quranic verse or specific hadith). Consider which method is more common in this scenario.
The passage does not explicitly give tarjih, but many later Hanafi scholars lean towards the Sahibayn's istihsan due to direct textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صی
وَ مَنْ أوْصَى بِأَنْ يُحجَ عَنْهُ فَأَحجُوْا عَنْهُ رَجُلا فَلَمَّا بَلَغَ الْكُوفَة ماتَ أوْ سُرِقَتْ نَفَقَتُهُ وَ قَدْ أَنْفَقَ البَصْفَ يُحِبُّ عَنِ الْمَيِّتِ مِنْ مَنْزِلِهِ بِثلث ما بَقِيَ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ قَالَا يُحَجُ عَنْهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ مَاتَ الْأَوَّلُ فَالْكَلَامُ هَهُمَا فِي اِعْتِبَارِ الثَّلْثِ وَفِي مَكَانِ الْحَجَ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَالْمَذْكُورُ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أمَّا عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يُحَجُّ عَنْهُ بِمَا بَقَى مِنَ الْمَالِ الْمَدْفوع إِلَيْهِ إِنْ بَقَى شَيْءٍ وَإِلَّا بَطَلَتِ الْوَصِيَّةُ اعْتِبَارً ا تَعْيِييُنِ الْمُؤْصِي إِذْ تَعْيِينُ الْوَصِيَ كَتَعُتُنِهِ وَعِند أبِى يُوسُفَ يُحجُ عَنهُ بمَا بَقى من الثلث الأول لأنَّهُ هُوَ الْمَحَلُّ لِنفاذ الوصيَّة ولا بي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ قِسْمَةَ الوَصِي و عَزَّلَه الْمَالَ لَا يَصِحُ إِلَّا بِالتَسْلِيم إلى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِى سَمَّاهُ الْمُؤْصِي لِأَنَّهُ لا حَضْمَ لَهُ لِيَقْبِضَ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا هَلَكَ قَبْلَ الأفْرَاز وَالْعَزل فيُحتُ بثُلُثِ مَا بَقى وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي فَوَجُهُ قَوْلِ أبي حنيفَةَ وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ أَنَّ الْقَدْر الموجُودَ مِنَ السَّفَر قَدْ بَطل فى حق أحكام الدُّنْيا قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ إِذا مات ابن آدم انقطع عَمَلُهُ إِلَّا مِنْ ثَلث الحَدِيث وتنفيذ الْوَصِيَّةِ مِنْ أحكام الدُّنْيا فبقيت الوصية من وطنه كان لَّمْ يُوْجِدِ الْخُرُوجُ وَجهُ قَوْلِهِما وَهُوَ الاسْتِحْسانُ أن سفرة لم يُبطل لقوله تعالى ، ومن يخرج مِنْ بَيْتِهِ مُهَاجِرًا إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ الآيَةَ وَ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ مَنْ مَاتَ فِى طَرِيقِ الْحَجّ كتب الله لهُ حَجَةٌ مُبْرُورَةً فِى كُلَّ سَنةٍ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَبْطُلُ سَفَرُهُ اعْتُبِرَتْ الْوَصِيَّةُ من ذلك المكان وأصْلُ الاختلاف فى الَّذى يَحْجُ بنفسه ويُنتنى عَلى ذلِكَ الْمَأْمُورِ بِالْحَجَ
And whoever makes a will that Hajj be performed on his behalf, and they send a man for Hajj on his behalf; when he reached Kufa, he died or his provisions were stolen, and he has spent half. He should perform Hajj on behalf of the deceased from his (the deceased's) home with one-third of what remains. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Hajj should be performed on his behalf from where the first (deputy) died. So the discussion here is concerning the consideration of the one-third and the place of Hajj. As for the first, the mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa. According to Muhammad, Hajj is performed with whatever remains of the money given to him if anything remains; otherwise the wasiyyah lapses, considering the testator's specification, for the specification of the executor is like his own specification. According to Abu Yusuf, Hajj is performed with what remains of the first one-third because it is the place for execution of the will. Abu Hanifa's proof: the division of the executor and his setting aside of the money is not valid except by handing over to the party named by the testator because there is no opponent to take possession, and it has not occurred, so it is as if the money perished before segregation and setting aside, so Hajj is performed with one-third of what remains. As for the second (the place), the proof of Abu Hanifa's statement, which is qiyas: the portion of journey that occurred has become void in respect of the rulings of this world. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When the son of Adam dies, his deeds are cut off except from three...' and executing the will is among the rulings of this world, so the will remains in effect from his home as if no departure occurred. The proof of the two's statement, which is istihsan: his journey is not void because of the verse 'Whoever leaves his home as an emigrant to Allah and His Messenger...' and the Prophet said: 'Whoever dies on the path of Hajj, Allah writes for him a Hajj accepted in every year.' And when his journey is not void, the will is considered from that place. The origin of the dispute is concerning one who performs Hajj himself and is applied to the one commanded to perform Hajj (the deputy).
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a scenario where a person makes a will (wasiyyah) that Hajj be performed on his behalf. The heirs send a deputy who reaches Kufa and then dies or has his provisions stolen, having already spent half of the allocated funds. The question: from where should the second deputy be sent, and from which portion of the estate should the expenses be taken? Abu Hanifa says: the second deputy should start from the deceased's home (ghar) and use one-third of the remaining wealth after the first deputy's death/loss. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: start from where the first deputy died (i.e., Kufa) and use the remaining funds. Within the Sahibayn, there is further difference: Muhammad says use whatever remains of the money given to the first deputy; if nothing remains, the wasiyyah lapses. Abu Yusuf says use what remains of the original one-third (the third set aside for wasiyyah). Abu Hanifa's argument (qiyas): the executor's act of setting aside the money is not valid unless it reaches the intended recipient; since it didn't, it's as if the money perished before segregation, so the wasiyyah is from the remaining one-third of the original estate. For the place, Abu Hanifa argues that the journey's portion that was completed is void in worldly rulings (like inheritance and wills), based on the hadith 'deeds are cut off except from three' and the principle that execution of a will is a worldly ruling; thus the will remains in effect from the original location (home). The Sahibayn's istihsan: the journey is not void, citing the Quranic verse about emigrants and the hadith about dying on the path to Hajj, so the will is executed from the place he died. The dispute's root: do we treat the journey as void (in terms of wasiyyah) or as valid?

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by a person for acts of worship or charity to be performed after death, here specifically for Hajj.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; here Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to treat the journey as void, likening it to the hadith of deeds being cut off.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; the Sahibayn use istihsan to uphold the validity of the journey based on Quran and Hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main point of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in this passage?
A) Whether the first deputy should be paid from one-third or the entire estate.
B) Whether the journey of the deceased deputy is considered void or valid for the execution of the will.
C) Whether the second deputy should be a different person.
D) Whether the heirs have authority to send another deputy.

Key Takeaway
The dispute over the deputy's journey illustrates how Hanafi imams apply qiyas and istihsan when executing a wasiyyah for Hajj.

Substitute Hajj: Funding and Location When the Deputy Dies
Intra-Hanafi dispute on execution of hajj bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on the funding source and starting location for substitute hajj when the appointed deputy dies mid-journey, and identify the proof (qiyas vs istihsan) behind each view.

Core Idea
When the deputy dies mid-journey, the bequest's execution splits — home or last point, original third or specific fund.

This lesson deals with a specific scenario: a person bequeaths that hajj be performed on his behalf; the executor appoints a deputy who sets out, but dies or loses the expenses partway. The Hanafi school has three views on where the substitute hajj should start and which fund should pay for it. Understanding this dispute requires careful attention to how each imam applies qiyas or istihsan, and how they view the spiritual value of the journey already undertaken.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Recognize that the case involves two variables: the location from which the substitute hajj should begin (the deceased's home vs the place where the deputy died) and the financial source (remaining estate, original third, or specific allocated money).
The passage explicitly states the discussion concerns two issues: 'consideration of the third and the place of hajj.'
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa rules that the substitute hajj is performed from the deceased's home using one-third of what remains of the estate. His proof is qiyas: the travel already undertaken is void for worldly rulings (execution of the bequest is a worldly act). He cites the hadith that actions cease at death except three. The journey is irrelevant; the bequest is executed as if no travel occurred.
The hadith 'When the son of Adam dies, his actions cease except from three' is referenced by Abu Hanifa.
3
Identify the Sahibayn positions and their proofs
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) both hold that the second journey starts from where the first deputy died. However, they differ on the fund: Abu Yusuf uses what remains of the original one-third bequest fund; Muhammad uses what remains of the specific money given to the first deputy. Both rely on istihsan: the journey is not void because of the spiritual reward (Quranic verse on migration and hadith on dying on the path of hajj).
Abu Yusuf considers the original third as the 'place for execution of the bequest,' while Muhammad emphasizes the testator's specification of the deputy.
4
Analyze the methodological conflict: qiyas vs. istihsan
Abu Hanifa applies strict qiyas: the journey is void for worldly rulings, so the bequest must start from home. The Sahibayn apply istihsan: the journey retains spiritual validity, so the starting point is where the deputy died. This is a classic example of qiyas being set aside for istihsan due to a stronger evidence (Quran and hadith about reward).
The passage labels Abu Hanifa's view as 'qiyas' and the Sahibayn's as 'istihsan.'
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa's view, the entire journey must be from home, which could be longer and more expensive. Under the Sahibayn, the journey starts from where the deputy died, potentially saving cost and effort. The fund also differs: Abu Hanifa recalculates one-third of the remaining estate; Abu Yusuf uses the original third; Muhammad uses the specific allocated money (if any remains).
The passage does not give a tarjih, but later Hanafi works often adopt Abu Hanifa's view as the mufta bihi.

Source Text

وَ مَنْ أوْصَى بِأَنْ يُحجَ عَنْهُ فَأَحجُوْا عَنْهُ رَجُلا فَلَمَّا بَلَغَ الْكُوفَة ماتَ أوْ سُرِقَتْ نَفَقَتُهُ وَ قَدْ أَنْفَقَ البَصْفَ يُحِبُّ عَنِ الْمَيِّتِ مِنْ مَنْزِلِهِ بِثلث ما بَقِيَ وَهَذَا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَ قَالَا يُحَجُ عَنْهُ مِنْ حَيْثُ مَاتَ الْأَوَّلُ فَالْكَلَامُ هَهُمَا فِي اِعْتِبَارِ الثَّلْثِ وَفِي مَكَانِ الْحَجَ أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَالْمَذْكُورُ قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أمَّا عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يُحَجُّ عَنْهُ بِمَا بَقَى مِنَ الْمَالِ الْمَدْفوع إِلَيْهِ إِنْ بَقَى شَيْءٍ وَإِلَّا بَطَلَتِ الْوَصِيَّةُ اعْتِبَارً ا تَعْيِييُنِ الْمُؤْصِي إِذْ تَعْيِينُ الْوَصِيَ كَتَعُتُنِهِ وَعِند أبِى يُوسُفَ يُحجُ عَنهُ بمَا بَقى من الثلث الأول لأنَّهُ هُوَ الْمَحَلُّ لِنفاذ الوصيَّة ولا بي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ قِسْمَةَ الوَصِي و عَزَّلَه الْمَالَ لَا يَصِحُ إِلَّا بِالتَسْلِيم إلى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِى سَمَّاهُ الْمُؤْصِي لِأَنَّهُ لا حَضْمَ لَهُ لِيَقْبِضَ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا هَلَكَ قَبْلَ الأفْرَاز وَالْعَزل فيُحتُ بثُلُثِ مَا بَقى وَأَمَّا الثَّانِي فَوَجُهُ قَوْلِ أبي حنيفَةَ وَهُوَ الْقِيَاسُ أَنَّ الْقَدْر الموجُودَ مِنَ السَّفَر قَدْ بَطل فى حق أحكام الدُّنْيا قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ إِذا مات ابن آدم انقطع عَمَلُهُ إِلَّا مِنْ ثَلث الحَدِيث وتنفيذ الْوَصِيَّةِ مِنْ أحكام الدُّنْيا فبقيت الوصية من وطنه كان لَّمْ يُوْجِدِ الْخُرُوجُ وَجهُ قَوْلِهِما وَهُوَ الاسْتِحْسانُ أن سفرة لم يُبطل لقوله تعالى ، ومن يخرج مِنْ بَيْتِهِ مُهَاجِرًا إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ الآيَةَ وَ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ مَنْ مَاتَ فِى طَرِيقِ الْحَجّ كتب الله لهُ حَجَةٌ مُبْرُورَةً فِى كُلَّ سَنةٍ وَإِذَا لَمْ يَبْطُلُ سَفَرُهُ اعْتُبِرَتْ الْوَصِيَّةُ من ذلك المكان وأصْلُ الاختلاف فى الَّذى يَحْجُ بنفسه ويُنتنى عَلى ذلِكَ الْمَأْمُورِ بِالْحَجَ
And whoever bequeaths that hajj be performed on his behalf, and they have a man perform hajj on his behalf, then when he reached Kufa he died or his expenses were stolen and he had spent half, it is performed on behalf of the deceased from his home with one-third of what remains. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they two said: hajj is performed on his behalf from where the first died. So the discussion here concerns the consideration of the third and the place of hajj. As for the first, the mentioned is the statement of Abu Hanifa. As for according to Muhammad, hajj is performed on his behalf with what remains of the money given to him, if anything remains, otherwise the bequest becomes void, by analogy to the testator's specification, for the executor's specification is like his own. And according to Abu Yusuf, hajj is performed on his behalf with what remains of the first third, because that is the place for execution of the bequest. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that the executor's division and setting aside of the money is not valid except by delivery to the direction which the testator named, because he has no opponent to take possession, and it was not found, so it becomes as if it perished before segregation and setting aside, so hajj is performed with one-third of what remains. As for the second, the face of Abu Hanifa's statement, and it is qiyas, is that the amount of travel that occurred has become void in respect to worldly rulings. He (peace be upon him) said: 'When the son of Adam dies, his actions cease except from three'—the hadith. And execution of the bequest is among worldly rulings, so the bequest remains from his home as if the departure had not occurred. The face of their statement, and it is istihsan, is that his travel is not void because of His statement (Exalted): 'And whoever goes out from his house as a migrant to Allah and His Messenger'—the verse. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever dies on the path of hajj, Allah writes for him an accepted hajj every year.' And when his travel is not void, the bequest is considered from that place. And the origin of the dispute is concerning the one who performs hajj himself and it is built upon that concerning the one commanded to perform hajj.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the case where a person bequeaths that hajj be performed on his behalf, the heirs appoint a deputy, and the deputy dies or loses his expenses mid-journey after spending half. The legal problem has two dimensions: (1) from which financial fund to finance the substitute hajj, and (2) from which location should the substitute hajj commence. The passage presents three positions: Imam Abu Hanifa's, Imam Abu Yusuf's, and Imam Muhammad's, with their respective proofs. Abu Hanifa holds that the bequest should be executed from the testator's home using one-third of the remaining estate, applying strict qiyas that the journey already undertaken is void for worldly purposes. Abu Yusuf considers the original one-third (the maximum bequest fund) and uses whatever remains of it. Muhammad considers the specific money allocated to the first deputy; if any remains, it is used; otherwise the bequest is void. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree that the second journey should start from where the first deputy died, based on istihsan: the journey is not void because of the spiritual reward and the Quranic verse on migration. Abu Hanifa differs, arguing that for worldly rulings (like executing a bequest), the journey is irrelevant; the bequest is executed from the home as if no travel occurred. The passage also clarifies that this dispute is analogous to the case where a person himself sets out for hajj and dies on the way.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest or will; specifically in this context, a bequest that hajj be performed on behalf of the deceased.
النائب (al-na'ib): The deputy appointed to perform hajj on behalf of the testator.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum limit for bequests according to Hanafi law.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; used by Abu Hanifa to argue that the travel is void for worldly rulings.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; used by Sahibayn to consider the travel valid due to religious merit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) From the deceased's home in his country
C) From the nearest point on the route
D) From Kufa, where the deputy reached

Key Takeaway
When the deputy for substitute hajj dies mid-journey, Abu Hanifa starts from home and recalculates the one-third; the Sahibayn start from where the deputy died but differ on the fund.

Dispute on Hajj by Proxy When Deputy Dies or Money Lost
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fulfilling a will for Hajj after deputy's failure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on financing a second Hajj journey when the deputy dies or loses funds, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between them.

Core Idea
When a Hajj deputy fails, the estate's one-third is reused differently: Abu Hanifa renews it each time, the Sahibayn only once.

A person makes a will that Hajj be performed on his behalf from his estate. The heirs appoint a deputy and give him travel expenses, but he dies on the way or the money is stolen. How should the will be fulfilled? Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani disagree on two key points: from which portion of the estate to finance a second attempt, and where the second journey should start. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and the practical consequences of each view.

Guided Path
1
Outline the scenario
Describe the situation that triggers the dispute: a testator wills Hajj to be performed on his behalf; the deputy dies or loses the funds on the way.
The deputy may have already spent part of the money.
2
Identify the two contested issues
The dispute revolves around (1) from which portion of the estate the second journey should be financed, and (2) from where the second journey should start (hometown vs. place of death).
3
Map each imam's ruling on issue 1
State the positions: Abu Hanifa takes one-third of the remaining estate repeatedly; Abu Yusuf uses only what remains of the original one-third; Muhammad al-Shaybani uses only what remains of the money given to the first deputy.
Use the example from the text: estate 4000, first allocation 1000.
4
Analyze the proofs
Examine the dalil for each position. Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith that deeds cease at death except three, making the first journey void. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad use qiyas and istihsan based on the Quran and hadith about reward.
The hadith is about cessation of deeds; the Quran verse (4:100) promises reward for the journey.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Abu Hanifa, the will may be fulfilled repeatedly from the diminishing estate; under the Sahibayn, the will fails if the remaining portion is insufficient.
Also affects the starting point: from home or from where the deputy died.

کتاب الحج

۵۲۴

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم

ہے یہ ہے کہ اس کا سفر باطل نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے جو شخص اپنے گھر سے اللہ اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف ہجرت کرتا ہوا۔ نکلے۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو کوئی حج کے راستہ میں مر گیا اس کے لئے ہر سال حج مقبول لکھا جاتا ہے۔ اور جب اس کا سفر باطل نہ ہوا تو وصیت اس جگہ سے معتبر ہوگی ۔ اور اصل اختلاف اس شخص کے بارے میں ہے جو خود حج کرتا ہے اور اس پر مامور بالمج بنی ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے وصیت کی کہ میری طرف سے کسی کو حج کرا دیا جائے۔ ورثہ نے اس کی طرف سے ایک آدمی کو سفر خرچ دے کر حج کے لئے بھیجا لیکن وہ نائب راستہ میں مرگیا یا اس کا خرچ چوری ہو گیا حالانکہ وہ آدھار و پیہ خرچ کر چکا ہے۔ پس موت کی صورت میں آدھا باقی ہے اور چوری کی صورت میں وہ بھی گیا۔ تو اب یہاں دو باتوں میں اختلاف ہے۔ ایک تو آئیں کہ دوسرے نائب کو یا اس نائب کو دوسرا سفر حج کس مال سے کرایا جائے۔ دوم اس میں کہ دوسرا سفر کہاں سے کرایا جائے ۔ پہلی بات میں امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ میت کے مال متروکہ میں جو باقی ہے اس کا تہائی لیا جائے۔ یہ بھی اگر چوری ہو گیا تو پھر مابقی کا تہائی لیا جائے ۔ مثلا حج کی دمیت کر کے مرنے والے کے پاس چار ہزار روپیہ میں سے ایک ہزار رو پسی نائب کو دے کر حج کو بھیج دیا۔ راستہ میں اس کا سارا روپیہ پیسہ چوری ہو گیا یا یہ مر گیا اور کچھ روپیہ خرچ ہو گیا اور کچھ اسکے پاس باقی رہا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ دوبارہ سفر کے لئے مابقی ترکہ کا ایک تہائی لیا جائے گا۔ اور وہ ایک ہزار روپیہ ہے کیونکہ کل رقم چار ہزار روپیتھی۔ اس میں سے ایک ہزار روپیہ تو پہلے دیا جا چکا جو راستہ میں چوری ہو گیا۔ اب ترکہ کا مال تین ہزار روپیہ باقی رہا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان تین ہزار روپیہ کا ایک تہائی یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ دوسرے سفر حج کے لئے دیا جائے اور وہ بھی اگر چوری ہو گیا تو باقی مال مترو کہ یعنی دو ہزار کا ایک تہائی لے کر حج کرایا جائے اگر ممکن ہو ۔ علی ہذا القیاس۔ اور امام ابو یوسف نے فرمایا ہے کہ پورے ترکہ کا جو تہائی ہے چوری کے بعد اس میں سے جو باقی رہ گیا دوسرا سفر حج اس سے کرایا جائے اگر ممکن ہو۔ مثلا کل ترکہ چار ہزار روپیہ تھے اس کا تہائی ایک ہزار تین سو تینتیس روپیہ اور تہائی روپیہ ہے۔ حج کا خرچ ایک ہزار روپیہ تھا جو وصی نے ایک شخص کو دیا لیکن راستہ میں اس سے یہ روپیہ چوری ہو گیا۔ اب کل ترکہ کے ایک تہائی میں سے تین سو تینتیس روپیہ اور ایک روپیہ کا ایک تہائی باقی ہے اگر ممکن ہو تو دوسرا سفر حج اسی مقدار باقی سے کرایا جائے گا اور اگر تین سو تینتیس روپیہ اور ایک روپیہ کے ایک تہائی میں حج کرنا ممکن نہ ہو تو مرنے والے کی وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ جو مال نائب کو اولا دیا گیا تھا یعنی ایک ہزار روپیہ اس ایک ہزار روپیہ میں اگر کچھ باقی رہ گیا ہو مثلاً پانچ سوروپیہ خرچ کر کے نائب مر گیا تو باقی پانچ سوروپیہ سے دوسرا سفر حج کرایا جائے اور اگر کچھ نہیں بچا بلکہ پورا مال چوری ہو گیایا جو بچا ہے اس سے حج کرناممکن نہیں ہے تو ایسی صورت میں اس کی وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ دوسری بات میں امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ دوسرا سفر حج بھی میت کے وطن سے کرایا جائے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ نائب اول جس جگہ مرا ہے وہاں سے دوسرا سفر کرایا جائے۔ پہلے مسئلہ میں امام محمد کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ وہ وصی کی تعیین کو موصی کی تعیین پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ یعنی اگر موصی (میت) خود مال کی مقدار متعین کر دیتا مثلا یوں کہتا کہ میرے مال میں سے ایک ہزار روپیہ سے میری طرف سے حج کرا دیا جائے۔ پھر وہ نائب راستہ میں مرجاتا یا اس کا سارا مال چوری ہو جاتا تو سارا مال چوری ہونے کی صورت میں وصیت باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر ایک ہزار روپیہ میں سے کچھ باقی رہتا تو اس باقی ہی مال سے دوسرا سفر حج کرایا جاتا اگر ممکن نہ ہوتا تو اس صورت میں بھی وصیت باطل ہو جاتی ۔ پس اسی طرح وصیت کے متعین کرنے کا حکم ہے یعنی وہی نے مال کی جو مقدار حج کے لئے نائب کو دینے کا فیصلہ کیا تھا نا ئب نے سفر کیا پھر وہ مال ہلاک ہو گیا اور سارا ختم ہو گیا یا کچھ باقی رہ گیا پہلی صورت میں بالیقین وصیت باطل ہوگی اور دوسری صورت میں باقی ماندہ رقم سے اگر دوسرا سفر حج کرانا ممکن ہو تو کرا دیا جائے۔ اور اگر ممکن نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں بھی وصیت، باطل ہو جائے گی۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس مال میں وصیت جاری ہوتی ہے وہ کل مال کا ایک تہائی ہے۔ پس اس میں سے خرچ کرنے یا چوری ہونے کے بعد اگر کچھ مال باقی ہے اور اس سے دوسرا سفر حج کرانا ممکن بھی ہے تو اس باقی سے کرا دیا جائے کیونکہ وصیت نافذ ہونے کا محل یہی کل مال کا تہائی ہے۔ لہذا پہلی مرتبہ اور دوسری مرتبہ اس میں سے سفر حج کرایا جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وصی کا مال متروکہ تقسیم کرنا اور اس کو الگ کرنا اسی وقت صحیح ہوگا جبکہ وھی اس مقصد میں صرف کرے جس کو موصی نے متعین کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ موصی کی طرف سے کوئی قبضہ کرنے والا نہیں ہے تو مقبوض اسی طور پر ہوگا کہ وھی اس کو جہت وصیت میں سپر د کر دے۔ اور یہاں جہت وصیت میں سپر د کرنا نہیں پایا گیا۔ کیونکہ جہت وصیت حج ہے اور حج ابھی ہوا نہیں پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گو یا مال وصیت تقسیم اور جدا کرنے سے پہلے تلف ہو گیا۔ پس اب جو کچھ باقی ہے یہی کل مال رہا پس اس کی تہائی سے دوسرا سفر حج کرانا چاہئے۔ اسی طرح جب موصی کی جہت وصیت کو سپرد کرنے سے پہلے تلف ہو گیا تو مابقی مال یعنی تین ہزار کی تہائی سے دوسرا سفر حج کرا دے حتی کہ اگر یہ بھی پورا ہونے سے پہلے تلف ہو گیا تو یہ معدوم شمار ہو کر مابقی یعنی دو ہزار روپیہ کی تہائی سے حج کرانا لازم ہوگا۔ دوسرے مسئلہ میں امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل اور وہی قیاس ہے یہ ہے کہ نائب کا جو سفر موجود ہے یعنی وطن سے لے کر اس کے مرنے کی جگہ تک وہ احکام دنیا کے حق میں معدوم ہو گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ آدمی جب مر جاتا ہے تو اس کا عمل منقطع ہو جاتا ہے سوائے تین اعمال کے۔ (1) صدقہ جاریہ (۲) علم نافع (3) ولد صالح اور یہ سفر ان تین اعمال میں سے نہیں ہے درانحالیکہ وصیت نافذ کرنا احکام دنیا سے ہے تو گویا اس کا یہ سفر یعنی وطن سے موت کی جگہ تک حدیث کی روشنی میں کالعدم ہو گیا ہے اور جب کالعدم ہو گیا تو گویا اس نے سفر شروع ہی نہیں کیا اور جب سفر شروع نہیں کیا تو وصیت کو پورا کرنے کے لئے میت کے وطن سے از سر نو حج کرانا واجب رہا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ اس کا سفر معدوم نہیں ہوا کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وَمَنْ يَخْرُجُ مِنْ بَيْتِهِ مُهَاجِرًا إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ يُدْرِكُهُ الْمَوْتُ فَقَدْ وَقَعَ أَجْرُهُ عَلَى اللهِ ( النساء ١٠٠) یعنی جو شخص اپنے گھر سے اللہ اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف ہجرت کر کے نکلا پھر اس کو راستہ میں موت نے آلیا تو اس کا ثواب اللہ پر ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ راستہ میں موت سے ثواب کامل ملتا ہے اور یہی سفر کا مقصود ہے اور سفر ہجرت میں سفرحج اور سفر جہاد بھی ہے بلکہ صریح نص ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص حج کے راستہ میں مرا تو اسکے لئے ہر سال ایک حج مقبول کا ثواب لکھا جاتا ہے۔ بہر حال جب اس سفر کا ثواب مل گیا تو اس کا یہ سفر باطل نہیں ہوا۔ اور جب سفر باطل نہیں ہوا تو وصیت کا اعتبار اسی جگہ سے ہوگا جہاں اس کی موت آئی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان اصل اختلاف اس شخص کے حق میں ہے جو خود حج کرنے کو نکالا تھا۔ راستہ میں مرگیا اور وصیت کر گیا کہ میری طرف سے حج کرا دیا جائے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک جہاں مرا ہے اسی مقام سے وصیت معتبر ہو گی ۔ اسی پر مامور بانج مبنی ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مامور جہاں مرا یہ سفر کا لعدم شمار ہوگا اور دوبارہ گھر سے نفاذ وصیت ہوگا اور صاحبین کے
Book of Hajj. 524. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Commentary on Hidayah, Volume Three. It is that his journey is not void. Because Allah Almighty said: Whoever leaves his home migrating to Allah and His Messenger, and then death overtakes him... And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever dies on the path of Hajj, for him a Hajj accepted is written every year. And when his journey is not void, then the will is valid from that place. And the original dispute is concerning the person who himself performs Hajj and upon him the appointed person (ma'mur) becomes obligated. Explanation of the scenario: A person made a will that Hajj be performed on his behalf by someone. The heirs gave travel expenses to a person and sent him for Hajj, but that deputy died on the way, or his expenses were stolen, even though he had already partially spent. So in case of death, half remains, and in case of theft, that too is gone. Now there is a dispute in two matters. First, from which wealth should a second deputy or the same deputy be sent for Hajj? Second, from where should the second journey be made? Regarding the first matter, Imam Abu Hanifa said: One-third of whatever remains of the deceased's estate should be taken. If that too is stolen, then one-third of the remainder should be taken. For example, the deceased had four thousand rupees, he gave one thousand rupees to the deputy and sent him for Hajj. On the way, all his money was stolen, or he died and some money was spent and some remained. Then Imam Abu Hanifa said: For a second journey, one-third of the remaining estate will be taken, and that is one thousand rupees because the total was four thousand, of which one thousand had already been given and lost. Now three thousand remains, so Imam Abu Hanifa says: one-third of these three thousand, i.e., one thousand rupees, should be given for the second Hajj journey, and if that too is stolen, then one-third of the remaining two thousand should be taken for Hajj if possible. And so on by analogy. Imam Abu Yusuf said: One-third of the entire estate, after theft, whatever remains of that, the second Hajj journey should be made from it if possible. For example, total estate was four thousand, its one-third is one thousand three hundred thirty-three and one-third rupees. The Hajj expense was one thousand, which the executor gave to a person, but on the way the money was stolen. Now from the one-third of the total estate, three hundred thirty-three and one-third rupees remain. If possible, the second Hajj journey will be made from that remaining amount, and if it is not possible to perform Hajj with three hundred thirty-three and one-third rupees, then the will of the deceased becomes void. Imam Muhammad said: From the money that was initially given to the deputy, i.e., one thousand rupees, if something remains from that one thousand, for example, the deputy spent five hundred and then died, then the second Hajj journey will be made with the remaining five hundred. And if nothing remains, or the whole money was stolen, or what remains is insufficient for Hajj, then in that case his will becomes void. Regarding the second matter, Imam Abu Hanifa said: The second Hajj journey should also be made from the deceased's hometown. And the Sahibayn said: The second journey should be made from the place where the first deputy died. In the first issue, Imam Muhammad's proof is qiyas. He makes an analogy between the executor's specification and the testator's specification. That is, if the testator (the deceased) himself specified the amount, e.g., he said: 'Have Hajj performed on my behalf with one thousand rupees from my property', then the deputy died on the way or all his money was stolen, then in case of total loss the will becomes void, and if something remains from the one thousand, the second Hajj journey would be made from that remainder if possible, otherwise the will also becomes void. Similarly, the ruling of the executor's specification is that he had decided the amount to give to the deputy for Hajj, the deputy traveled, then the money was destroyed and all gone or something remained; in the first case, certainly the will is void, and in the second case, if a second Hajj journey is possible with the remaining amount, then it should be done; if not possible, then also the will becomes void. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that the property in which the will operates is one-third of the total estate. So after spending or theft, if some property remains from that one-third, and it is possible to make a second Hajj journey with it, then it should be made from that remainder, because the locus of the will's execution is this one-third of the total property. Therefore, the first and second Hajj journeys will be made from it. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the executor's division of the estate and setting it aside is only correct when he spends it for the purpose specified by the testator. Because there is no one to take possession from the testator, so the taken property will be considered as having been delivered for the will's purpose. Here, the delivery for the will's purpose has not occurred, because the purpose of the will is Hajj, and Hajj has not yet happened. So it is as if the property was destroyed before division and separation. So now whatever remains is the entire property; thus, the second Hajj journey should be made from its one-third. Similarly, when the property was destroyed before being assigned to the testator's will purpose, then the second Hajj journey should be made from one-third of the remaining property, i.e., three thousand, such that if this too is destroyed before completion, it is considered nonexistent, and it becomes necessary to perform Hajj from one-third of the remaining two thousand. In the second issue, Imam Abu Hanifa's proof, which is also qiyas, is that the deputy's journey, i.e., from his hometown to the place of his death, is considered nonexistent from the perspective of worldly rulings. Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When a person dies, his deeds are cut off except three: ongoing charity, beneficial knowledge, and a righteous child. And this journey is not among these three deeds, whereas executing the will is from worldly rulings. So, his journey, i.e., from hometown to death place, is rendered void in light of the hadith, and when it is void, it is as if he never started the journey. And when the journey was not started, to fulfill the will, it remains obligatory to perform Hajj anew from the deceased's hometown. The Sahibayn's proof and the reason for istihsan is that his journey is not void, because Allah Almighty said: 'And whoever leaves his home migrating to Allah and His Messenger, and then death overtakes him, his reward has indeed become due from Allah' (An-Nisa 4:100). That is, whoever leaves his home migrating to Allah and His Messenger, then death overtakes him on the way, his reward is on Allah. From this it is understood that death on the way gives complete reward, and this is the purpose of the journey. The journey of migration includes the journey of Hajj and the journey of jihad. Rather, there is a clear text that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever dies on the path of Hajj, for him each year a Hajj accepted is written. In any case, when the reward of this journey has been obtained, his journey is not void. And when the journey is not void, the will will be considered from the place where his death occurred. The author of Hidayah says: The original dispute between Imam Sahib and the Sahibayn concerns the person who himself set out to perform Hajj, died on the way, and made a will that Hajj be performed on his behalf. According to the Sahibayn, the will is valid from the place where he died. And upon this the appointed person (ma'mur) is based; according to Imam Sahib, the journey of the appointed person where he died is considered void, and the will will be executed again from the home, and according to the Sahibayn...
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) concerning the fulfillment of a will (wasiyyah) to perform Hajj on behalf of a deceased person when the appointed deputy (na'ib) dies or loses the money before completing the Hajj. The text presents two main issues: (1) from which portion of the estate should the second Hajj journey be financed, and (2) from where (the deceased's hometown or the place of the deputy's death) should the second journey commence. The passage first states the scenario: a person makes a will that Hajj be performed on his behalf. The heirs give travel expenses to a deputy and send him, but he dies on the way or the money is stolen. If he dies, part of the money remains; if stolen, nothing remains. The disagreement among the three Hanafi masters (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is detailed. For the first issue, Imam Abu Hanifa holds that each time, one-third of the remaining estate (after previous losses) should be taken for a new attempt. Abu Yusuf holds that the will operates on the original one-third of the total estate, so only what remains of that one-third (after the first loss) can be used for a second attempt; if insufficient, the will becomes void. Imam Muhammad analogizes to the case where the testator himself specifies a fixed amount: the second journey can only be made from what remains of that specified amount. The second issue concerns the starting point: Imam Abu Hanifa considers the first journey void due to the hadith that deeds cease at death (except three), so the second journey must start from the deceased's hometown. The Sahibayn consider the journey not void because the Quran and hadith indicate that reward is obtained for the journey, so it is valid; thus the second journey should start from where the deputy died. The commentary by the author of Hidayah clarifies that the original dispute is about a person who himself goes for Hajj and makes a will, and then it is applied analogically to the deputy (ma'mur).

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will or testament in which a person directs that Hajj be performed on his behalf from his estate.
تہائی (thuluth): One-third of the deceased's estate, which is the maximum amount that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without permission of heirs.
نائب (na'ib): A deputy or agent appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of the testator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if the first deputy for Hajj dies on the way having spent half of the money, from what amount should the second deputy be financed?
A) From the original one-third of the total estate
B) From one-third of the remaining estate after the first loss
C) From whatever remains of the money given to the first deputy
D) From the entire estate without restriction

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on Hajj proxy failure reveals that the school prioritizes fulfilling the will even after obstacles, but differs on how the estate's one-third is reused.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Executing Hajj Wasiyyah After Death on Journey
Intra-Hanafi dispute with proofs on wasiyyah validity after death on journey

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the validity of a journey when the traveler dies en route, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine where the Hajj should be performed.

Core Idea
The journey of a deceased person is void in worldly rulings for Abu Hanifa, but valid for the Sahibayn — affecting where his Hajj wasiyyah is executed.

This lesson addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: a person sets out for Hajj, dies on the way, and had made a wasiyyah (will) for Hajj to be performed on his behalf. The core question is whether the journey is considered valid or void in worldly rulings, and consequently whether the proxy should start Hajj from the deceased's home or from the place of death. The disagreement rests on different interpretations of a hadith about the severance of deeds at death and the reward for dying on a sacred journey.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
The scenario involves a person who intended to perform Hajj, died en route, and left a wasiyyah for Hajj to be performed on his behalf. The question: where should the proxy commence the Hajj — from the original home or from the place of death?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa holds that the journey is void in worldly rulings. His proof is the hadith: 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off except three...' The journey is not among those three, so it is as if it never began. Therefore the Hajj must start from the original home.
He also uses qiyas: the wasiyyah wealth was not delivered to its purpose, so it is considered wasted.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that the journey is valid. Their proof is Quran 4:100 (reward for one who dies while migrating) and a hadith that dying on the path of Hajj brings great reward. Since reward is granted, the journey is not void.
They rely on istihsan (juristic preference) over the qiyas of Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, the proxy must travel from the deceased's home to perform Hajj. According to Sahibayn, the proxy may start Hajj from the place of death, potentially saving time and expense.
This difference applies both when the deceased himself made the wasiyyah and when the proxy (na'ib) dies en route.
5
Apply to the proxy (na'ib) case
The same dispute extends to a proxy who dies while performing Hajj on behalf of another. Abu Hanifa: the proxy's journey is void, so the delegation must be re-executed from home. Sahibayn: the journey is valid, so the wasiyyah is fulfilled from the place of death.
Sahib al-Hidayah states this as the fundamental difference.

دلیل اور وہی قیاس ہے یہ ہے کہ نائب کا جو سفر موجود ہے یعنی وطن سے لے کر اس کے مرنے کی جگہ تک وہ احکام دنیا کے حق میں معدوم ہو گیا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ آدمی جب مر جاتا ہے تو اس کا عمل منقطع ہو جاتا ہے سوائے تین اعمال کے۔ (۱) صدقہ جاریہ (۲) علم نافع (۳) ولد صالح اور یہ سفر ان تین اعمال میں سے نہیں ہے درانحالیکہ وصیت نافذ کرنا احکام دنیا سے ہے تو گویا اس کا یہ سفر یعنی وطن سے موت کی جگہ تک حدیث کی روشنی میں کالعدم ہو گیا ہے اور جب کالعدم ہو گیا تو گویا اس نے سفر شروع ہی نہیں کیا اور جب سفر شروع نہیں کیا تو وصیت کو پورا کرنے کے لئے میت کے وطن سے از سر نو حج کرانا واجب رہا۔ صاحبین کی دلیل اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ اس کا سفر معدوم نہیں ہوا کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے وَمَنْ يَخْرُجُ مِنْ بَيْتِهِ مُهَاجِرًا إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ ثُمَّ يُدْرِكُهُ الْمَوْتُ فَقَدْ وَقَعَ أَجْرُهُ عَلَى اللهِ ( النساء ١٠٠) یعنی جو شخص اپنے گھر سے اللہ اور رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف ہجرت کر کے نکلا پھر اس کو راستہ میں موت نے آلیا تو اس کا ثواب اللہ پر ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ راستہ میں موت سے ثواب کامل ملتا ہے اور یہی سفر کا مقصود ہے اور سفر ہجرت میں سفرحج اور سفر جہاد بھی ہے بلکہ صریح نص ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص حج کے راستہ میں مرا تو اسکے لئے ہر سال ایک حج مقبول کا ثواب لکھا جاتا ہے۔ بہر حال جب اس سفر کا ثواب مل گیا تو اس کا یہ سفر باطل نہیں ہوا۔ اور جب سفر باطل نہیں ہوا تو وصیت کا اعتبار اسی جگہ سے ہوگا جہاں اس کی موت آئی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان اصل اختلاف اس شخص کے حق میں ہے جو خود حج کرنے کو نکالا تھا۔ راستہ میں مرگیا اور وصیت کر گیا کہ میری طرف سے حج کرا دیا جائے تو صاحبین کے نزدیک جہاں مرا ہے اسی مقام سے وصیت معتبر ہو گی ۔ اسی پر مامور بانج مبنی ہے کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک مامور جہاں مرا یہ سفر کا لعدم شمار ہوگا اور دوبارہ گھر سے نفاذ وصیت ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک و میں سے جہاں مرا سے وصیت کا نفاذ ہوگا۔
And if it is not possible, then in that case too the wasiyyah becomes invalid. Abu Yusuf's proof: the wealth subject to wasiyyah is one-third of the total estate. So after spending or theft, if some wealth remains and a second Hajj journey is possible from it, it should be performed from that remainder because the place of execution of wasiyyah is this one-third. Therefore, the first and second time the Hajj journey will be performed from it. Abu Hanifa's proof: the executor's distribution and segregation of the estate is only valid when he spends it for the purpose specified by the testator. Because there is no one taking possession on behalf of the testator, so possession will only be when he delivers it to the direction of the wasiyyah. Here the direction of wasiyyah was Hajj, and Hajj has not yet occurred, so it is as if the wealth of wasiyyah was wasted before distribution and segregation. So whatever remains is the entire estate, so the second Hajj journey should be performed from its one-third. Similarly, when it was wasted before delivering to the direction of wasiyyah, then from the remaining wealth (i.e., one-third of three thousand) he should perform the second Hajj journey, so that if that too is wasted before completion, it is considered non-existent and performing Hajj from the one-third of the remainder (i.e., two thousand rupees) becomes obligatory. In the second issue, Abu Hanifa's proof—and it is the qiyas—is that the agent's existing journey from his home to the place of his death is considered non-existent in terms of worldly rulings. Because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'When a person dies, his deeds are cut off except three: ongoing charity, beneficial knowledge, and righteous child.' This journey is not among these three, while executing wasiyyah is from worldly rulings, so his journey from home to the place of death is, in light of the hadith, as if it were void. And when it is void, it is as if he never started the journey, and when he did not start, performing Hajj anew from the deceased's home to fulfill the wasiyyah remained obligatory. The Sahibayn's proof and basis of istihsan: his journey is not void because Allah says: 'Whoever leaves his home as a migrant towards Allah and His Messenger, and then death overtakes him, his reward is with Allah' (An-Nisa 4:100). This shows that death on the path brings full reward, and that is the purpose of the journey. The journey of hijrah includes the journey of Hajj and jihad. There is also a clear text that the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever dies on the path of Hajj, for him is written the reward of an accepted Hajj every year.' In any case, when the reward for this journey is granted, his journey is not void. And when the journey is not void, the wasiyyah is considered from the place where he died. Sahib al-Hidayah states: The fundamental difference between Imam [Abu Hanifa] and the two companions (Sahibayn) concerns the person who himself set out to perform Hajj, died on the way, and made a wasiyyah that Hajj be performed on his behalf. According to the two companions, the wasiyyah will be considered from the place where he died. This also applies to the appointed agent (ma'mur): according to Imam, the agent's journey where he died will be considered void, and the wasiyyah will be executed from home anew; according to the two companions, it will be executed from where he died.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) on a specific issue: a person sets out for Hajj, dies en route, and had made a wasiyyah (will) for Hajj to be performed on his behalf. The question is whether the Hajj should be performed from the deceased's original home (as per Abu Hanifa) or from the place where he died (as per the Sahibayn).

The passage first presents Imam Abu Yusuf's position (though it begins with 'Imam Abu Yusuf's proof') regarding the first scenario where wealth was spent or stolen. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the one-third of the estate designated for wasiyyah remains the locus of the obligation; if any part remains, the Hajj should be performed from that remainder. Imam Abu Hanifa counters that the wasiyyah is only valid when the wealth is delivered to the specified purpose (the Hajj journey); since the Hajj has not occurred, the wealth is considered wasted before delivery, so the remaining wealth becomes the entire estate, and the second Hajj must be from its one-third.

Then the passage moves to a second scenario concerning a proxy (na'ib) who dies while performing Hajj on behalf of another. Imam Abu Hanifa uses qiyas (analogy): the proxy's journey from home to the place of death is void under worldly rulings because, according to the hadith that after death only three deeds continue, the journey is severed. Thus the proxy never started the journey, and the wasiyyah must be fulfilled from the original home. The Sahibayn rely on istihsan (juristic preference) citing Quran 4:100 and a hadith that dying on the path of Hajj brings reward, so the journey is valid, and the wasiyyah is executed from the place of death.

Sahib al-Hidayah summarizes: the dispute applies both to the original testator and to the appointed agent (ma'mur). Imam Abu Hanifa holds the journey void, requiring a fresh start from home; the Sahibayn hold the journey valid, so the wasiyyah is executed from the place of death.

All evidence is clearly cited: the hadith on cutting off deeds, Quran 4:100, and the hadith on dying during Hajj. The commentary follows the order of the text, presenting each position with its proof and the final summary.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A will or bequest; here specifically a testamentary instruction to perform Hajj on behalf of the deceased using one-third of the estate.
نائب (na'ib): A proxy or agent appointed to perform Hajj on behalf of another; in this context, the person who dies while acting as an agent.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; here used by Sahibayn to prioritize the Quranic and hadith evidence about reward over the general principle of severance of deeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), why is the journey of a person who dies en route to Hajj NOT considered void?
A) Because the journey is mentioned in the hadith about three ongoing deeds.
B) Because the Quran and hadith promise reward for dying on the path of Hajj, indicating the journey's validity.
C) Because the wasiyyah itself makes the journey valid regardless of death.
D) Because the proxy can always choose the starting point.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, there is a legitimate disagreement over whether the journey of a person who dies en route to Hajj is void or valid for executing a wasiyyah, depending on the weight given to the hadith on severed deeds versus texts promising reward.

Ruling on Talbiyah for Both Parents
Ruling on changing intention after talbiyah for both parents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person makes talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of both parents and explain the distinction from an appointed agent (ma'mur).

Core Idea
If you make talbiyah for both parents, you may perform Hajj for one; the reward is dedicated after Hajj, not before.

This lesson examines a concise ruling in Hanafi fiqh: what happens when a person declares ihram for Hajj on behalf of both parents? The text clarifies that the intention made at talbiyah does not bind the performer to both; rather, the reward assignment occurs after the Hajj. We will also understand why this differs from the case of a paid agent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial intention
The person makes talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of both father and mother simultaneously.
Talbiyah here includes the intention to dedicate the reward.
2
Recognize the ruling
The text states it is sufficient to perform the Hajj for one of them. This is the core legal outcome.
The word 'yujzihi' indicates validity and sufficiency.
3
Understand the rationale
The reward (thawab) is dedicated after the Hajj performance. Therefore, the prior intention to dedicate to both becomes void, and one can choose after the act.
This is based on the principle that dedication of reward occurs after the deed.
4
Apply the distinction with ma'mur
Contrast with a ma'mur (appointed agent) who cannot change the beneficiary because he acts under a contract. This distinction is central to the ruling.
The text refers to a previous distinction: a volunteer vs. a contracted agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ أَهَلَّ بِحَجَّةٍ عَنْ أَبَوَيْهِ يُجْزِيهِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَهُ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا لِأَنَّ مَنْ حَجَّ عَنْ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ فَإِنَّمَا يَجْعَلُ ثَوَابَ حجّه لَهُ وَذَلِكَ بَعْدَ أداءِ الْحَج فَلَغَتْ بَيْتَهُ قَبلَ أدَائِهِ وَصحَ جَعَلَهُ ثَوَابَهُ لأحدهما بعد الأداءِ بِخِلَافِ المَأْمُورِ عَلَى مَا فَرَّقْنَا مِنْ قَبل وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوابِ ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اپنے والدین کی طرف سے حج کا تلبیہ کہا تو اس کو جائز ہے کہ وہ حج کو والدین میں سے ایک کی طرف سے کر دے۔ کیونکہ جس نے دوسرے کی طرف سے بغیر اس کی اجازت کے حج کیا تو اس حج کا ثواب اس غیر کے لئے کر دیتا ہے اور یہ حج وا کرنے کے بعد ہے۔ پس حج ادا کرنے سے پہلے کی اس کی نیت افر ہوگئی ہے اور ادا کرنے کے بعد اس کا ثواب والدین میں سے ایک کے ایسے کرنا صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف مامور کے اس بنا پر کہ ہم نے سابق میں فرق بیان کر دیا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم با اصواب۔
He said: Whoever makes talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of both his parents, it suffices him to make it for one of them. Because whoever performs Hajj on behalf of another without his permission, he only gives the reward of his Hajj to that other, and that is after the performance of the Hajj. So his intention before performance becomes void, and it is correct for him to give its reward to one of them after performance, unlike the appointed agent (ma'mur) based on the distinction we made before. And Allah knows best what is correct. Translation: And whoever says talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of his parents, it is permissible for him to perform the Hajj on behalf of one of them. Because whoever performs Hajj on behalf of another without his permission, he gives the reward of that Hajj to that other, and that is after completing the Hajj. So his intention before performance becomes void, and after performance it is correct for him to assign the reward to one of the parents. Unlike the appointed agent, based on the distinction we explained previously. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This is a short matn (statement) from the text, followed by an Urdu translation and brief explanation. The ruling: If a person makes talbiyah (declaration of intention) for Hajj on behalf of both parents (e.g., saying 'Labbaik for Hajj on behalf of my father and mother'), it is valid for him to perform the Hajj for only one of them. The reason is that when one performs Hajj on behalf of another without their specific permission, he is essentially dedicating the reward to that person after the Hajj is completed. The intention to dedicate for both is made before performance, but since the dedication occurs after the Hajj (when the reward is earned), the prior intention is void. After the Hajj, he can assign the reward to whichever parent he chooses. This differs from the case of an appointed agent (ma'mur) who is explicitly authorized to perform Hajj on behalf of someone; the agent cannot change the beneficiary because he acts under a specific contract. The text refers to a previous distinction made in the book. The passage emphasizes that the dedication of reward (isal al-thawab) is a separate act that occurs after the Hajj, so the initial talbiyah does not bind him to both parents.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The declaration 'Labbaik Allahumma Labbaik' made to enter the state of ihram, specifying the intended Hajj or Umrah; here it includes the intention of offering it on behalf of someone.
مأمور (ma'mur): A person who is specifically appointed by someone (the amir/muwakkil) to perform Hajj on their behalf under a contract; he is bound by the appointment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone says talbiyah for Hajj on behalf of both parents, what is the ruling?
A) The Hajj is invalid for both
B) He must perform Hajj for both parents
C) It is permissible to perform it for one parent after the Hajj
D) The Hajj must be repeated for one parent

Key Takeaway
Making talbiyah for both parents does not bind the performer; after Hajj, the reward can be assigned to one parent, unless the performer is a paid agent.

Minimum and Types of Hady
Ruling with proof: minimum hady and types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum hady (sacrificial animal) according to the Hanafi school, identify the three permissible types, and explain the Prophetic proof for the minimum.

Core Idea
The minimum hady is a sheep; camel and cow are also valid as higher types.

Hady is the animal sacrificed in the Haram during Hajj, required for tamattu', qiran, and certain penalties. This lesson establishes the minimum acceptable animal and the full set of permissible types, based on a direct statement from the Prophet ﷺ and the inference that a minimum implies higher categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage defines hady and states its minimum: 'أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ' (its minimum is a sheep). This is the primary ruling.
2
Examine the dalil
The proof is a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ was asked about hady and replied 'its minimum is a sheep.' The wording is a direct answer, establishing the minimum as a sheep.
The hadith is ahad (single narration), giving zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Recognize the inference for higher types
Since the Prophet specified a minimum, there must be higher types. The text mentions camel and cow as the higher categories, alongside sheep.
The reasoning is by implication (dalil al-khitab or mafhum al-ghayah?).
4
Confirm the three types
The passage explicitly lists three types: camel (إبل), cow (بقر), and sheep/goat (غنم). They are equal in the purpose: to draw near to Allah through sacrifice in the Haram.
All three are acceptable; sheep is the minimum.
5
Apply the ruling
A pilgrim may offer any of the three types. Offering a sheep fulfills the minimum; offering a camel or cow is superior but not obligatory.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بابُ الْهَدْي ترجمہ یہ باب بدی کے بیان میں ہے الهَدَى أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ سُئِلَ عَنِ الْهَدَي فَقَالَ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ ترجمہ ارنی درجہ کی بدنی بکری ہے کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم سے بدی کے بارے میں دریافت کیا گیا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ادانی درجہ کی ہری بھری ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔ تشریحی هدی کی اقسام قبال وهو من ثلثة أنواع الابل والبقر والغنم لأنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمَّا جَعَلَ الشَّاة أدنى لَا بُدَّ أنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ أعلى وَهُوَ وَالْجُرُورُ لِأَنَّ الْهُدَى مَا يُهدى إلى الحرم لِيَتَقَرَّبَ بِهِ فِيهِ وَالْأَصْنَافُ الثَّلَثَةُ سَوَاءٌ فِي هَذَا الْمَعْنى
Chapter of Hady. Translation: This chapter is about the sacrificial animal (hady). The minimum of hady is a sheep, because it is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ was asked about hady and he said: 'Its minimum is a sheep.' Translation: The minimum of hady is a sheep because the Prophet ﷺ was asked about hady and he said: 'Its minimum is a sheep.' Commentary: It is clear. Commentary: The types of hady: He said: It is from three types: camel, cow, and goat/sheep. Because when the Prophet ﷺ made the sheep the minimum, necessarily there must be a higher type, and that is the camel and the cow, because hady is what is sent to the Haram to draw near to Allah through it, and the three types are equal in this meaning.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on Hady (the sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj). It begins with the definition: the minimum hady is a sheep (shaat), supported by a hadith where the Prophet ﷺ directly stated this when asked. The Urdu commentary then clarifies that this is clear. Next, the text states that hady can be of three types: camel (ibil), cow (baqr), and goat/sheep (ghanam). The reasoning: since the Prophet ﷺ designated the sheep as the minimum, there must be a higher type (i.e., camel and cow). Moreover, the purpose of hady is to send an animal to the Haram for nearness to Allah, and all three types serve this purpose equally. The passage thus establishes both the minimum value (a sheep) and the permissible categories of animals. It does not discuss conditions of age or defects; that would come later in the chapter.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram (Mecca) for nearness to Allah during Hajj.
شاة (shaat): Sheep or goat; the minimum hady.
إبل (ibil): Camel; a higher type of hady.
بقر (baqr): Cow; a higher type of hady.
غنم (ghanam): Sheep/goat collectively; includes shaat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum acceptable animal for hady according to the hadith cited in the passage?
A) A camel
B) A cow
C) A sheep
D) Any animal

Key Takeaway
The minimum hady is a sheep; camel and cow are also permissible, as all three serve the same purpose of drawing near to Allah in the Haram.

Redirecting Hajj Intended for Both Parents to One
Permissibility of directing joint hajj talbiyah to one parent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on redirecting hajj intended for both parents, explain the talil based on reward assignment after performance, and distinguish it from the case of the ma'mur.

Core Idea
A single hajj intended for two can be redirected to one after performance; intention before performance is void.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah regarding hajj performed on behalf of another without explicit permission. The key is understanding when the intention becomes binding and how reward is assigned. You will see that the Hanafi school allows a volunteer to redirect a joint intention to one recipient, unlike a commissioned agent (ma'mur) whose intention is restricted from the start.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Initial Intention
The person makes talbiyah for hajj intending it for both parents simultaneously. Understand the scenario — this is a single hajj with a dual intention.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The text rules: it suffices (yujzihi) to make the hajj on behalf of one parent. This is permissible (ja'iz) and valid.
3
Analyze the Closing Argument (Talil)
The reasoning: when one performs hajj for another without permission, the reward is assigned only after completion. Therefore, the initial intention for both is void (laghw) before performance. After hajj, redirecting the reward to one parent is valid.
This is based on the principle that reward assignment (ja'l al-thawab) occurs after the act, not before.
4
Distinguish the Case of the Ma'mur
The text says 'contrary to the commanded one (al-ma'mur)', referring to a person who is specifically commissioned to perform hajj on behalf of a designated person. For the ma'mur, the intention is tied to the command and cannot be redirected, as explained earlier.
The ma'mur acts under a binding contract (ijarah or tawkil), so his intention is restricted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے اپنے والدین کی طرف سے حج کا تلبیہ کہا اسے جائز ہے کہ وہ حج کو کسی ایک طرف سے کر دے قَالَ وَمَنْ أَهَلَّ بِحَجَّةٍ عَنْ أَبَوَيْهِ يُجْزِيهِ أَنْ يَجْعَلَهُ عَنْ أَحَدِهِمَا لِأَنَّ مَنْ حَجَّ عَنْ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ فَإِنَّمَا يَجْعَلُ ثَوَابَ حجّه لَهُ وَذَلِكَ بَعْدَ أداءِ الْحَج فَلَغَتْ بَيْتَهُ قَبلَ أدَائِهِ وَصحَ جَعَلَهُ ثَوَابَهُ لأحدهما بعد الأداءِ بِخِلَافِ المَأْمُورِ عَلَى مَا فَرَّقْنَا مِنْ قَبل وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوابِ ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اپنے والدین کی طرف سے حج کا تلبیہ کہا تو اس کو جائز ہے کہ وہ حج کو والدین میں سے ایک کی طرف سے کر دے۔ کیونکہ جس نے دوسرے کی طرف سے بغیر اس کی اجازت کے حج کیا تو اس حج کا ثواب اس غیر کے لئے کر دیتا ہے اور یہ حج وا کرنے کے بعد ہے۔ پس حج ادا کرنے سے پہلے کی اس کی نیت افر ہوگئی ہے اور ادا کرنے کے بعد اس کا ثواب والدین میں سے ایک کے ایسے کرنا صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف مامور کے اس بنا پر کہ ہم نے سابق میں فرق بیان کر دیا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم با اصواب۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔ جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Whoever makes talbiyah for hajj on behalf of both his parents, it suffices him to make it on behalf of one of them, because whoever performs hajj on behalf of another without his permission, he only assigns the reward of his hajj to him, and that is after performing the hajj. So his intention becomes void before performance, and after performance his assigning the reward to one of them is valid, contrary to the commanded (one), as we distinguished previously. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah, with commentary. The issue is: a person intends hajj on behalf of both parents simultaneously (e.g., making talbiyah with the intention of both). The ruling is that it is valid for him to subsequently specify the hajj for only one parent after performing it. The reasoning is that when someone performs hajj on behalf of another without the other's permission, the reward goes to that other person only after the hajj is completed. Before completion, the intention is not binding. Therefore, his initial intention for both is ineffective (laghw) before performance, but after performing the hajj, he can validly direct the reward to one of them. This differs from the case of a person who is commanded (al-ma'mur) to perform hajj on behalf of a specific person, where the intention is restricted from the start. The distinction was explained earlier. The commentary confirms this ruling and notes it is clear.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The declaration of intention for hajj or umrah, typically saying 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk'.
مامور (al-ma'mur): A person who is commanded or appointed to perform hajj on behalf of a specific person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the person is a ma'mur.
B) Because reward is assigned only after the hajj is performed.
C) Because the intention must be for one person only from the start.
D) Because both parents must give permission after the hajj.

Key Takeaway
A volunteer can redirect a joint hajj intended for two to one recipient after performance because reward assignment occurs after the act, unlike a commissioned agent.

Minimum of Hady is a Sheep
Determining the minimal sacrificial animal for hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum animal for hady and identify the hadith proof that establishes it.

Core Idea
The Prophet explicitly set the minimum hady as a sheep — no larger animal is required.

This lesson examines a foundational rule in the chapter of hady: the minimum sacrifice acceptable during Hajj. The text from Al-Hidayah provides a clear ruling supported by a direct prophetic statement. Understanding this baseline prevents unnecessary burden on pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the legal minimum for the hady animal as given in the text: a sheep (or goat).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence: the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about hady and replied, 'Its lowest is a sheep.'
The proof is a hadith; its transmission is ahad but the meaning is clear.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling: the word 'adnahu' (its lowest) sets a definitive minimum, implying that a sheep suffices and anything less does not.
The explicit phrasing (sarih) leaves no ambiguity regarding the minimum.
4
Note the cross-madhhab agreement
Confirm that this ruling is agreed upon by all major schools, so there is no ikhtilaf on the basic minimum.
Disagreement exists only on whether a share in a larger animal (e.g., 1/7 of a camel) is equivalent, but the minimum animal remains a sheep.

Source pages p. 527

This passage opens the chapter on Hady (sacrificial animals brought to the Haram). It states that the minimum acceptable animal for hady is a sheep (or goat). The proof is a hadith: when asked about hady, the Prophet said the minimum is a sheep. This establishes the baseline; larger animals like camels and cows are also valid but are considered higher. Species Permissible for Hady: Camel, Cow, and Goat
Specifying the three species permissible for hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three species permissible for hady in the Hanafi school and explain the proof (talil) that establishes them exclusively.

Core Idea
Only camels, cows, and goats/sheep are valid for hady; any other animal is invalid.

This passage specifies the animals that can be offered as hady during Hajj and Umrah. It presents a proof based on the Prophet's designation of the sheep as the minimum, implying the existence of higher categories, and the common purpose of taqarrub. Understanding this ruling ensures that your sacrifice is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and species
The passage states that hady must be from one of three types: camels, cows, or goats/sheep. This is the operative ruling.
2
Understand the first proof: from the minimum to the higher
The Prophet made the sheep the lowest type of hady. From this, we infer that there must be a higher type; otherwise, setting the sheep as the minimum would be meaningless. The higher types are camels and cows.
This reasoning is talil (deductive inference).
3
Understand the second proof: common purpose of taqarrub
The essence of hady is to send an animal to the Haram to draw near to Allah. All three species equally fulfill this purpose, so they are all valid.
This is a textual expansion of the meaning of hady.
4
Conclude the exclusivity
Only these three species are valid. No other animal, regardless of size, is permissible for hady according to the Hanafi school.
This is the mufta bihi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it (hady) is of three types: camels, cows, and goats. Because when the Prophet (peace be upon him) made the sheep the lowest, there must be a higher (type), and that is the camel and cow. Because hady is what is sent to the Haram to draw near through it therein, and the three species are equal in this meaning.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage explains the three valid species for hady: camels (ibl), cows (baqar), and goats/sheep (ghanam). The proof is twofold: first, since the Prophet set the sheep as the minimum, logically there must be a higher type, which are camels and cows. Second, the essence of hady is to send an animal to the Haram for the purpose of drawing near to Allah (taqarrub). All three species fulfill this purpose equally, so all are valid. The Urdu commentary elaborates similarly.

Key Terms
ابل بقر غنم (ibil, baqar, ghanam): Camels, cattle (cows), and small livestock (sheep/goats). These are the only species allowed for hady in the Hanafi school.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram during Hajj or Umrah to seek nearness to Allah.
تقرب (taqarrub): Drawing near to Allah through an act of worship. The purpose of hady is taqarrub.
