Animals Valid for Hady: Equivalence with Udhiyah
Establishing equivalence between hady and udhiyah animals via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that the animals valid for hady are the same as for udhiyah, and identify the qiyas (analogy) that forms its proof.

Core Idea
Hady and udhiyah share the same legal conditions because both are acts of devotion involving bloodshed.

This lesson examines a concise yet foundational ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the animals permissible for hady (sacrificial offering during Hajj) are exactly those permissible for udhiyah (Eid sacrifice). The text from Al-Hidayah establishes this through a clear qiyas (analogy), citing the common cause (illa) of being a 'qurbah connected to spilling blood'. Understanding this analogy helps you see how Hanafi jurists systematically extend rulings across similar acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the legal equivalence: only animals valid for udhiyah are valid for hady.
The text explicitly says 'nothing is permissible... except what is permissible in udhiyah'.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
Recognize the qiyas structure: the text gives the reason (illa) 'because it is a qurbah connected to spilling blood, like udhiyah'.
This is a clear qiyas jali (manifest analogy).
3
Extract the Illa (Effective Cause)
The common cause is being an act of devotion (qurbah) that involves the spilling of blood (iraqat al-dam).
This illa is shared between hady and udhiyah, making them legally analogous.
4
Confirm the Mahall (Subject)
Because of the shared illa, both hady and udhiyah are specified by the same subject (mahall), meaning the same animal types and conditions.
Thus, the conditions for udhiyah animals apply equally to hady.
5
Apply the Conditions
List the known conditions: camel (5+ years), cow (2+ years), sheep/goat (1+ year), and must be free from defects (e.g., blindness, lameness).
These conditions are derived from udhiyah rulings and are now binding for hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ فِى الْهَدَايَا إِلَّا مَا جَازَ فِى الصّحَايَا لِأَنَّهُ قُرْبَةٌ تَعَلَّقُت بِإِرَاقَةِ الدَّمِ كَالأَضْحِيَّةِ فَيَتَحَصَّصَانِ بِمَحَلِّ وَاحِدٍ ترجمہ اور ہدایا میں وہی جانور جائز ہیں جو ضحایا میں جائز ہیں کیونکہ بدی بھی اضحیہ کے مانند ایسی قربت ہے جو خون بہانے سے متعلق ر ہے۔ نہیں وہ دون ایک محل کے ساتھ خاص ہیں۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And nothing is permissible in hadaya except what is permissible in adhaya (udhiyah), because it is an act of devotion (qurbah) connected to spilling blood, like udhiyah, so both are specified by the same subject (mahall).
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This ruling establishes that the same animals valid for udhiyah (the sacrifice on Eid al-Adha) are also valid for hady (sacrificial animals for hajj). The reasoning is qiyas (analogy): both hady and udhiyah are acts of devotion (qurbah) that involve the spilling of blood (iraqat al-dam). Because they share this essential characteristic, they share the same subject (mahall) meaning the same types of animals. Therefore, conditions for udhiyah animals (like age, health, no defects) apply equally to hady animals. The commentary affirms this is clear.

Key Terms
قربۃ تعلقت باراقۃ الدم (qurbatun ta'allaqat bi-iraqat al-dam): An act of worship connected to the spilling of blood (slaughtering).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Because both are optional

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the conditions for hady and udhiyah are identical because both are qurbah linked to bloodshed.

Two Exceptions Where Only a Camel Suffices for Hady
Exceptions to the general rule of sheep in hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two exceptions where a sheep is not sufficient for hady and identify the required animal.

Core Idea
A sheep suffices for all hady except two serious violations: tawaf in janabah and intercourse after wuquf — only a camel atones.

This lesson memorizes a key rule from al-Hidayah: the general permissibility of using a sheep for hady, and the two specific cases where only a camel is valid. Tawaf al-ziyarah while in major impurity and sexual intercourse after standing at Arafat both incur a penalty that cannot be fulfilled by a sheep.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the general rule
Start with the base rule: a sheep (or goat) is valid for all types of hady (sacrificial offerings during Hajj). This is the default.
2
Identify the two exceptions
The text lists exactly two cases where a sheep does not suffice: (1) performing tawaf al-ziyarah while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and (2) having sexual intercourse after the wuquf at Arafat.
These are serious violations that require a heavier expiation.
3
Specify the required animal
In these two exceptions, only a badanah (camel) is valid. No other animal, such as a cow or sheep, can substitute.
The term badanah in Hanafi fiqh specifically means a camel; a cow is not sufficient.
4
Understand the rationale
The reason for the higher requirement is the gravity of the sin. Tawaf in janabah invalidates the tawaf and intercourse after wuquf invalidates the Hajj (or makes it incomplete). Both demand a more significant sacrifice.
The text refers to a previous explanation (وقد بينا المعنى فيما سبق) for the detailed reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشَّاةَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْن مَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الزَّيَارَة جُنَّبًا وَمَنْ حَامِعِ بَعدِ الْوُقُوبِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ فِيهِمَا إِلَّا يُدْنَةٌ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَا الْمَعْنَى فِيمَا سَبَقَ ترجمہ اور بکری ہر جگہ میں جائز ہے علاوہ دو جگہ سے (ایک) جس نے بحالت جنابت طواف زیارت کیا اور (دوسرے ) وہ جس نے وقوف کے بعد جماع کیا۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں جگہوں میں جائز نہیں مگر بدنہ۔ اور انیل ہم سابق میں بیان کر چکے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And the sheep is valid in everything except in two cases: one who performs tawaf al-ziyarah while in a state of janabah, and one who has intercourse after standing (wuquf). Then it is not valid in these two except a badanah (camel). And we have explained the meaning previously.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This is a memorization anchor: a sheep (or goat) suffices for all types of hady except in two specific situations where only a camel (badanah) is acceptable. The two exceptions are: (1) A person who performs tawaf al-ziyarah (the essential circumambulation of the Kaaba) while in a state of janabah (major impurity, e.g., after sexual intercourse without ghusl). (2) A person who has sexual intercourse after the wuquf (standing) at Arafat. In both cases, a sheep is not sufficient; a camel (or cow? but text says badanah which is a camel) is required. The reason, as explained earlier, likely relates to the severity of the sin and the need for a heavier expiation. The commentary simply notes it is clear.

Key Terms
بدنہ (badanah): A camel, specifically the larger sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Leaving a wajib and failing to give charity
D) Only for qiran hady

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a sheep suffices for all hady except two cases: tawaf al-ziyarah in janabah and intercourse after wuquf; only a camel atones.

Eating from Hady of Tamattu', Qiran, and Nafil
Ruling on eating from voluntary and tamattu'/qiran hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating from tamattu', qiran, and nafil hady, and cite the dalil from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Eating from your own tamattu', qiran, and nafil hady is permissible, just like udhiyah.

Many pilgrims assume that hady meat must be entirely given in charity, but the Hanafi school permits the offerer to eat from certain types of hady. This lesson clarifies which types and why, based on the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is eating from the meat of hady offered for tamattu', qiran, or nafil. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible).
The ruling applies to the person who offered the animal; others may eat if given permission.
2
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The text reasons that these types of hady are 'dam nasak' – ritual sacrifices similar to udhiyah, which the offerer may eat from.
This distinguishes them from penalty hady (dam al-jinaya) which cannot be eaten.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith that the Prophet (SAW) ate from his own hady meat and drank its broth.
The hadith is cited as sahih (authentic).
4
Examine the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action (fi'l) is legislative; it indicates permissibility unless there is evidence to the contrary. The Hanafi principle is that the Prophet's actions that are not proven to be specific to him are general for the ummah.
This is a key usul principle: fi'l al-nabi yufid al-ibahah.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that eating from tamattu' and qiran hady is not allowed. The Hanafi response is that these are dam nasak, and the Prophet's practice confirms permissibility.
The practical difference is that Hanafis may eat, while Shafi'is must give all meat as sadaqah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ الأكل من هذي التطوع والمتعة والقران لأنه دَم نَسَب فَيَجُوزُ الْأُكُلُ مِنْهَا بِسْزِلَةِ الْأَضَحِيَّةِ وَقَدْ صَحْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أكل من لحم هديهِ وَحَسَّامِنَ الْمِرْقَةِ ترجمہ تخلی اور نیکی بدی ، میری تمتع اور بیدی قرآن میں سے خود کھانا جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ نسک کا دم ہے تو الضحیہ کی طرح ان میں سے کیا ہوا ہے۔ اور یہ میچ ہے کہ حضور نے اپنے بدی کے گوشت میں سے کھایا اور شور بے میں سے پیا۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And it is permissible to eat from nafil hady, tamattu', and qiran, because it is the blood of a rite (dam nasak), so it is permissible to eat from it in the status of udhiyah. And it is confirmed that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ate from the meat of his hady and drank from the broth.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This ruling permits the one who offers hady to eat from it if the hady is voluntary (nafil), part of tamattu' (the hajj performed with umrah first), or qiran (combined hajj and umrah). The reasoning is that these types of hady are like the udhiyah sacrifice—they are offerings (dam nasak) that the owner can consume. The proof is a hadith that the Prophet ate from the meat of his own hady and drank its broth. This indicates that consumption is allowed. The Urdu commentary confirms this.

Key Terms
دم نسک (dam nasak): Blood (sacrifice) of a ritual, i.e., a sacrificial animal offered as part of a rites of hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of hady is NOT mentioned as permissible to eat from in the text?
A) Nafil
B) Tamattu'
C) Qiran
D) Penalty hady

Key Takeaway
Nafil, tamattu', and qiran hady may be eaten because they are ritual sacrifices (dam nasak), unlike penalty hady.

Types of Hadi Animals and Correspondence with Udhiya
Explains types of Hadi animals and establishes equivalence with Udhiya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of animals valid for Hadi and explain the principle that Hadi and Udhiya share the same animal requirements.

Core Idea
Only animals valid for Udhiya are valid for Hadi — both are blood-based acts of worship with identical requirements.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a basic question: Which animals can be offered as Hadi during Hajj? It provides two proofs and then links Hadi to Udhiya, establishing a key principle. Understanding this equivalence is essential for fulfilling Hadi obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Valid Animals
Read the passage to determine which animals are explicitly mentioned as valid for Hadi.
Three types: camel, cow, goat.
2
Examine the First Proof
The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) graded the goat as the lowest Hadi, implying that higher grades (camel, cow) are acceptable.
This is a Prophetic practice indicating validity.
3
Examine the Second Proof
Hadi is an act of seeking nearness by offering an animal in the Haram; all three animals serve this purpose equally.
Rational analogy based on the purpose of worship.
4
Apply the Principle Linking Hadi and Udhiya
The text states that only animals valid for Udhiya are valid for Hadi, because both are acts of worship involving bloodshed.
This principle unifies the requirements.
5
Apply to a New Scenario
Given an animal that fails Udhiya conditions (e.g., too young), determine if it can be used for Hadi.
Conclusion: Not valid, because the principle requires Udhiya validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بلا یه جمله سوم ۵۲۷ کتاب الحج اندر تقرب حاصل کیا جائے ۔ اور اس معنی میں تینوں قسمیں برابر ہیں۔ تشریح بدی تین قسم کے جانور ہو سکتے ہیں ۔ اونٹ ،گائے، بکری ۔ اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بکری کو ادنی درجہ کی بدی قرآدیا ہے اور ادنی کے لئے اعلیٰ ہونا ضروری ہے اور اعلیٰ میں گائے اور اونٹ ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بدی وہ ہے جس کو حرم کے اندر اس لئے بھیجا جائے تا کہ اس کے ساتھ تقرب حاصل کیا جائے اور اس مقصد میں تینوں ( بکری ، گائے ، اونٹ ) برابر ہیں ۔ اس لئے ان تینوں کو بدی قرار دیا گیا۔ ہدایا میں وہی جانور درست ہے جو ضحایا میں درست ہے وَلَا يَجُوزُ فِى الْهَدَايَا إِلَّا مَا جَازَ فِى الصّحَايَا لِأَنَّهُ قُرْبَةٌ تَعَلَّقَتُ بِإِرَاقَةِ الدَّمِ كَالأَضْحِيَّةِ فَيَتَحَصَّصَانِ بِمَحَلِّ وَاحِدٍ ترجمہ اور ہدایا ہمیں وہی جانور جائز ہیں جو ضحایا میں جائز ہیں کیونکہ بدی بھی اضحیہ کے مانند ایسی قربت ہے جو خون بہانے سے متعلق ر ہے۔ نہیں وہ دون ایک محل کے ساتھ خاص ہیں۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And in Hadi, only those animals are valid which are valid in Udhiya, because it is an act of worship related to the shedding of blood like Udhiya, so they both are confined to one specification. Translation: And in Hadi, only those animals are permissible which are permissible in Udhiya, because Hadi also, like Udhiya, is an act of worship related to shedding blood; both are specific to one specification.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It first states that the types of animals permissible for Hadi are camel, cow, and goat. Two proofs are given: first, the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) considered the goat as the lowest grade of Hadi, implying that higher grades (camel and cow) are also valid. Second, Hadi is an offering sent to the Haram for seeking nearness to Allah, and all three animals serve this purpose equally. Then the text establishes a principle: only those animals that are valid for Udhiya (sacrifice on Eid al-Adha) are valid for Hadi. The reason is that both Hadi and Udhiya are acts of worship involving the shedding of blood, so they share the same requirements regarding the animal's type, age, and condition.

Key Terms
الهدايا (al-hadaya): Sacrificial animals offered in the Haram during Hajj or for penalties.
الضحايا (al-dahaya): Sacrificial animals slaughtered on Eid al-Adha (Udhiya).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only camel
B) Only goat
C) Camel, cow, and goat
D) Only cow

Key Takeaway
Camel, cow, and goat are all valid for Hadi, and only animals valid for Udhiya are valid for Hadi.

Exceptions: When a Goat Is Insufficient for Hajj Violations
States two exceptions where a goat is insufficient for expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that a goat suffices for any Hajj violation and identify the two exceptions that require a badanah.

Core Idea
A goat suffices for all Hajj violations except Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah and intercourse after Wuquf.

In the Hanafi school, the expiation (dam) for most Hajj violations is a goat. However, this passage highlights two serious violations that demand a larger expiation—a badanah (camel or cow). Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly fulfilling the requirements of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Read the passage and note that it states 'the goat is permissible in everything,' meaning for all jinayat (violations) in Hajj, a goat is sufficient expiation.
2
Locate the two exceptions
The text explicitly lists two violations: (1) performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah, and (2) engaging in sexual intercourse after the Wuquf at Arafat.
3
Determine the alternative requirement
For these two exceptions, the passage states that a goat is not permissible; only a badanah (a camel or cow) is acceptable as expiation.
Badanah is considered a higher form of expiation.
4
Recognize the authority of the ruling
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school. The text references a previous explanation for the reasoning.
Al-Hidayah presents this as the relied-upon ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بکری ہر جنایت سے کافی ہے مگر دو جناتوں میں کافی نہیں وَالشَّاةَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْن مَنْ طَافَ طَوَافَ الزَّيَارَة جُنَّبًا وَمَنْ حَامِعِ بَعدِ الْوُقُوبِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَجُوزُ فِيهِمَا إِلَّا يُدْنَةٌ وَقَدْ بَيَّنَا الْمَعْنَى فِيمَا سَبَقَ ترجمہ اور بکری ہر جگہ میں جائز ہے علاوہ دو جگہ سے (ایک) جس نے بحالت جنابت طواف زیارت کیا اور (دوسرے ) وہ جس نے وقوف کے بعد جماع کیا۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں جگہوں میں جائز نہیں مگر بدنہ۔ اور انیل ہم سابق میں بیان کر چکے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And the goat is permissible in everything except two places: one who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah, and one who has intercourse after Wuquf. Then it is not permissible in these two except a badanah. And we have explained the meaning previously. Translation: And a goat is permissible in every case except two cases: (1) one who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah and (2) one who had intercourse after Wuquf. Because in these two cases it is not permissible except a badanah. And we have explained its meaning previously.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a ruling stating a general rule with two exceptions. The general rule is that a goat is sufficient for any violation (jinayah) in Hajj. However, there are two violations for which a goat is not sufficient: (1) performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of major ritual impurity (janabah), and (2) engaging in sexual intercourse after the Wuquf at Arafat. For these two, only a badanah (a camel or a cow) is acceptable. The text refers to a previous explanation for the reasoning, which is that these are major violations that require a more significant expiation.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The essential tawaf of Hajj, performed after coming from Mina on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow offered as a sacrificial animal.
جناية (jinayah): A violation or offence committed during Hajj that requires expiation (dam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a goat is sufficient for all Hajj violations except performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of janabah and engaging in intercourse after Wuquf, both of which require a badanah.

Eating from Hadi: Permissible and Prohibited Types
Explains permissibility of eating from voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran Hadi, and prohibition from expiatory Hadi, with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which types of Hadi the pilgrim may eat from (voluntary, Tamattu', Qiran) and which are prohibited (expiatory), and cite the two proofs from the Sunnah for each ruling.

Core Idea
Not all Hadi meat is for eating — voluntary and Hajj ritual Hadi are permissible; expiatory Hadi is exclusively for the poor of the Haram.

In this lesson, we examine a key distinction in the rulings of Hadi (sacrificial animals brought during Hajj). The Hanafi school, drawing on the Prophet's practice and a specific prohibition at Hudaybiyyah, clarifies that some Hadi are meant to be eaten by the pilgrim, while others are strictly for charity. Understanding this distinction is essential for anyone performing Hajj or issuing fatwas related to its rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three permissible types
Locate in the text the types of Hadi from which eating is allowed: voluntary (tatabbu'), Tamattu', and Qiran. Note that these are collectively called 'dam nusuk' (ritual sacrifice).
2
Understand the analogy to Udhiya
The text states these are like Udhiya (sacrifice of Eid). Reflect: just as one may eat from Udhiya, one may eat from these Hadi. This is the basis of analogy.
3
Identify the prohibited types
Find the phrase 'wa la yajuzu al-akl min baqiyyat al-hadaya' — all other Hadi (expiatory/kafarat and jinayat) are not permissible to eat. They are exclusively for the poor of Haram.
4
Analyze the first proof: Prophet's action
The text cites that the Prophet ate from his Hadi and drank its broth. This is a proof of permissibility for the first category. Note that the Prophet's action (fi'l) indicates permissibility (ibaha) and also recommendation.
5
Analyze the second proof: Hudaybiyyah prohibition
The text reports that when the Prophet was prevented (ihsar) at Hudaybiyyah, he sent expiatory Hadi with Najiya and forbade him and his companions from eating it because they were wealthy. This shows expiatory Hadi are for the poor only.

Source Text

السَّلَامُ أكل من لحم هديهِ وَحَسَّامِنَ الْمِرْقَةِ ترجمہ تخلی اور نیکی بدی ، میری تمتع اور بیدی قرآن میں سے خود کھانا جائز ہے کیونکہ یہ نسک کا دم ہے تو الضحیہ کی طرح ان میں سے کیا ہوا ہے۔ اور یہ میچ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی اور ایسے ہی مستحب ہے اس طریقہ پر صدقہ کرنا جو ضحایا میں معلوم ہو چکا ہے۔ اور جو باقی ہدی ہیں ان میں سے کھانا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ کفارے کی قربانیاں ہیں ۔ اور صحیح طور پر ثابت ہے کہ جب حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم حدیبیہ میں محصر ہوئے اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ہدایا کو ناجیبہ اسلمی کے ہاتھوں بھیجا تو ناجی سے فرمایا کہ ان میں سے کچھ مت کھا ئیو اور نہ تیرے ساتھی اس میں سے کچھ کھا ئیں ۔ تشریح مسئلہ، مذکورہ ہدایا یعنی نفلی ہدی ۔ ہدی تمتع اور ہدی قرآن میں سے خود کھانا مستحب ہے۔ جیسا کہ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اپنے ہدی کا گوشت بھی کھایا اور اس کا شور با بھی پیا اور ہدایا کو نا جید اسلمی کے ہاتھوں بھیجا تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ناجیہ سے فرمایا کہ آنمیں سے نہ تم کھانا اور نہ تمہارے رفقاء کھائیں ان کو کھانے سے اس لئے منع کیا کہ یہ سب مالدار تھے۔ اس سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دم احصار وغیرہ جو کفارات اور جنایات کی قربانیاں ہیں وہ سب فقراء کا حق ہے اس میں سے نہ خود کو کھانا جائز ہے اور نہ مالداروں کو کھلا نا جائز ہے۔
And it is permissible to eat from Hadi of voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran, because it is the blood of a ritual [sacrifice], so it is permissible to eat from it like Udhiya. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet ate from the meat of his Hadi and drank from its broth. And it is recommended for him to eat from it due to what we have narrated, and likewise it is recommended to give charity in the manner known in Udhiya. And it is not permissible to eat from the rest of the Hadi because they are blood of expiations. And it is authentically reported that when the Prophet was prevented (ihsar) at Hudaybiyyah and sent the Hadi with Najiya al-Aslami, he said to him, 'Do not eat from it, you and your companions, anything.'
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage combines two rulings with proofs. First, it is permissible to eat from three types of Hadi: voluntary Hadi, Hadi of Tamattu', and Hadi of Qiran. The proof is that these are ritual sacrifices (nusuk) like Udhiya, and the Prophet himself ate from his Hadi and drank its broth. Moreover, it is recommended (mustahab) to eat from them and also to give charity in thirds (one-third eat, one-third gift, one-third charity). Second, it is not permissible to eat from any other type of Hadi, which are those of expiation (kafarat) and penalties (jinayat). These are solely the right of the poor of the Haram. The proof is the hadith of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet forbade Najiya and his companions from eating the Hadi because they were wealthy. This indicates that expiatory Hadi are only for the poor, and neither the offerer nor the wealthy may eat from them.

Key Terms
دم نُسُك (dam nusuk): Blood of a ritual sacrifice, i.e., an animal offered as an act of worship in Hajj.
دم كفارات (dam kafarat): Blood of expiation, i.e., sacrifice offered to compensate for violations or omissions in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on eating from a Hadi offered for Tamattu'?
A) Prohibited
B) Permissible and recommended
C) Only for the wealthy
D) Only if the pilgrim is poor

Key Takeaway
Only voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran Hadi may be eaten by the offerer; expiatory Hadi are exclusively for the poor of the Haram.

Time for Slaughtering Hadi: Voluntary vs. Tamattu'/Qiran
Details the time for slaughtering different types of Hadi: voluntary may be before, but Tamattu'/Qiran only on Yawm al-Nahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for slaughtering voluntary Hadi versus Tamattu'/Qiran Hadi with respect to Yawm al-Nahr, and explain the proof from the Quran and the distinction based on the nature of worship.

Core Idea
Voluntary Hadi may be slaughtered before Yawm al-Nahr because the act of sending to the Haram suffices; Tamattu'/Qiran Hadi is wajib on Yawm al-Nahr.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in the Hanafi school regarding the slaughter of Hadi (sacrificial animals) during Hajj. While a general rule states that Hadi is only sacrificed on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah), a detailed analysis reveals that voluntary Hadi (nadhr or tatabbu') has a more flexible timing. We will explore the textual proof from the Quran and the Hanafi legal reasoning that leads to the correct view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling
The matn states that slaughter of voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran Hadi is not permissible except on Yawm al-Nahr. This is the starting point.
This appears to be a general rule.
2
Locate the exception for voluntary Hadi
The author cites al-Asl (Imam Muhammad) which allows slaughter of voluntary Hadi before Yawm al-Nahr. This is declared the correct view (sahih).
The exception is based on the nature of voluntary worship.
3
Understand the rationale for the exception
For voluntary Hadi, the worship (qurbah) is realized by conveying the animal to the Haram, not solely by the act of slaughter on a specific day. Therefore, slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr is valid.
The act of bringing the animal to the Haram is itself an act of devotion.
4
Examine the proof for Tamattu'/Qiran restriction
The Quranic verse (22:28-29) commands eating from the sacrifice and then accomplishing tafath (purification rites), which is specific to Yawm al-Nahr. Additionally, these types of Hadi are analogous to Udhiya (sacrifice of Eid), which must be on that day.
The dalil is both textual (Quran) and analogical (qiyas).
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The correct Hanafi position is: voluntary Hadi may be slaughtered before Yawm al-Nahr (though better on the day), while Tamattu'/Qiran Hadi must be slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہدی تطوع تمتع اور قران کو یوم انحر میں ہی ذبح کیا جائے وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ هَدى التطوع وَالْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ قَالَ وَ فِي الْأَصْلِ يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ دَمِ التَطَوُّع قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَدَبَّحَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ اَفْضَلَّ وَهذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّ الْقُرْبَةَ فِى التَّطَوُّعَاتِ بِاعْتِبَارٍ أَنَّهَا هَدَايَا وَذَلِكَ يَتَحَقَّقُ بِتَبْلِيغِهَا إِلَى الْحَرمِ فَإِذَا وُجِدَ ذَلِكَ جَازَ ذَبْحُهَا فِي غَيْرِ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَ فِي أَيَّامِ النَّحْرِ أَفْضَلُ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى الْقُرْبَةِ فِى إِرَاقَةِ الدَّمِ فِيهَا أظْهَرُ أمَّادَمُ الْمُتَعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ فَلِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأطِعُمُوا البَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ ثُمَّ لِيَقْضُوا تَفَتَهُمْ وَقَضَاءُ التَّفَثِ يَخْتَصُّ بَيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَلأَنَّهُ دَمُ نَسُكِ فَيُخْتَصُّ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ كَالْأَضْحِيَّةِ
And it is not permissible to slaughter the Hadi of voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran except on Yawm al-Nahr. He said: And in al-Asl it is permissible to slaughter the blood of voluntary before Yawm al-Nahr, and slaughter on Yawm al-Nahr is better, and this is the correct view, because the worship in voluntary acts is by virtue of them being Hadi, and that is realized by conveying them to the Haram. So when that is found, it is permissible to slaughter them on other than Yawm al-Nahr, and in the days of al-Nahr it is better because the meaning of worship in shedding blood is more apparent in them. As for the blood of Tamattu' and Qiran, due to His saying: 'Then eat from them and feed the distressed poor, then let them accomplish their rites of purification' (Quran 22:28-29), and the accomplishment of purification is specific to Yawm al-Nahr, and because it is the blood of a ritual sacrifice, so it is specific to Yawm al-Nahr like Udhiya.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with a nuance. The initial statement says that slaughter of voluntary Hadi, Hadi of Tamattu', and Hadi of Qiran is not permissible except on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah). However, a more detailed view is then given: for voluntary Hadi, it is permissible to slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr as long as the animal has been conveyed to the Haram, because the essence of worship in voluntary Hadi is in sending it to the Haram. But slaughter on Yawm al-Nahr is better because the act of slaughter itself is more manifestly an act of worship. For Hadi of Tamattu' and Qiran, it must be on Yawm al-Nahr. The proof is the Quranic verse that links eating from the sacrifice and then accomplishing the rites of purification (tafath), which includes shaving and trimming nails, and this is specific to Yawm al-Nahr. Additionally, it is analogized to Udhiya, which is also specific to Yawm al-Nahr.

Key Terms
يوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice in Hajj.
تفث (tafath): The rites of purification after sacrifice, including shaving the head and trimming nails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only on Yawm al-Nahr
B) Before Yawm al-Nahr and on Yawm al-Nahr
C) Only on the day of Arafah
D) Any time in Hajj

Key Takeaway
Voluntary Hadi may be slaughtered before Yawm al-Nahr because the act of sending to the Haram suffices; Tamattu'/Qiran Hadi must be on Yawm al-Nahr due to explicit Quranic command and analogy to Udhiya.

Eating from Hadi: Voluntary vs. Expiatory
Ruling on eating from hadi with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating from hadi, distinguishing between voluntary and expiatory types, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Eating from the hadi is recommended only for voluntary offerings; expiatory hadi are exclusively for the poor.

This lesson examines a concise but important ruling from the Hanafi school on the permissibility of consuming the meat of sacrificial animals (hady) during Hajj. The key distinction lies in the purpose of the offering: voluntary (tatawwu') versus expiatory (kafarah). The ruling is supported by a clear prophetic directive that establishes a principle of exclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which act is being ruled upon (eating from the hadi) and for which categories. Note that the ruling varies based on the type of hadi.
Voluntary hadi: mustahabb; expiatory hadi: not permissible (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: the hadith of Najiyah al-Aslami at Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet forbade eating from the hadi of ihsar.
The hadith is the primary evidence for excluding expiatory hadi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the prohibition in the hadith specifically applies to expiatory hadi and why the Hanafi school restricts it to such cases.
The explicit prohibition (الناهي) indicates that eating from expiatory hadi is not permissible, as opposed to voluntary hadi.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing school: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that eating from all hadi is permissible, citing the general command 'And eat from them'.
The dispute centers on whether the general verse is restricted by the specific hadith.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi position is mufta bihi: the hadith specifies the Prophet's action for expiatory hadi, and the general verse is understood with this exception.
The principle of 'al-khass yuqaddam 'ala al-'amm' is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْتَحِبُّ لَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلَ مِنْهَا لِمَا رَوَيْنَا وَكَذَا يَسْتَحِبُّ أَنْ يَتَصَدَّقَ عَلَى الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي عُرِفَ فِي الصَّحَايَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ الأكُلُ مِنْ بَقِيَّةِ الْهَدَايَا لأَنَّهَا مَاءُ كَفَارَاتِ وَ قَدْ صَحٌ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَمَّا أَحْصِرَ بِالْحَدِيبِيَّةِ وَبَعَثَ الْهَدَايَا عَلى يَدَى نَاجِيَةِ الْأَسْلِمّى قَالَ لَهُ لَا تَأكُلُ أنْتَ وَرَفَقَتُكَ مِنْهَا شَيًّا
It is recommended for him to eat from them (the hadi) due to what we narrated. Likewise, it is recommended to give charity in the manner known for sacrificial animals (udhiyah). And it is not permissible to eat from the rest of the hadi because they are blood of expiations. And it is authentically established that the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he was prevented (blockaded) at al-Hudaybiyyah and sent the hadi with Najiyah al-Aslami, said to him: 'Neither you nor your companions should eat anything from them.'
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the permissibility of eating from the sacrificial animals (hady) brought for Hajj. The ruling distinguishes between two categories: first, the voluntary hadi (tatawwu'), including the hadi of tamattu' and qiran; second, the penalty/expiation hadi (dimā' al-kafārāt). For the first category, it is mustahabb (recommended) for the pilgrim to eat from the meat, following the practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) who ate from his own hadi. It is also recommended to give a portion in charity, following the same method as for udhiyah (sacrificial animals on Eid al-Adha): one-third for consumption, one-third for gifts, and one-third for storage. For the second category—any hadi that is offered as an expiation for an offense (such as dam al-ihsār, dam al-jināyāt, etc.)—it is not permissible for the pilgrim to eat at all, because these are solely for expiation purposes and belong to the poor of the Haram. The proof is the authentic hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) at Hudaybiyyah, where he sent the hadi for expiation due to being prevented from entering Makkah, and he ordered Najiyah and his companions not to eat from it. The text also notes that the companions were wealthy, indicating that the meat of expiatory hadi is exclusively for the poor.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): The animal sent to the Haram as a sacrificial offering; can be voluntary or wajib due to ihsār, tamattu', qiran, or jināyah.
مستحب (mustahabb): An action that is recommended but not obligatory; reward for doing, no sin for leaving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of hadi is it permissible for the pilgrim to eat from?
A) Dam al-ihsar (penalty for being prevented from completing Hajj)
B) Hadi al-tatawwu' (voluntary)
C) Dam al-jinayah (penalty for a hunting violation)
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Eating from the hadi is mustahabb only for voluntary offerings; expiatory hadi are exclusively for the poor and the pilgrim must not eat from them.

Timing of Slaughter for Voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran Hadi
Ruling on timing of slaughter for different hadi types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling on the timing of slaughter for voluntary hadi versus tamattu' and qiran hadi, and state the evidence from Quran, qiyas, and Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Voluntary hadi may be slaughtered before Yawm al-Nahr; obligatory hadi (tamattu', qiran) only on it.

This lesson clarifies a subtle but important distinction: while the matn of al-Quduri appears to restrict all three types of hadi to Yawm al-Nahr, the Hanafi school, relying on Imam Muhammad's al-Asl, permits voluntary hadi (dam al-tatawwu') to be slaughtered earlier. The reasoning is that voluntary hadi is a gift to the Haram, realized by delivery, whereas tamattu' and qiran hadi are ritual sacrifices (dam nusuk) tied to the completion of Hajj rites, analogous to udhiyah. Understanding this difference is essential for correct practice and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of hadi
The passage mentions three types: voluntary (tatawwu'), tamattu', and qiran. Note their different legal natures: voluntary is supererogatory, tamattu'/qiran are obligatory for those performing Hajj tamattu' or qiran.
2
Recognize the matn's blanket ruling and its exception
The text states that according to Quduri, none of these may be slaughtered except on Yawm al-Nahr. But the commentator immediately cites al-Asl, which permits voluntary before that day. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved in favor of al-Asl.
The commentator declares this the sahih (correct) position.
3
Understand the rationale for voluntary hadi
The nearness (qurbah) in voluntary acts is achieved by delivering the animal to the Haram. Once delivered, it becomes a valid hadi and can be slaughtered any time. Slaughter on Yawm al-Nahr is more virtuous because spilling blood on that day is more apparent in worship.
The key distinction: voluntary hadi is essentially a gift (hadiya) to the Haram.
4
Analyze the proof for tamattu' and qiran
First, the Quranic verse (al-Hajj 22:29) linking the slaughter to the completion of rites (qada' al-tafath), which occurs on Yawm al-Nahr. Second, qiyas: tamattu'/qiran hadi is dam nusuk (ritual blood) like udhiyah, which is restricted to the days of Nahr.
The completion of rites (shaving/trimming) is specific to Yawm al-Nahr by ijma'.
5
Synthesize the practical rule
Voluntary hadi: permissible before Yawm al-Nahr, better on it. Tamattu' and qiran hadi: must be on Yawm al-Nahr. If delayed, they must be made up.
This is the mufta bihi (operative position for fatwa).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ هَدى التطوع وَالْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ قَالَ وَ فِي الْأَصْلِ يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ دَمِ التَطَوُّع قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَدَبَّحَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ اَفْضَلَّ وَهذَا هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ لِأَنَّ الْقُرْبَةَ فِى التَّطَوُّعَاتِ بِاعْتِبَارٍ أَنَّهَا هَدَايَا وَذَلِكَ يَتَحَقَّقُ بِتَبْلِيغِهَا إِلَى الْحَرمِ فَإِذَا وُجِدَ ذَلِكَ جَازَ ذَبْحُهَا فِي غَيْرِ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَ فِي أَيَّامِ النَّحْرِ أَفْضَلُ لِأَنَّ مَعْنَى الْقُرْبَةِ فِى إِرَاقَةِ الدَّمِ فِيهَا أظْهَرُ أمَّادَمُ الْمُتَعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ فَلِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَكُلُوا مِنْهَا وَأطِعُمُوا البَائِسَ الْفَقِيرَ ثُمَّ لِيَقْضُوا تَفَتَهُمْ وَقَضَاءُ التَّفَثِ يَخْتَصُّ بَيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَلأَنَّهُ دَمُ نَسُكِ فَيُخْتَصُّ بَيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ كَالْأَضْحِيَّةِ
It is not permissible to slaughter the hadi of voluntary (tatawwu'), tamattu', and qiran except on the Day of Nahr. He (al-Quduri) said: And in al-Asl, it is permissible to slaughter the blood of voluntary before the Day of Nahr, and slaughter on the Day of Nahr is better. And this is the correct (opinion) because the nearness (to Allah) in voluntary acts is considered by their being hadi, and that is realized by delivering them to the Haram. So when that is achieved, it is permissible to slaughter them on other than the Day of Nahr, and on the Days of Nahr it is better because the meaning of nearness in spilling blood is more apparent therein. As for the blood of tamattu' and qiran, (the restriction is) due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'Then eat from them and feed the poor and needy. Then let them complete their rites.' And the completion of rites (qada' al-tafath) is specific to the Day of Nahr. And because it is the blood of a ritual (dam nusuk), so it is specific to the Day of Nahr just like the udhiyah.
Source pages p. 529

Commentary
This passage discusses the timing for slaughtering different types of hadi. The main text (matn) states that none of these three types can be slaughtered except on Yawm al-Nahr (10th of Dhul Hijjah). However, the commentator immediately cites a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Asl, which is part of the Zahir al-Riwayah, allowing the voluntary hadi (tatawwu') to be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr. The reasoning is that the sacrificial act (qurbah) for voluntary hadi is achieved simply by delivering the animal to the Haram. Once it reaches the Haram, it becomes a valid hadi and can be slaughtered at any time. Nevertheless, slaughtering on the Day of Nahr or the days of Tashriq is more virtuous because spilling the blood in those days has a clearer element of worship. As for the hadi of tamattu' and qiran, they are strictly confined to the Day of Nahr. The proof is the verse 'Then let them complete their rites' (al-Hajj 22:28-29), and the completion of rites (halq or taqsir) is performed on Yawm al-Nahr. Additionally, these are ritual sacrifices (dam nusuk) similar to udhiyah, which can only be slaughtered on the specified days. Thus, the correct Hanafi position is that voluntary hadi may be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr with permission, while tamattu' and qiran hadi are restricted to the Day of Nahr.

Key Terms
دم التطوع (dam al-tatawwu'): Voluntary hadi, offered as an act of devotion.
دم المتعة والقران (dam al-mut'ah wa al-qiran): The obligatory hadi for those performing Hajj tamattu' or qiran.
قضاء التفث (qada' al-tafath): Completion of personal grooming rites (shaving, trimming) after Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position, when may the voluntary hadi (dam al-tatawwu') be slaughtered?
A) Only on Yaum al-Nahr
B) Before Yaum al-Nahr but better on it
C) Only on the 12th of Dhul Hijjah
D) Any day of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes voluntary hadi (flexible timing) from obligatory hadi (fixed to Yawm al-Nahr) based on the nature of the act: voluntary is a gift to the Haram, obligatory is a ritual sacrifice tied to the completion of Hajj.

intermediate
6 min
Timing of Slaughter for Penalty Hadi: Any Time Permissible
Inter-madhhab dispute on timing for expiatory hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the timing of expiatory hadi slaughter and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Expiatory hadi is a kafara, not a ritual slaughter—so it must be prompt, not tied to the Day of Nahr.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding when the penalty bloods (dimā' al-kafārāt) in Hajj must be slaughtered. While Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes them to the hadi of tamattu' and qiran, restricting their time to the Day of Nahr, the Hanafi school distinguishes them based on their legal nature: they are expiations (kafārāt) for a deficiency, and thus promptness—not a specific date—is the governing principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is slaughtering the 'rest of the hadi' (baqiyyat al-hadaya), i.e., expiatory bloods. The dispute: can they be slaughtered at any time (Hanafi) or only on Yawm al-Nahr (Shafi'i)?
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds it is only permissible on Yawm al-Nahr. His proof is qiyas (analogy) to the hadi of tamattu' and qiran, arguing they are all 'dam jabr' (blood for reparation).
Dam jabr is the common term in Shafi'i school for these bloods.
3
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds it is permissible at any time. Their proof: these are 'dimā' kafārāt' (expiatory bloods) required to repair a deficiency, so promptness (ta'jil) is the objective, not a set date.
The key term is kafara, which implies immediate rectification.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal of the qiyas
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy: tamattu' and qiran bloods are 'dam nusuk' (ritual blood) connected to the festival, like udhiyah, whereas expiatory bloods are kafārāt. Since the underlying cause differs, the qiyas does not hold.
This is an example of fasid al-i'tibar (invalid analogy) due to difference in illa.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: According to Hanafi, one can slaughter expiatory hadi any time, even before Yawm al-Nahr or later. According to Shafi'i, if slaughtered outside the Days of Nahr (10-13 Dhul Hijjah), it is not valid and must be repeated.
This difference can affect pilgrims who commit violations early or late in Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ بَقِيَّةِ الْهَدَايَا فِي أَي وَقَت شَاءَ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ اعْتِبَارًا بِدَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَان فَإِنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ دَمُ جَبَرٍ عِندَهُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ هَذِهِ دِمَاءُ كَفَّارَاتِ فَلا يَخْتَصُّ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ لأنها لما وَجَبَتْ لِجَبر النُّقْصَانَ كَانَ التَّعْجِيْلُ بِهَا أَوْلَى لِارْتِفَاعِ النُّقْصَانِ بِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَأخِيرِ بِخَلافِ دَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ لِأَنَّهُ دَمُ نُسُكِ
It is permissible to slaughter the rest of the hadi (i.e., the penalty blood) at any time he wishes. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible except on the Day of Nahr, drawing an analogy to the blood of tamattu' and qiran, for each one of them is, in his view, blood of reparation (dam jabr). And our (Hanafi) evidence is that these are blood of expiations (dimā' kafārāt), so they are not specific to the Day of Nahr, because when they became obligatory for repairing a deficiency, hastening with them is better for the removal of the deficiency without delay, unlike the blood of tamattu' and qiran because that blood is a ritual blood (dam nusuk).
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the timing of slaughter for the 'remaining hadi' (baqiyyat al-hadaya) — these are the expiatory bloods (dimā' al-kafārāt) such as dam al-ihsar (penalty for being prevented from completing Hajj), dam al-jinayah (penalty for hunting violations), dam al-fawt (penalty for missing Hajj), etc. The Hanafi position is that these can be slaughtered at any time, not restricted to the Day of Nahr. Imam al-Shafi'i, on the other hand, analogizes these to the hadi of tamattu' and qiran, arguing that they are all 'dam jabr' (blood for reparation/compensation) and therefore should be restricted to the Day of Nahr. The Hanafi response is based on the nature of these bloods: they are expiations (kafārāt) that became obligatory to repair a deficiency in the Hajj. Since their purpose is to remove a deficiency, it is more appropriate to perform them promptly without waiting for a specific day, because delay contradicts the goal of removing the deficiency. In contrast, tamattu' and qiran bloods are ritual slaughter (dam nusuk) connected to the festival, so they are restricted to the Day of Nahr, similar to udhiyah. This is a clear distinction based on the underlying rationale (ta'lil).

Key Terms
بقية الهدايا (baqiyyat al-hadaya): The hadi other than voluntary, tamattu', and qiran, i.e., expiatory bloods.
دم جبر (dam jabr): Blood for reparation; Shafi'i's term for tamattu'/qiran and penalty hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can the expiatory hadi (e.g., dam al-ihsar) be slaughtered?
A) Only on Yawm al-Nahr
B) At any time
C) Only after the end of Dhul Hijjah
D) Only on the Day of Tamyeez

Key Takeaway
Expiatory hadi can be slaughtered at any time because it is a kafara, not a ritual blood tied to Yawm al-Nahr.

Location of Hadi Slaughter and Meat Distribution
Ruling on location for slaughtering all hadi and distribution of meat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the location of hadi slaughter and explain why distribution of meat is not restricted to the Haram, contrasting with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
All hadi must be slaughtered inside the Haram, but the meat may be given to any poor person outside.

In this passage, al-Quduri establishes a foundational rule for sacrifice during Hajj and Umrah: every hadi, whether obligatory or voluntary, must be slaughtered within the sacred precincts of Makkah. He then addresses a practical dispute: may the meat be sent outside the Haram? The Hanafi school permits it, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling and its basis
The Hanafi school rules that all hadi must be slaughtered within the Haram. The proof is from Quran 5:95 and the hadith that all of Mina is a slaughter place.
The verse 'hadyan baligh al-ka'bah' is interpreted to mean reaching the Haram.
2
Locate the disputed subsidiary issue
The disagreement is about distribution of meat: Hanafi allows giving to any poor, Shafi'i restricts to poor of the Haram.
This is the ikhtilaf highlighted in the text.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the hadi is specifically for the poor of the Haram, based on the verse indicating the meat should reach the Ka'bah area.
The opponent's dalil is textual but interpreted differently.
4
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is that delivery to the Haram is fulfilled by slaughtering there; after that, charity is a general act of worship valid to any poor person.
The Hanafi position separates location of sacrifice from distribution of meat.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis can send meat to family outside Makkah, while Shafi'is must consume or distribute it within the Haram.
This practical difference matters for pilgrims who wish to benefit relatives abroad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ الْهَدَايَا إِلَّا فِى الْحَرَمِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فِي جَزَاءِ الصَّيْدِ هَدْيَا بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ فَصَارَ أَصْلَا فِي كُلِّ دَم هُوَ كَفَارَةٌ وَلَانَّ الْهَدَى اِسْمٌ لِمَا يُهُدَى إِلَى مَكَان وَمَكَانُهُ الْحَرَمُ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مِنى كُلُّهَا مَنْحَرٌ وَ فِجَاج هكَةٌ كُلُّهَا مَنْحَرٌ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَتَصَدَّقَ بِهَا عَلَى مَسَاكِينِ الحَرَمِ وَغَيْرِهِمْ خِلَافًا لِشَافِعِى لِأَنَّ الصَّدَقَةَ قُرُبَةٌ مَعْقُوَلَةٌ وَالصَّدَقَةُ عَلَى كُلَّ فَقِيْرٍ قُرْبَةٌ
He (al-Quduri) said: It is not permissible to slaughter the hadi except in the Haram due to the saying of Allah the Exalted regarding the penalty of hunting: 'a hadi reaching the Ka'bah'. Thus, this became a principle for every blood that is an expiation. And because 'hadi' is a name for something that is sent to a place, and its place is the Haram. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'All of Mina is a slaughter place, and the mountain passes of Makkah are all a slaughter place.' And it is permissible to give charity from it to the poor of the Haram and others, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because charity is an understood act of worship, and giving charity to every poor person is an act of worship.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage establishes the requirement that all hadi, whether voluntary or obligatory, must be slaughtered within the Haram boundaries (the sacred precincts of Makkah). The primary proof is from the Quranic verse regarding the penalty for hunting: 'a hadi reaching the Ka'bah' (Quran 5:95). The word 'Ka'bah' here refers to the Haram in general, not the literal Ka'bah building. This verse becomes the foundational principle for all types of blood that are offered as expiation. Additionally, the linguistic meaning of 'hadi' — something sent to a specific place — indicates that the intended destination is the Haram. The Prophet (ﷺ) confirmed that all of Mina and the mountain roads of Makkah are valid slaughter locations. This ruling applies to all hadi, including voluntary. The passage then addresses a subsidiary issue: whether the meat of hadi can be given in charity to poor people outside the Haram. The Hanafi position allows it, because charity is a recognized act of worship regardless of location, and any poor person is a valid recipient. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, restricts the meat to the poor of the Haram. The Hanafi view is that since the hadi has been delivered to the Haram (by slaughtering it there), the condition is fulfilled, and the meat may be distributed elsewhere. The underlying principle is that the obligation is to bring the hadi to the Haram, not to confine its consumption there.

Key Terms
الحرم (al-Haram): The sacred territory of Makkah, within which all hadi must be slaughtered.
منحر (manhar): Place of slaughter; specifically, any place where it is permissible to slaughter hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only at the Ka'bah
B) Anywhere in the Haram including Mina
C) Only at Mina
D) Anywhere in the world

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires all hadi to be slaughtered within the Haram but allows the meat to be given in charity to any poor person, regardless of location.

Slaughtering Expiatory Hadaya: Any Time?
Dispute on timing of expiatory hadaya slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits slaughtering expiatory hadaya at any time and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on analogy.

Core Idea
Expiatory blood is due for a deficiency; prompt removal is better, so no fixed time.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the timing of slaughtering hadaya that are not for tamattu' or qiran. Abu Hanifa and his school hold that such hadaya, being expiatory (kaffarat), may be sacrificed at any time, while Imam Shafi'i restricts them to the Day of Nahr by analogy with ritual sacrifices. The difference hinges on the nature of the blood and the effective cause ('illa). By understanding the Hanafi response, you will see how the school contrasts expiatory and ritual blood to reject a superficial analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi position (any time) and the Shafi'i position (only on the Day of Nahr).
2
Understand the Shafi'i proof
Shafi'i uses qiyas: the blood of tamattu' and qiran are dam jabar (reparation) and are restricted to the Day of Nahr; thus all dam jabar should be restricted.
3
Examine the Hanafi distinction
Hanafis respond that expiatory blood (kaffarat) is not ritual blood (dam nusk). The 'illa differs: kaffarat are due for a deficiency, so promptness is better; tamattu' and qiran blood are part of the hajj rites.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi allows slaughter at any time, even before the Day of Nahr; Shafi'i only on the Day of Nahr.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to the strength of the meaning-based distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ بَقِيَّةِ الْهَدَايَا فِي أَي وَقَت شَاءَ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِي لَا يَجُوزُ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ اعْتِبَارًا بِدَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَان فَإِنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ دَمُ جَبَرٍ عِندَهُ وَلَنَا أَنَّ هَذِهِ دِمَاءُ كَفَّارَاتِ فَلا يَخْتَصُّ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ لأنها لما وَجَبَتْ لِجَبر النُّقْصَانَ كَانَ التَّعْجِيْلُ بِهَا أَوْلَى لِارْتِفَاعِ النُّقْصَانِ بِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَأخِيرِ بِخَلافِ دَمِ الْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ لِأَنَّهُ دَمُ نُسُكِ
And it is permissible to slaughter the rest of the hadaya at any time he wishes. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible except on the Day of Nahr, by analogy with the blood of tamattu' and qiran, for each one, according to him, is blood of reparation. And our proof is that these are expiatory blood, so they are not restricted to the Day of Nahr, because when they become obligatory for repairing a deficiency, hastening with them is better to remove the deficiency without delay, contrary to the blood of tamattu' and qiran, because it is blood of a ritual.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and al-Shafi'i regarding the time for slaughtering hadaya that are not from tamattu' or qiran. The ruling states that such hadaya (e.g., for kaffarat) may be slaughtered at any time. Imam Shafi'i restricts slaughter to the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), drawing an analogy with the blood of tamattu' and qiran, which he considers to be blood for repairing a deficiency (dam jabar). The Hanafi response distinguishes: expiatory blood (dimā' al-kaffārāt) is due for a deficiency, so promptness in slaughtering is preferable to remove the deficiency quickly. In contrast, the blood of tamattu' and qiran is a ritual sacrifice (dam nusk), which is linked to the specific time of the Day of Nahr. Thus, the 'illa (effective cause) differs, and the analogy fails. The Hanafis prioritize the meaning (ma'nā) over a superficial analogy.

Key Terms
بقية الهدايا (baqiyyat al-hadaya): Hadaya other than those for tamattu' and qiran, such as expiatory offerings (kaffarat).
دم كفارات (dam kaffarat): Blood (sacrificial animal) due as expiation for sins or omissions.
دم نُسُك (dam nusk): Blood of a ritual sacrifice, specifically for tamattu' and qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only on the Day of Nahr
B) At any time
C) Within the three days after Nahr
D) Only before the Day of Nahr

Key Takeaway
Expiatory hadaya may be slaughtered anytime because they remedy a deficiency; ritual hadaya of tamattu' and qiran are fixed to the Day of Nahr.

Ruling on Ta'rif (Publicizing) of Hadaya
Ruling on ta'rif of hadaya with reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ta'rif of hadaya and distinguish between when ta'rif is recommended and when it is not, based on the type of hady.

Core Idea
Ta'rif of hadaya is not obligatory; it is only recommended for ritual sacrifices like tamattu' and qiran, not for expiatory offerings.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, the author clarifies the legal status of ta'rif (publicizing or bringing to 'Arafat) for sacrificial animals (hadaya). The key is to understand that the essence of hady is the transfer to the Haram and the shedding of blood, not public announcement. Hence ta'rif is not an obligation. However, for certain hadya tied to specific rituals, ta'rif becomes recommended to ensure the animal is properly managed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is ta'rif (publicizing or bringing to 'Arafat) of hadaya. The author states directly: 'wa la yajibu al-ta'rif' — it is not obligatory.
The ruling is explicitly negative: no obligation.
2
Understand the linguistic reasoning (talil)
The word 'hady' itself indicates transfer to a place for nearness through bloodshed, not about publicity. Thus, the essence of hady does not require ta'rif.
Hanafi usul: the meaning of the word itself guides the ruling.
3
Identify the exception for tamattu'
The author says: 'fa-in 'arrafa bi-hady al-mut'ati fa-hasan' — if one performs ta'rif for the hady of tamattu', it is good (recommended).
The exception is based on practical need: the sacrifice is fixed to the Day of Nahr, and without ta'rif the animal might be lost.
4
Contrast with expiatory blood (dimā' al-kaffārāt)
Expiatory hady is different: it can be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr, and its cause is a sin (jinayah) which should be concealed (satr). Hence ta'rif is not recommended for these.
The rationale is based on the nature of the sacrifice: ritual vs. expiatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَجبُ التَّعْريفُ بِالْهَدَايَا لأنَّ الهَدَى يُنبِئُ عَنِ النَّقْلِ إِلى مَكَان لِيَتَقَرَّبَ بِارَاقَةِ دَم فِيْهِ لَا عَنِ التَّعْرِيْفِ فَلا يَجبُ فَإِن عَرَّفَ بِهَدَى الْمُتْعَةِ فَحَسَنٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَتَوَقَّتُ بِيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَعَسَى لَا يَجِدُ مَنْ يُمْسِكُهُ فَيَحْتَاجُ إلى أن يُعَرَّفَ بِهِ وَلِأَنَّهُ دَمُ نُسُكٍ فَيَكُونُ مَبْنَاهُ عَلَى التَّشْهِيْرِ بِخِلافِ دِمَاءِ الْكَفَّارَاتِ لِأَنَّهُ يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُهَا قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَ سَبَبُهُ الْجِنَايَةُ فَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ السَّتْرُ
He said: And ta'rif (publicizing) of the hadaya is not obligatory, because 'hady' indicates transfer to a place to draw near by shedding blood therein, not about ta'rif, so it is not obligatory. If he does ta'rif for the hady of tamattu', then it is good, because it is restricted to the Day of Nahr, and perhaps he will not find someone to hold it, so he needs to do ta'rif with it. And because it is blood of a ritual, so its basis is on publicity, contrary to expiatory blood, because it is permissible to slaughter them before the Day of Nahr as we mentioned, and its cause is a transgression, so concealment is appropriate for it.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage defines and rules on ta'rif (making known or publicizing) of hadaya. The word 'hady' etymologically means something sent to a place (the Haram) for sacrifice, not a public announcement. Therefore, ta'rif is not obligatory. However, for the hady of tamattu' (and by extension qiran), ta'rif is recommended (hasan). The reason is that its slaughter is fixed to the Day of Nahr, so it may be difficult to find someone to tend the animal until that day; bringing it to 'Arafat (ta'rif in the sense of taking to 'Arafat) ensures it is available. Also, since it is a ritual sacrifice (dam nusk), it is based on publicity (tashhir). Expiatory blood (dimā' al-kaffārāt) is different: it can be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr, and its cause is a sin (jinayah) which should be concealed (satr). Thus, the obligation of ta'rif does not apply, but it is praiseworthy for the tamattu' hady. The commentary clarifies that ta'rif has two meanings: taking to 'Arafat or making publicly known (by putting a necklace or marking). Both are not obligatory, but recommended for nusk.

Key Terms
التَّعْريفُ (al-ta'rif): Making known; bringing the hady to 'Arafat or publicly marking it.
هَدْيُ التَّمَتْع (hady al-tamattu'): The sacrificial animal offered by a pilgrim performing tamattu' hajj.
دِمَاءُ الْكَفَّارَاتِ (dimā' al-kaffārāt): Blood (animals) offered as expiation for sins or omissions during hajj or otherwise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of hady is it recommended to perform ta'rif (publicizing) for?
A) Expiatory hady (kaffarat)
B) Hady of tamattu'
C) All types of hady
D) Hady of qiran only

Key Takeaway
Ta'rif of hadaya is not obligatory; it is only recommended for ritual sacrifices (tamattu' and qiran) due to their fixed time and public nature, but not for expiatory offerings which require concealment.

6 min
Definition of Hadaya is Not Obligatory
Ruling that marking hadaya is not wajib with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'rif of hadaya and explain the linguistic and textual proof for why it is not wajib.

Core Idea
The term 'hadi' means transfer to Haram, not marking; thus ta'rif is not wajib.

The Hidayah addresses a practical question: must the pilgrim mark or bring the sacrificial animal to 'Arafat? The clear Hanafi position is that this act, called ta'rif, is not an obligation. This lesson examines the linguistic and scriptural basis for this ruling, distinguishing between different types of hadaya.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Ta'rif (definition) of hadaya: the author states 'la yajibu' – it is not obligatory. Note that the act itself is not a condition for the validity of the sacrifice.
2
Locate the dalil
The main dalil is linguistic: the word 'hadi' means transferring an animal to the Haram to shed blood, not marking or taking to 'Arafat. No textual command for ta'rif exists.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Since the word 'hadi' does not imply ta'rif, and no Quranic verse or hadith mandates it, there is no basis for obligation. The absence of a command (nass) is the key.
4
Identify the recommendation for tamattu' and qiran
Despite the general non-obligation, the text says defining the hadi of tamattu' is 'hasan' (good). It gives two reasons: the fixed slaughter time (Day of Nahr) and the nature of a ritual sacrifice requiring publicity. This applies also to qiran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَلَا يَجبُ التَّعْريفُ بِالْهَدَايَا لأنَّ الهَدَى يُنبئُى عَنِ النَّقْلِ إِلى مَكَان لِيَتَقَرَّبَ بِارَاقَةِ دَم فِيْهِ لأَنَّ عَنِ التَّعْرِيْفِ فَلا يَجبُ فَإِن عَرَّفَ بِهَدَى الْمُتْعَةِ فَحَسَنٌ لِأَنَّهُ يَتَوَكَّتُ بيَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَعَسَى لَا يَجِدُ مَنْ يُمْسِكُهُ فَيَحْتَاجُ إلى أن يُعرف به ولأنَّهُ دَمُ نُسُكِ فَيَكُونُ مَبْنَاهُ عَلَى التَّشْهِيْرِ بِخِلافِ دِمَاءِ الْكَفَّارَاتِ لِأنَّهُ يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُهَا قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ عَلَى مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَ سَبهِ الْجِنَايَةُ فَيَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ السَّتُرُ
ترجمہ کہا اور ہدایا کی تعریف واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ فقط ہدی خبر دیتا ہے کسی مکان کی طرف منتقل کرنے کی ۔ تا کہ اس میں خون بہا کر تقرب حاصل کیا جائے نہ کہ تعریف سے ۔ پس تعریف واجب نہیں ہے۔ پھر اگر ہدی تمتع کو تعریف کیا تو اچھا ہے کیونکہ ہدی تمتع کا ذبح کرنا یوم نحر کے ساتھ مختص ہے۔ پس ممکن ہے کہ اس کو ایسا آدمی نہ ملے جو اس کو روکے رکھے۔ اس لئے اس کو عرفات میں لے جانے کی طرف محتاج ہوگا۔ اور اس لئے کہ ہدی تمتع تو نسک کی قربانی ہے پس وہ شہرت پر مبنی ہے۔ برخلاف کفارات کی قربانیوں کے۔ اس لئے کہ ان کا ذبح کرنا یوم نحر سے پہلے جائز ہے اس بنا پر جو ہم نے ذکر کیا اور اس کا سبب جنایت ہے اس لئے پوشیدگی اس کے مناسب ہے۔ تشریح تعریف کے دو معنی ہیں ایک عرفات میں لے جانے کے دوم قلادہ ڈال کر یا اشعار کر کے شہرت دینے کے۔ بہر حال دونوں معنی کے اعتبار سے ہدی کے جانوروں کی تعریف واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ہدی نام ہے حرم میں لے جانے کا تا کہ اس میں خون بہا کر تقرب حاصل کیا جائے تعریف کرنے کا نام ہدی نہیں ہے اس لئے تعریف واجب نہیں۔ حاصل یہ کہ تعریف کا وجوب دوطریقہ سے ثابت ہو سکتا تھا۔ ایک تو یہ کہ کوئی نص موجود ہو ۔ دوم یہ کہ لفظ ہدی سے تعریف کے معنی مفہوم ہوتے ہوں۔ اور یہاں دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں۔ اس لئے تعریف واجب نہ ہوگی۔ لیکن اگر ہدی تمتع یا ہدی قرآن کو تعریف کیا گیا تو اچھا ہے تعریف اگر عرفات میں لے جانے کے معنی میں ہے تو اچھا اس لئے ہے کہ ہدی کا ذبح کرنا یوم نحر کے ساتھ مختص ہے۔ پس ہو سکتا ہے کہ اس کو کوئی آدمی ایسا میسر نہ آئے جو ہدی کے جانور کو یوم نحر تک اپنے پاس رکھے۔ اور اس کی حفاظت کرے اس لئے اس بات کی ضرورت پڑے گی کہ وہ اس کو اپنے ساتھ عرفات میں لے جائے ۔ اور اگر تعریف بمعنی مشتہر کرنا ہے تو تعریف کے اچھا ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہدی تمتع نسک کی قربانی ہے اس لئے اس کی بنیاد تشہیر پر ہوگی تاکہ طاعات کو اعلان سے ادا کرنے میں لوگوں کو توفیق ہو۔ برخلاف کفارات کی قربانیوں کے کیونکہ ان میں دونوں و جہیں جاری نہیں ہیں۔ کیونکہ کفارات کی قربانیوں کو یوم نحر سے پہلے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے۔ پس جب کوئی ہدی کو رکھنے والا نہ ملے تو اس کو ذبح کرے عرفات میں ساتھ لے جانے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور چونکہ دم کفارہ کا سبب جرم ہے اس لئے پوشیدگی اس کے زیادہ مناسب ہوگی ۔ پس کفارات کی قربانیوں میں تعریف کسی معنی میں بہتر نہیں ہے۔
He said: And definition (ta'rif) is not obligatory for hadaya, because the word hadi only indicates transfer to a place to seek nearness by shedding blood therein, not definition. So definition is not obligatory. If one defines the hadi of tamattu', that is good, because its slaughter is restricted to the Day of Nahr, so he may not find someone to keep it, thus he needs to define it (by taking it to Arafat). And because it is a sacrificial blood (dam nusuk), its basis is publicity, unlike the blood of expiations (kaffarat), because their slaughter is permissible before the Day of Nahr as we mentioned, and their cause is a crime, so concealment relates to them.
Translation: He said: And definition of hadaya is not obligatory, because the word hadi only indicates transferring to a place so that by shedding blood therein one seeks nearness, not definition. So definition is not obligatory. Then if one defines the hadi of tamattu', it is good, because the slaughter of hadi tamattu' is specified for the Day of Nahr. So it is possible that he does not find a person to keep it; therefore he will need to take it to Arafat. And because hadi tamattu' is a sacrificial offering, its basis is on publicity, unlike the sacrifices of expiations, because their slaughter is permissible before the Day of Nahr according to what we mentioned, and their cause is a crime, so concealment is appropriate for them. Explanation: Ta'rif has two meanings: one is taking to Arafat, the second is giving fame by putting a necklace or marking (ish'ar). In any case, according to both meanings, definition of hadaya is not obligatory. Because hadi is a name for taking to the Haram to shed blood therein to seek nearness; definition is not the name of hadi. Therefore definition is not obligatory. The conclusion is that obligation of definition could be established in two ways: first, by a text (nass); second, by the word hadi implying the meaning of definition. Both are absent here, so definition is not obligatory. But if one defines the hadi of tamattu' or qiran, it is good. If definition is in the meaning of taking to Arafat, it is good because the slaughter of hadi is restricted to the Day of Nahr; so it is possible that he does not find a person who will keep the animal until that day, thus he will need to take it himself. And if definition is in the meaning of making famous, the reason for its goodness is that hadi tamattu' is a sacrifice of the ritual, so its basis is publicity so that people may be facilitated in performing acts of worship openly. Unlike the sacrifices of expiations, because both aspects are not applicable to them. Since expiatory sacrifices can be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr, there is no need to take them to Arafat if no one keeps them; and because the cause of expiation blood (dam kaffarah) is a crime, concealment is more appropriate. Therefore, in expiatory sacrifices, definition is not better in any sense.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Hidayah explaining that defining (ta'rif) hadaya—either by taking them to 'Arafat or by marking them publicly—is not obligatory (wajib). The author gives the reasoning: the term 'hadi' linguistically means transferring an animal to the Haram for sacrifice, not marking it. Therefore, no textual or linguistic basis establishes obligation. However, for the hadi of tamattu' or qiran, doing so is recommended (hasan) because its slaughter time is fixed to the Day of Nahr, and one may need to ensure the animal is available or make it known. This is contrasted with expiatory sacrifices (dam al-kaffarat), which can be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr and whose cause is a crime requiring concealment. Thus, definition is not recommended for them. The Hanafi position is clear: definition is not wajib, and its permissibility varies by type of hadi.

Key Terms
تعریف (ta'rif): Definition/marking of the hadi by taking it to 'Arafat or making it known (e.g., by placing a necklace or making a mark).
ہدی (hadi): Animal brought to the Haram for sacrifice to seek nearness to Allah, particularly in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which type of Hadi is definition (ta'rif) considered good (hasan) according to the Hanafi school?
A) All types of hadaya
B) Hadi tamattu' and hadi qiran
C) Only hadi ifrad
D) Hadi of expiations (kaffarat)

Key Takeaway
Ta'rif of hadaya is not wajib; it is mustahabb for tamattu' and qiran, but not for expiatory sacrifices.

Preferred Slaughter Methods: Nahr for Camels, Dhabh for Cows/Sheep
Ruling on preferred slaughter methods for camels vs. cows/sheep with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred method of slaughter (nahr vs. dhabh) for camels and for cows/sheep according to the Hanafi school, and explain the Quranic and prophetic evidence supporting each.

Core Idea
For camels, nahr while standing is afdal; for cows and sheep, dhabh while lying down is sunnah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the recommended method of sacrifice for different animals. While any valid method of slaughter produces halal meat, the Hanafi school distinguishes between camels and other livestock based on Quranic commands and Prophetic practice. Understanding this distinction ensures one follows the sunnah in worship and avoids makruh practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the preferred method for each animal
The text states that for camels (budun), the afdal is nahr; for cows (baqar) and sheep (ghanam), the afdal is dhabh.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence for each method
The verses: 'wa-nhar' (108:2) interpreted as referring to camels; 'an tadhbahu baqarah' (2:67) for cows; 'bi-dhibhin 'azim' (37:107) for the sacrifice.
3
Trace the Prophetic practice (Sunnah)
Authentic reports show the Prophet performed nahr on camels and dhabh on cows and sheep.
4
Understand the practical details
For camels, standing is best; for cows and sheep, lying down is best because the slaughter place is more visible, making the cut easier.
5
Note the ruling level
The text uses 'afdal' and 'sunnah', indicating it is a strongly recommended practice (sunnah muakkadah), not obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَالْأَفْضَلُ فِي الْبُدُنِ السَّحْرَ وَ فِى الْبَقَرِ وَالْغَيْمِ الذَّبْحُ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالى (فَصَلَّ الرَبِّكَ وَانْحَرُ) قِيلَ فِي تَأْوِيلِهِ الْجُزُور وَقَالَ اللهُ تعالى (أَنْ تَذْبَحُوا بَقَرَةً) وَقَالَ اللهُ تعالى (وَفَدَيْنَاهُ بِذِبْحٍ عَظِيمٍ وَالدَّبْحُ مَا أُعِدَّ لِلذَّبْحِ وَقَدْ صح أن النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَحْرَ الْإِبِلَ وَذَبَحَ الْبَقَرَ وَالْعَلَمَ ثُمَّ إِنْ شَاءَ نَكَّرَ الْإِبِل فِي الْهَدَايَا قِيَامًا أَوْ أَضْجَعَهَا وَأَيَّ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَ فَهُوَ حَسَنٌ وَالْأفْضَلُ أنْ تُنْحَرَ قِيَامًا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ نَحْرَ الْهَدَايَا قِيَامًا وَأَصَحَابُهُ كَانُوا يَنْحَرُ ونَها قِيَامًا مَعْقُولَةَ الْيَدِ الْيُسْرَى وَلَا يُذْبَحُ الْبَقَرُ وَالْغَنَمُ قِيَاماً لأَنَّ فِى حَالَةِ الْاِضْطِجَاعِ الْمَذْبَحُ أَبْيَنُ فَيَكُونُ الذَّبْحُ أَيْسَرُ وَالذَّبْحُ هُوَ السُّنَّة فيهما
ترجمہ فرمایا اور اونٹ کی قربانی کرنے میں نحر افضل ہے اور گائے اور بکری میں ذبح کرنا افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ نماز پڑھا اپنے رب کے واسطے اور تحر کر۔ اس کی تاویل میں کہا گیا کہ جزور (اونٹ) اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ تم گائے ذبح کرو ۔ اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہم نے اس کو فدیہ دیا ذبح عظیم کے ساتھ ۔ اور ذبح وہ جانور جو ذبح کے واسطے مہیا ہو ۔ اور یہ صحیح ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اونٹ کا نحر کیا اور گائے اور بکری کو ذبح کیا۔ پھر اگر چاہے تو اونٹ کو ہدایا میں کھڑا کر کے نحر کرے یا اس کو بٹھلا دے اور جو طریقہ ان میں سے اختیار کرے اچھا ہے۔ اور افضل یہ ہے کہ اس کو کھڑا کر کے نحر کرے۔ کیونکہ مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ہدایا کو کھڑا کر کے نحر کیا ہے اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے صحابہ اونٹوں کو کھڑا کر کے نحر کرتے درانحالیکہ بایاں ہاتھ باندھ دیتے تھے اور گائے اور بکری کو کھڑا کر کے ذبح نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ لٹانے کی حالت میں ذبح کرنے کی جگہ خوب ظاہر ہوتی ہے تو ذبح کرنا آسان ہوگا اور ان دونوں میں ذبح ہی سنت ہے۔
He said: And the best (afdal) in camels (budun) is nahr, and in cows and sheep is dhabh, because Allah Almighty said: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice (nahr)' [108:2]—it is said in its interpretation that it refers to the camel. And Allah Almighty said: 'Slaughter (dhabh) a cow' [2:67]. And Allah Almighty said: 'And We ransomed him with a great sacrifice (dhibh)' [37:107]. And dhabh is that which is prepared for slaughter. And it is authentically reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed nahr on camels and dhabh on cows and sheep. Then if he wishes, he may slaughter the camel in the hadaya standing or lay it down; whichever he does is good. But the best is to slaughter it standing, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed nahr on hadaya standing, and his Companions used to perform nahr on them standing with the left foot tied. And cows and sheep should not be slaughtered standing, because in a lying position the slaughter place is more visible, so slaughter is easier, and dhabh is the sunnah in both.
Translation: He said: In sacrificing a camel, nahr is better, and in cow and goat, dhabh is better. Because Allah Almighty said: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice.' It is said in its interpretation that it refers to the camel. And Allah Almighty said: 'Slaughter a cow.' And Allah Almighty said: 'And We ransomed him with a great sacrifice.' And dhabh is the animal prepared for slaughter. And it is authentic that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed nahr on camels and dhabh on cows and goats. Then if he wishes, he may perform nahr on the camel standing or lay it down; whichever he does is good. And the best is to perform nahr standing, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed nahr on hadaya standing, and his Companions used to perform nahr on them standing while tying the left hand. And cows and goats should not be slaughtered standing, because in a lying position the place of slaughter is clearly visible, so slaughter becomes easier, and dhabh is the sunnah in both.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the preferred method of sacrifice for different animals. For camels (budun), the superior method is nahr (slitting the throat at the base of the neck while standing), based on the command in Surah al-Kawthar 'wa-nhar', interpreted as referring to camels, and the practice of the Prophet. For cows and sheep, the superior method is dhabh (cutting the throat while lying on the side), based on Quranic references to dhabh of a cow and the great sacrifice, as well as prophetic practice. The text also notes that one may slaughter camels either standing or lying, but standing is better due to the Prophet's example. For cows and sheep, slaughtering standing is discouraged because the lying position exposes the throat more clearly, making the slaughter easier and more accurate. The sunnah for them is dhabh while lying down. All methods are valid, but the ruling differentiates according to the nature of the animal.

Key Terms
نحر (nahr): Cutting the throat of the camel at the base of the neck while standing; the preferred method for camels.
ذبح (dhabh): Cutting the throat of an animal while lying on the side; the method for cows, sheep, goats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the most preferred way to slaughter a camel for hadi?
A) By dhabh while lying on its side
B) By nahr while standing
C) By nahr while lying down
D) Either method is equally preferable

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that nahr (standing cut at base of neck) is preferred for camels, while dhabh (lying cut on throat) is the sunnah for cows and sheep.
