Slaughtering the Hadi Personally (Awla)
Ruling with proof on personal slaughter of hadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on personal slaughter of hadi, identify the proof from the Prophet's actions, and explain when delegation is permissible.

Core Idea
Personally slaughtering the hadi is better if you are skilled; delegation is allowed if you are not.

This passage addresses a common question during Hajj: should the pilgrim slaughter his own sacrificial animal or delegate? The Hanafi school provides a balanced answer based on the Prophet's practice and the principle that personal involvement in worship enhances humility, while also recognizing practical limitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering the hadi. The ruling is that it is awla (better/recommended) to do it personally if skilled.
'Awla' is a level above mubah but not wajib; roughly equivalent to mustahabb or sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's action during the Farewell Hajj: he personally slaughtered more than sixty camels and delegated the rest to Ali.
The hadith shows both personal action and delegation, providing a complete legal model.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's personal action indicates preference (awlawiyyah), while his delegation shows permissibility (jawaz) of deputizing.
The Hanafi inference is that personal performance is better when possible, but delegation is valid when needed.
4
Consider the exception
If a person is not skilled or finds difficulty, delegation is permitted and may even be necessary.
The text explicitly states: 'if a person is not guided to that or is not skilled, we permit delegation to others.'
5
Summarize the practical consequence
The pilgrim is encouraged to slaughter personally if able, but no sin if he delegates due to lack of skill.
This balances devotional ideal with ease (yusr), a hallmark of Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْأَولى أنْ يَتَوَلَّى ذَبْحُهَا بِنَفْسِهِ إِذَا كَانَ يُحْسِنُ ذَلِكَ لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ سَاقَ مِائَةَ بُدُنَةٌ فِى حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ فَنَحَرَنِيفًا وَسِيِّينَ بِنَفْسِهِ وَوَلَّى الْبَاقِي عَلِيًّا وَلِأَنَّهُ قُرْبَةً وَالتَوَلّى فِى الْقُرُبَاتِ أَوْلَى لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ زِيَادَةِ الْخُشُوع إِلَّا أَنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ قَدْ لَا يَهْتَدِى لِذلِكَ وَلَا يُحْسِنُهُ فَجَوَّزْنَا تَوْلِيَّةَ غَيره
ترجمہ اور اولیٰ یہ ہے کہ ہدایا کے ذبح کا خود متولی ہو بشر طیکہ ذبح کرنا اچھی طرح جانتا ہو کیونکہ روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حجتہ الوداع کے موقع پر سو بد نہ چلائے پس (ان میں سے) کچھ اوپر ساٹھ بد نہ خود نحر فرمائے اور باقی کا ذمہ دارعلی کوبنایا اور اس لئے کہ تحر کرنا ایک قربت ہے اور طاعات میں بذات خود متولی ہونا بہتر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں عاجزی زیادہ ہے مگر یہ کہ بھی انسان خود اس کی راہ نہیں پاتا اور
And it is more appropriate (awla) that he personally undertakes (yatawalla) their slaughter if he is skilled in that, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) drove one hundred camels (badanah) during the Farewell Hajj; he personally performed nahr on more than sixty of them and delegated the rest to 'Ali. And because it is an act of worship (qurbah), and undertaking personally in acts of worship is better due to the increase of humility (khushu'). However, if a person is not guided to that or is not skilled in it, we permit delegation to others.
Translation: And it is more appropriate that he personally undertakes the slaughter of the hadaya provided that he knows how to slaughter well, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) drove one hundred camels during the Farewell Hajj; he personally performed nahr on more than sixty of them and entrusted the rest to 'Ali. And because slaughter is an act of worship, and personally undertaking acts of worship is better because of the greater humility involved. However, if a person himself does not find the way or is not skilled, we permit delegation to someone else.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that it is preferable (awla) for the pilgrim to personally slaughter his hadi if he knows how to do so correctly. The proof is the Prophet's practice in the Farewell Hajj, where he personally slaughtered the majority of his sacrificial camels and delegated the rest to 'Ali. The reasoning is that slaughter is an act of worship (qurbah), and direct personal involvement increases humility and devotion (khushu'). However, the text makes an important concession: if the person is not skilled or capable, then delegating to another is permissible. This reflects the Hanafi balance between encouraging personal devotion and recognizing practical limitations. The ruling applies specifically to hadaya (sacrificial animals brought for Hajj).

Key Terms
أولى (awla): More appropriate/recommended; higher than mubah but not wajib.
قربت (qurbah): Act of worship that brings one closer to Allah; here specifically slaughter of hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding who should slaughter the hadi?
A) It must be the pilgrim himself
B) It is better for the pilgrim to do it if skilled, but delegation is allowed
C) Only a butcher may slaughter
D) The pilgrim must delegate to avoid sin

Key Takeaway
Personal slaughter of the hadi is a recommended act (sunnah muakkadah), but delegation is permissible if the pilgrim lacks skill or faces difficulty.

Charity of Hady's Cover and Nose-Rope
Ruling on giving jilal and khitam in charity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the charity of the hady's cover and nose-rope, explain the proof from the Prophet's command, and apply the ruling to ensure the butcher's wage is not taken from the hady.

Core Idea
The cover and nose-rope of a hady must be given in charity; the butcher's wage cannot be taken from them.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, Imam al-Quduri states the ruling that the covering (jilal) and nose-rope (khitam) of a sacrificial animal (hady) must be given in charity after slaughter. The commentator expands by citing the prophetic command to Ali (RA) as proof. This ruling is based on the Hanafi principle that an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wajib). Understanding this helps ensure the hady remains purely dedicated to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules that the jilal and khitam of the hady must be given in charity (tasaddaq). Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, or recommended?
The Hanafi school considers it wajib based on the imperative.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the Prophet's (PBUH) command to Ali (RA): 'Give in charity its cover and its nose-rope, and do not give the wage of the butcher from it.' Identify the type of dalil (Quran, Sunnah, etc.) and its transmission strength.
This is an ahad hadith, so its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the imperative 'تصدق' (give in charity) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless diverted.
There is no diversion here, so it remains wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may permit using the accessories for any good purpose. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: the practical difference in ruling.
The Hanafi position is more restrictive.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to give them in charity. There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِجُلَالِهَا وَ خِطَامِهَا وَلَا يُعْطَى أَجْرَةُ الْجَرَّارِ مِنْهَا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لِعَلَّى تَصَدَّقُ بِجَلَالِهَا وَ خِطَامِهَا وَلَا تُعْطَى أَجْرَةَ الْجَزَارِ مِنْهَا
He said: And he gives in charity its cover and its nose-rope, and the wage of the butcher is not given from it, due to his saying, peace be upon him, to Ali: 'Give in charity its cover and its nose-rope, and do not give the wage of the butcher from it.'
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Imam al-Quduri (in the matn) with the commentator's expansion. The ruling: The cover (jilal) and nose-rope (khitam) of a sacrificial animal (hady) must be given in charity after slaughter, and cannot be used to pay the butcher's wage. The proof is a direct command from the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) instructing exactly this. The Hanafi school follows this as a wajib (obligatory) act; the cover and rope are part of the animal and must be disposed of in a beneficial way without personal gain. The prohibition of using them for wages ensures that the entire animal remains dedicated to Allah.

Key Terms
جلال (jilal): The covering or saddlecloth placed on the hady animal.
خطام (khitam): The nose-rope or halter used to lead the hady.
أجرة الجزار (ujrat al-jazzar): The wage paid to the butcher for slaughtering the hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They may be kept by the owner.
D) They must be burned after slaughter.

Key Takeaway
The jilal and khitam of a hady must be given in charity; they cannot be used for the butcher's wage.

Riding the Hady When Necessary
Conditions for riding the hady animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riding the hady animal and identify the condition that permits it.

Core Idea
The hady is dedicated to Allah; riding it is prohibited unless compelled by necessity.

The hady animal is set aside purely for Allah. Normally, deriving any personal benefit from it, such as riding, is not allowed. However, the Hanafi school recognizes an exception when the person driving the animal is genuinely in need of a ride. This lesson examines the ruling, its condition, and the supporting evidence from the Prophet’s practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is riding the badanah (hady animal). The default ruling is prohibition: 'if he is independent of that, he does not ride it.'
The animal is dedicated exclusively to Allah.
2
Locate the exception
The text states: 'if he is compelled to riding it, he rides it.' The exception is necessity (idtirar).
The condition of being mudtarr (compelled) is key.
3
Examine the dalil
The Prophet (peace be upon him) saw a man driving a badanah and said: 'Ride it, woe to you!' This indicates permissibility in the given context.
Hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'irkab' is interpreted as permissive (ibahah) due to the context of need, not as obligatory. The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarinah shifting it to ibahah.
The qarinah here is the driver's incapability and need.
5
Evaluate the authoritative weight
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi. It is accepted in the Hanafi school.
The mufta bihi position: riding is only permissible when the person is unable to walk and has no other ride.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ سَاقَ بَدَنَةً فَاضْطَرَّ إلى رُكُوبِهَا رَكِبَهَا وَإِنِ اسْتَغْنَى عَنْ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَرْكَبُهَا لِأَنَّهُ جَعَلَهَا خَالِصًا لِلَّهِ فَلَا يَسْعَى أن يَصْرِفَ شَيْئًا مِنْ عَيْنِهَا أَوْ مَنَا فِيهَا إِلى نَفْسِهِ إلى أن يَبْلُغَ مَحلَّهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَحتاج إلى رُكُوبِهَا لِمَا رُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَأَى رَجُلًا يَسُوقُ بَدَنَةً فَقَالَ إِرْكَبُهَا وَيلك وَتَأْوِيلُهُ أَنَّهُ كَانَ عَاجِزًا مُحْتَاجًا
And whoever drives a badanah and is compelled to riding it, he rides it; and if he is independent of that, he does not ride it, because he has made it exclusively for Allah, so he should not seek to divert anything of its essence or its benefits to himself until it reaches its destination, except if he needs to ride it, because it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) saw a man driving a badanah and said: 'Ride it, woe to you!' and its interpretation is that he was incapable and needy.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on riding the hady animal. The general principle is that since the animal is dedicated purely to Allah, deriving any personal benefit from it (like riding) is not allowed until it reaches its slaughter place. However, an exception is made if the person driving it is exhausted and has no other means of conveyance. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered a man to ride his badanah, indicating permission in cases of need. The Hanafi school interprets this as a dispensation for genuine necessity, not a general permission. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow brought for sacrifice as hady.
مضطر (mudtarr): One who is compelled due to exhaustion or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At any time during the journey.
B) Only if the animal is about to die.
C) When the driver is tired and has no other means of conveyance.
D) It is never permissible.

Key Takeaway
Riding a hady animal is only permissible when the driver is compelled by necessity; otherwise it is prohibited because the animal is dedicated to Allah.

Liability for Damage and Milk of the Hady
Expansion of rulings on hady damage and milk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings: compensation for damage from riding the hady, and the charity obligation for milk if used personally, and distinguish when milking is allowed.

Core Idea
The hady is sacred property; any damage or personal use requires compensation or charity.

The hady (sacrificial animal) is dedicated to Allah and thus its corpus and benefits are inviolable. This passage from the Hidayah addresses two practical issues: what happens if the pilgrim rides the hady and causes a loss in value, and what rules apply to the milk of a female hady. Understanding these rulings reinforces the principle that a dedicated animal remains in divine ownership, and any personal benefit taken from it must be compensated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two subjects
The passage covers two distinct rulings: (1) compensation for decrease in value from riding the hady, and (2) management of the milk of a female hady.
2
Analyze the damage ruling
If riding the hady causes a visible decrease in its value, the rider must pay compensation (dhaman) equal to the amount of the loss. This is because the animal is guaranteed (maddamun 'alayh) and any misuse requires replacement.
The compensation is wajib.
3
Distinguish milk scenarios by time
If the slaughter time is near, do not milk; instead sprinkle cold water on the udder to stop lactation. If the slaughter time is far, milking is allowed to prevent harm to the animal, but the milk must be given in charity.
The key factor is the proximity to dhabh (slaughter).
4
Apply the charity rule if used
If the pilgrim milks the hady and uses the milk for his own need (not charity), he must give in charity the equivalent amount of milk or its monetary value.
This is because the milk is part of the animal's corpus and is guaranteed.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The rulings are based on the principle that the hady is maddamun 'alayh – its benefits are not ownerless. Any personal use requires compensation (either by replacing the benefit or giving its value in charity).
This distinguishes the hady from ordinary livestock.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ رَكِبَهَا فَانْتَقَصَ بِرُكُوبِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ ضِمَانُ مَا نَقَصَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهَا لَئِنْ لَمْ يَحْلِبُهَا لِأَنَّ اللَّبَنَ مُتَوَكَّدٌ مِنْهَا فَلَا يَصْرِفُهُ إِلى حَاجَةٍ نَفْسِهِ وَيَنْضِحُ ضَرْعَهَا بِالْمَاءِ الْبَارِدِ حَتَّى يُنْقَطِعَ اللَّبَنُ وَلَكِنْ هَذَا إِذَا كَانَ قَرِيبًا مِنْ وَقْتِ الدَّبْح فَإِنْ كَانَ بَعِيدًا مِنْهُ يَحْلِبُهَا وَ يَتَصَدَّقُ بِلَبَنِهَا كَيلَا يَضُرَّ ذَلِكَ بِهَا وَإِنْ صَرَفَهُ إِلَى حَاجَةِ نَفْسِهِ تَصَدَّقَ بمثله أو بِقِيْمَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ مَضْمُونَ عَلَيْهِ
And if he rides it and it decreases by his riding, then upon him is compensation for what decreased of that. And if it is a female with milk, he does not milk it because the milk is produced from it, so he should not divert it to his own need. And he sprinkles its udder with cold water until the milk stops. But this is when the time of slaughter is near. If it is far from it, he milks it and gives its milk in charity so that it does not harm her. And if he diverts it to his own need, he gives in charity its like or its value because it is guaranteed upon him.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings. First, if riding the hady causes a loss in its value, the rider must compensate for the exact amount of the loss (dhaman). Second, regarding the milk of a female hady: if the slaughter time is near, she should not be milked; instead, cold water is sprinkled on her udder to stop milk production. If the slaughter time is far, milking is allowed to prevent harm to the animal, and the milk must be given in charity. If one uses the milk for himself, he must give in charity the equivalent or its value. The reasoning is that the milk is part of the animal's corpus (muta'akkid) and is maddamun 'alayh (guaranteed), so misuse requires compensation. These rulings derive from the principle that a dedicated hady remains in the ownership of Allah, and any personal benefit taken requires replacement.

Key Terms
ضمان (dhaman): Liability to compensate for loss or damage caused.
نضح (naddaha): Sprinkling water on the udder to stop lactation.
مضمون عليه (maddamun 'alayh): That which is guaranteed and must be compensated if misused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what must a pilgrim do if he uses the milk of his female hady for himself when the slaughter time is far?
A) Nothing, because the milk is his property.
B) He must give in charity the equivalent milk or its value.
C) He must slaughter the animal immediately.
D) He is excused if he did not intend harm.

Key Takeaway
The hady is guaranteed; riding it requires compensation for any decrease, and its milk, if taken for personal use, requires charity of its like or value.

Replacement of Hady When Lost or Defective
Ruling on voluntary vs. obligatory hady when lost or defective

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between voluntary and obligatory hady and state the replacement ruling for each.

Core Idea
Voluntary hady is tied to the specific animal; obligatory hady remains a liability that must be replaced.

When a hady animal dies or becomes incapacitated before sacrifice, the ruling depends on its nature. In this passage from al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani explains the distinction between voluntary and obligatory hady, and also addresses severe defects. Understanding this distinction is crucial for fulfilling Hajj obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the loss or incapacitation of a hady animal. The ruling varies: for voluntary hady, no replacement; for obligatory hady, replacement is required.
The text explicitly states 'laysa 'alayhi ghayruhu' and 'alayhi an yuqima ghayrahu maqamahu'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (talil): voluntary hady is attached to the specific animal; obligatory hady is a liability on the person.
No direct Quran or hadith is cited; the reasoning is based on the nature of obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For voluntary: 'al-qurbatu ta'allaqat bi hadha al-mahall' – the devotion is tied to this specific animal. For obligatory: 'al-wajibu baqin fi dhimmatihi' – the obligation remains in his liability.
This distinguishes between a 'mahall-specific' act and a 'dhimmah-based' obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools require replacement for voluntary hady if the animal dies due to owner's negligence. The Hanafi school holds no replacement in any case.
Cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position (no replacement for voluntary) is the mufta bihi and is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The text does not discuss negligence; the ruling is absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ سَاقَ هَدْيًا فَعَطَبَ فَإِنْ كَانَ تَطَوُّعًا فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ لِأَنَّ الْقُرْبَةَ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِهَذَا الْمَحَلَّ وَ قَدْ فَاتَ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَنْ وَاجِب فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُقِيمَ غَيْرَهُ مَقَامَهُ لأَنَّ الْوَاجِبِ بَاقٍ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ عَيْبُ كَثِيرُ يُقَامُ غَيْرُهُ مَقَامَهُ لِأَنَّ الْمُعِ بِمِثْلِهِ لَا يَتَأَدَّى بِهِ الْوَاجِبُ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ وَصَنَعَ بِالْمُعِيبِ مَا شَاءَ لِأَنَّهُ الْتَحَقَ بِسَائِرٍ أَمْلَارَكم
And whoever drives a hady and it becomes incapacitated: if it is voluntary, then there is no other upon him because the act of devotion is attached to this specific animal and it has been lost; and if it is from an obligation, then upon him is to place another in its place because the obligation remains in his liability; and if a severe defect befalls it, another is placed in its place because the defective [animal] with such defect does not fulfill the obligation, so there must be another; and he may do with the defective what he wishes because it has rejoined the rest of his property [؟].
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between voluntary (tatawwu') and obligatory (wajib) hady. If a voluntary hady dies or becomes incapacitated before reaching the slaughter place, there is no replacement required because the act of devotion was specifically tied to that animal (mahall). Once it is lost, the devotion is lost; no substitute is due. However, if the hady was obligatory (e.g., for a violation during Hajj), the obligation remains on the person's liability (dhimmah), so he must replace it with another animal. The same applies if the animal develops a severe defect ('ayb kathir) that renders it unsuitable for sacrifice; a replacement must be provided, and the defective animal can then be disposed of as the owner wishes (since it reverts to being his property). The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, and the tarjih within the Hanafi school is that this is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary act of devotion, not obligatory.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory act, here specifically hady due to a Hajj violation or vow.
عيب كثير ('ayb kathir): A severe defect that makes the animal unsuitable for sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a person's obligatory hady dies before reaching the slaughter place?
A) No replacement needed; the obligation is waived.
B) He must replace it with another animal.
C) He must give the value in charity.
D) He must fast instead.

Key Takeaway
The obligation to replace hady depends on its nature: voluntary hady is animal-specific, obligatory hady is a liability that must be fulfilled.

Riding and Milking the Hady: Conditions and Compensation
Ruling on compensation for riding and milking Hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on riding and milking the Hady and apply the conditions that determine the required compensation or charity.

Core Idea
Using the Hady for personal benefit requires compensation; its milk is sacred but can be given in charity when necessary.

The Hady is a sacrificial animal dedicated solely to Allah. While a pilgrim may need to ride or milk it, such actions are not unrestricted. This lesson explains when these actions are permitted, when they require compensation or charity, and the critical factor of proximity to slaughter time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions on the Hady
The passage covers two actions: riding the Hady and milking it. Recognize that each has different rulings based on conditions.
2
Determine the ruling for riding
Riding the Hady is permissible, but if it causes a decrease in value, compensation (daman) is wajib. Identify the cause: the riding itself leads to loss.
Compensation is measured by the decrease in value.
3
Determine the ruling for milking
Milking is prohibited when slaughter is near; if far, it is allowed but the milk must be given in charity. The key condition is the time remaining until slaughter.
If near, sprinkle cold water to stop milk; if far, milk and give charity.
4
Apply the consequence of personal use
If the milk is used for personal need (even if from a far-time milking), the user must give charity of its like or value because the milk is 'guaranteed' (madmun 'alayh).
Daman applies to the milk as it is part of the Hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر ہدی پر سوار ہوادار سواری کی وجہ سے کوئی نقص پیدا ہو گیا اس پر ضمان لازم ہے اگر دودھ ہے تو دودھ نہ دو ھے
وَلَوْ رَكِبَهَا فَانْتَقَصَ بِرُكُوبِهِ فَعَلَيْهِ ضِمَانُ مَا نَقَصَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهَا لَبَنٌ لَمْ يَحْلِبُهَا لِأَنَّ اللَّبَنَ مُتَوَكِّدٌ مِنْهَا فَلَا يَصْرِفُهُ إِلَى حَاجَةِ نَفْسِهِ وَيَنْضِحُ ضَرْعَهَا بِالْمَاءِ الْبَارِدِ حَتَّى يَنْقَطِعَ اللَّبَنُ وَلَكِنْ هَذَا إِذَا كَانَ قَرِيبًا مِنْ وَقْتِ الذَّبْحِ فَإِنْ كَانَ بَعِيدًا مِنْهُ يَحْلِبُهَا وَيَتَصَدَّقُ بِلَبَنِهَا كَيْلَا يَضُرَّ ذَلِكَ بِهَا وَإِنْ صَرَفَهُ إِلَى حَاجَةِ نَفْسِهِ تَصَدَّقَ بِمِثْلِهِ أَوْ بِقِيمَتِهِ لِأَنَّهُ مَضْمُونٌ عَلَيْهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر اس پر یہ سوار ہو گیا پھر اس کی سواری کی وجہ سے اس میں نقص آگیا تو اس کی وجہ سے جو کچھ اس میں نقصان آئے گا وہ اس کا ضامن بنے۔ اور اگر مادہ ہدی کے لئے دودھ ہو تو وہ اس کو نہ دو ہے۔ کیونکہ دودھ اسی جانور سے پیدا ہوا ہے تو اس کو اپنی ذاتی ضرورت میں صرف نہ کرے اور اس کے تھنوں پر ٹھنڈے پانی کی چھینٹیں مارتا ر ہے تا کہ دودھ آنا بند ہو جائے۔ لیکن یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ ذبح کا پر وقت قریب ہو۔ اور اگر وقت ذبح دور ہو تو اسکو دو ہے اور اس کا دودھ مساکین پر صدقہ کر دے تاکہ تھنوں کا دودھ اس کو ضر ر نہ پہنچائے ۔ اور اگر دودھ کو اس نے اپنی ضرورت میں صرف کیا تو اس کے مثل کا یا اس کی قیمت کا صدقہ کر دے کیونکہ یہ دودھ مضمون علیہ ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم بدی کے جانور پر سوار ہوا اور سواری کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کی مالیت میں نقصان پیدا ہو گیا تو جس قدر نقصان آیا ہے اس کا یہ شخص ضامن ہو گا یعنی بقدر نقصان صدقہ کر دے۔ اور اگر ہدی مادہ جانور ہے اور وہ دودھ دیتا ہے تو محرم اس کا دودھ نہ نکالے۔ کیونکہ دودھ بھی اسی سے پیدا ہوا ہے اس لئے اس کو اپنی ضرورت میں خرچ نہ کرے ور اس کے تھنوں پر ٹھنڈے پانی سے چھینٹا مارتا رہے تا کہ دودھ سوکھ جائے۔ لیکن یہ حکم کس وقت ہے جبکہ قربانی کا وقت قریب ہو۔ اور اگر وقت ذبح دور ہو تو اس کو دوہ لے اور اس کے دودھ کو صدقہ کر دے تا کہ تھنوں کا دودھ اس کو ضرر نہ پہنچائے اور اگر اس دودھ کو اپنے مصرف میں لایا تو اس کا مثل صدقہ کر دے یعنی اس قدر صدقہ کر دے کیونکہ دودھ مثل ہے یا اس کی قیمت صدقہ کر دے۔ کیونکہ قیمت بھی مثل معنوی ہے۔ دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ اس پر دودھ کا ضمان واجب ہے۔ اور جس چیز کا ضمان لازم ہو اس کا یہی حکم ہے کہ وہ مشکلی ہے تو اس کا مثل دے اور اگر مثل میسر نہ ہو تو قیمت دے۔
And if he rode it and it decreased due to his riding, then he is responsible for the compensation of what decreased from that. And if it has milk, he should not milk it because the milk is a part of it, so he should not use it for his own need. And he should sprinkle its udder with cold water until the milk stops. But this is when the time of slaughter is near. If it is far, he should milk it and give its milk in charity so that it does not harm it. And if he used it for his own need, he should give in charity its like or its value because it is guaranteed upon him.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the Hady (sacrificial animal) brought for Hajj. The passage covers two scenarios: first, if a person rides the Hady animal and causes a decrease in its value, he must compensate for the loss by giving charity equal to the decrease. Second, if the Hady is a female with milk, the owner must not milk it for personal use, as the milk is considered part of the animal dedicated to Allah. If the slaughter time is near, he should sprinkle the udder with cold water to stop milk production. If slaughter is far off, he should milk it and give the milk in charity to prevent harm to the animal. If he uses the milk himself, he must give its equivalent or value in charity because it is considered a guaranteed (madhmun) item. The commentary emphasizes that compensation is wajib, and if the thing is available, give its like; otherwise, its value.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): The sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj or Umrah, whether voluntary or obligatory.
ضمان (daman): Compensation or guarantee for loss or damage, here meaning monetary or in-kind charity.
مضمون عليه (madmun 'alayh): That which is guaranteed or under liability; the milk is considered guaranteed and cannot be used without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person uses the milk of the Hady for his own need when slaughter time is near, what must he do?
A) He must sacrifice the animal immediately.
B) He must give charity of the milk's like or value.
C) He may keep the milk without penalty.
D) He must return the milk to the udder.

Key Takeaway
The Hady's milk is like its body: it cannot be used for personal gain; if used, charity is wajib, and riding that causes damage requires compensation.

Ruling on Hady that Dies or Becomes Defective
Ruling on replacement of Hady upon death or defect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on replacement of Hady when it dies or becomes defective, distinguishing between voluntary and obligatory Hady.

Core Idea
A voluntary Hady need not be replaced; an obligatory Hady must be replaced because the obligation remains in the liability.

The sacrifice of Hady during Hajj is a significant act of worship, but what happens if the animal dies or becomes defective before sacrifice? This lesson from the Hanafi school clarifies the ruling based on whether the Hady was voluntary or obligatory. Understanding this distinction protects you from unnecessary obligations and ensures proper fulfillment of duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of Hady
Determine if the Hady is voluntary (tatawwu') or obligatory (wajib). This is the key factor governing the ruling.
Obligatory Hady includes that due for tamattu', qiran, or a vow.
2
Apply the ruling for death or loss
If voluntary, no replacement is required because the act of devotion was tied to that specific animal. If obligatory, replacement is wajib because the obligation remains in the dhimma.
3
Apply the ruling for a major defect
If a major defect ('ayb kathir) occurs, the same distinction applies: replacement only for obligatory Hady, as the defective animal cannot fulfill the obligation.
Minor defects are overlooked.
4
Disposition of the defective animal
The defective animal becomes the owner's property to do with as he wishes, like any other possession.
He may sell it, use it, or sacrifice it as nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس نے ہدی کو چلایا پھر وہ ہلاک ہوگئی اگر نفلی ہدی ہے اس پر اس کا بدل لازم نہیں
وَمَنْ سَاقَ هَدْيًا فَعَطِبَ فَإِنْ كَانَ تَطَوُّعًا فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ غَيْرُهُ لِأَنَّ الْقُرْبَةَ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِهَذَا الْمَحَلِّ وَقَدْ فَاتَ وَإِنْ كَانَ عَنْ وَاجِبٍ فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يُقِيمَ غَيْرَهُ مَقَامَهُ لِأَنَّ الْوَاجِبَ بَاقٍ فِي ذِمَّتِهِ وَإِنْ أَصَابَهُ عَيْبٌ كَثِيرٌ يُقَامُ غَيْرُهُ مَقَامَهُ لِأَنَّ الْمُعِيبَ لَا يَتَأَدَّى بِهِ الْوَاجِبُ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ وَصَنَعَ بِالْمَعِيبِ مَا شَاءَ لِأَنَّهُ الْتَحَقَ بِسَائِرِ أَمْلَاكِهِ
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے ہدی چلائی پھر وہ ہلاک ہو گئی پس اگر وہ بدی نفلی ہو تو اس پر دوسری واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قربت تو اسی محل کے ساتھ متعلق ہوئی تھی اور وہ محل فوت ہو گیا اور اگر وہ ہدی واجب ہو تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ دوسرے کو اس کی جگہ قائم کرے کیونکہ واجب اسکے ذمہ میں باقی ہے۔ اور اگر اس میں بہت عیب آگیا تو بھی اس کی جگہ دوسری ہدی قائم کی جائے کیونکہ جو جانور عیب کثیر کے ساتھ عیب دار ہو تو اس کے ساتھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور دوسرے کی ضرورت ہوگی۔ اور عیب دار کے ساتھ جو چاہے کرے کیونکہ یہ بھی اس کے باقی املاک میں مل گیا۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص ہدی لے کر گیا لیکن ہدی ہلاک ہوگئی تو اب اگر وہ ہدی نفلی ہے تو اس پر دوسری ہدی واجب نہ ہوگی کیونکہ طاعت و قربت اسی محل یعنی اس بدی کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور وہ فوت ہو گئی۔ اور اگر وہ ہدی واجب ہے تو اسپر اس کی جگہ دوسری ہدی واجب ہوگی۔ کیونکہ واجب اس کے ذمہ میں باقی ہے صرف خریدنے سے اس کا ذمہ پاک نہ ہو گا۔ جب تک کہ ہدی اپنے محل پر نہ پہنچ جائے ۔ اور اگر بدی کے جانور میں عیب بہت پیدا ہو گیا تو بھی اس کی جگہ دوسری ہدی قائم کی جائے۔ کیونکہ عیب کثیر کی صورت میں واجب ادا نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے دوسری ہدی کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور جو ہدی عیب دار ہے اس کا جو چاہے کرے کیونکہ وہ اس کی دوسری مملوکہ چیزوں کے ساتھ لاحق ہوگئی ۔
And whoever brought a Hady and it became disabled, if it was voluntary, then there is no other upon him because the act of devotion was tied to this specific one and it is gone. If it was obligatory, then upon him is to replace it because the obligation remains in his liability. And if a major defect affects it, then another is put in its place because the defective one does not fulfill the obligation, so another is necessary. And he may do with the defective one as he wishes because it joins the rest of his properties.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between voluntary (nafl) and obligatory (wajib) Hady. If a voluntary Hady dies or is lost, no replacement is needed because the act of worship was specific to that animal and has already been attempted. However, if the Hady was obligatory (e.g., due to a vow or as a penalty for a Hajj violation), the obligation remains in the person's liability (dhimma), so he must replace it with another animal. Similarly, if a major defect arises (e.g., blindness, broken leg), it must be replaced because a defective animal cannot fulfill the wajib. The defective animal then becomes the owner's property to do with as he wishes, like any other possession.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary act of worship, here specifically voluntary Hady.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory act, here Hady that is due as a religious duty (e.g., for tamattu', qiran, or vow).
عيب كثير ('ayb kathir): Major defect that prevents the animal from being suitable for sacrifice (e.g., severe lameness, blindness).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person brings a voluntary Hady and it dies on the way, what is the ruling?
A) He must replace it with another animal.
B) He must give charity equivalent to its value.
C) No replacement is required.
D) He must sacrifice it and distribute the meat.

Key Takeaway
The replacement of Hady is only required when it is obligatory; a voluntary Hady that dies or becomes defective does not require replacement.

Ruling on a Disabled Badanah (Hady)
Ruling on treating a disabled voluntary or obligatory Badanah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the Hanafi ruling for a disabled voluntary and obligatory Hady (badanah) and explain the dalil from the hadith of Najiyyah al-Aslami.

Core Idea
A disabled voluntary Hady must be slaughtered and given to the poor; an obligatory Hady must be replaced.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario during Hajj: an animal designated for sacrifice (Hady) becomes disabled before reaching its destination. The ruling distinguishes between voluntary and obligatory Hady, with clear actions based on a Prophetic command. By studying this, you will learn how the Hanafi school handles unexpected obstacles in devotional acts and the rationale behind the required actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of Hady
First, recognize that the passage distinguishes between voluntary (nafl) Hady and obligatory (wajib) Hady. This distinction determines the subsequent legal consequences.
Voluntary Hady is offered purely for devotion; obligatory Hady is required by a vow, penalty, or as part of a specific Hajj type.
2
Outline the required actions for voluntary Hady
For a voluntary badanah that becomes disabled, the owner must slaughter it, dye its necklace (or sandal) with blood, and strike its hump with blood to mark it as Hady. The owner and any rich person may not eat from it; only the poor may eat.
These actions serve to identify the animal as Hady and ensure its distribution to the needy.
3
Determine the ruling for obligatory Hady
If the disabled Hady was obligatory, the owner must replace it with another animal. The disabled one becomes the owner's property to dispose of as he wishes, since it is no longer suitable for its original purpose.
The original obligation is not fulfilled by the disabled animal; a sound replacement is required.
4
Analyze the dalil: hadith of Najiyyah al-Aslami
The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded Najiyyah to perform these actions for a disabled voluntary Hady. This explicit command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul, even though the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
The command is the primary evidence; Hanafis consider it binding for voluntary Hady under these circumstances.
5
Understand the legal rationale (ta'lil)
The permission to consume the Hady is conditional on its reaching the sacred precincts (mahall). Before that, consumption is unlawful. However, allowing it to become carrion is wasteful; feeding the poor is a form of devotion and fulfills the purpose of drawing near to Allah.
This rationale explains why the owner cannot eat from it even after slaughtering it on the way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بدنہ راستے میں ہلاک ہو گیا اگر نفلی بد نہ تھا اسے نحر کرے اور اسکے نعل کو خون سے رنگ دے اور کچھ اس کی کہان پر لگا دے نہ خود اور نہ اغنیاء اس سے کھائیں
وَإِذَا عَطِبَتِ الْبَدَنَةُ فِي الطَّرِيقِ فَإِنْ كَانَ تَطَوُّعًا نَحَرَهَا وَصَبَغَ نَعْلَهَا بِدَمِهَا وَضَرَبَ بِهَا صَفْحَةَ سَنَامِهَا وَلَا يَأْكُلُ هُوَ وَلَا غَيْرُهُ مِنَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ بِذَلِكَ أَمَرَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَاجِيَةَ الْأَسْلَمِيَّ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالنَّعْلِ قِلَادَتُهَا وَفَائِدَةُ ذَلِكَ أَنْ يَعْلَمَ النَّاسُ أَنَّهَا هَدْيٌ فَيَأْكُلَ مِنْهَا الْفُقَرَاءُ دُونَ الْأَغْنِيَاءِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْإِذْنَ فِي تَنَاوُلِهَا مُعَلَّقٌ بِشَرْطِ بُلُوغِهَا مَحَلَّهَا فَيَنْبَغِي أَنْ لَا يَحِلَّ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ أَصْلًا إِلَّا أَنَّ التَّصَدُّقَ عَلَى الْفُقَرَاءِ أَفْضَلُ مِنْ أَنْ يَتْرُكَهَا جَزْرَ السِّبَاعِ وَفِيهِ نَوْعُ تَقَرُّبٍ وَالتَّقَرُّبُ هُوَ الْمَقْصُودُ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ وَاجِبَةً أَقَامَ غَيْرَهَا مَقَامَهَا وَصَنَعَ بِهَا مَا شَاءَ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَبْقَ صَالِحًا لِمَا عَيَّنَهُ وَهُوَ مِلْكُهُ كَسَائِرِ أَمْلَاكِهِ
ترجمہ اور اگر راستہ میں بد نہ ہلاک ہو گیا پس اگر یہ بد نہ نفلی ہو تو اس کو نحر کر دے اور اس کے نعل اس کے خون سے رنگ دے اور اس کے کوہان پر اس کے خون کا چھاپہ مار دے اور نہ اس کو خود کھائے اور نہ اس کے علاوہ دوسرے مالدار لوگ کھا نہیں ۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ناجیہ اسلمی کو اسی کا حکم کیا تھا۔ اور فعل سے مراد اس کا قلادہ ہے اور فائدہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ لوگ جان لیں کہ یہ ہدی ہے۔ پس اس میں سے فقراء ہی کھائیں نہ کہ مالدار لوگ اور اس لئے کہ اس کے تناول کی اجازت مشروط ہے اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ وہ اپنے محل کو پہنچ جائے۔ پس مناسب ہے کہ اس سے پہلے بالکل حلال نہ ہو مگر یہ کہ اس کو فقراء پر صدقہ کرنا افضل ہے اس ہے کہ اس کو درندوں کی غذا چھوڑے اور فقراء پر تصدق میں ایک طرح کا تقرب حاصل ہے اور تقرب ہی مقصود ہے۔ اور اگر وہ بد نہ واجب ہدی تھا تو اس کی جگہ دوسرا قائم کرے اور ہر نہ مذبوحہ کے ساتھ جو چاہے کرے کیونکہ یہ اس چیز کے واسطے لائق نہیں رہا جس کے لئے اس کو نا مزد کیا تھا اور وہ ہدی اس کی ملک ہے جیسے اس کی دیگر املاک ہیں ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ہدی کا بد نہ راستہ میں ہلاک ہونے کے قریب ہو گیا تو اب اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں یہ بد نہ نکلی ہو گا یا واجب ہو گا۔ اگر نفلی ہے تو اس کو نحر کر دے اور اس کے خون سے اس کے نعل او کو ہان کو آلودہ کر دے اور اس میں سے نہ خود کھائے اور نہ دوسرے
And when the she-camel (badanah) becomes disabled on the way, if it is voluntary, slaughter it, dye its sandal (necklace) with its blood, and strike its hump. He should not eat from it, nor should any rich person. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, commanded Najiyyah al-Aslami with that. What is meant by 'na'l' is its necklace. The benefit is that people may know it is a Hady, so the poor eat from it, not the rich. This is because permission to consume it is conditioned on its reaching its place. So it should not be lawful at all before that, except that giving it in charity to the poor is better than leaving it as prey for beasts, and in that is a type of devotion, and devotion is the objective. If it was obligatory, he puts another in its place and does with it what he wishes because it is no longer suitable for what he designated, and it is his property like the rest of his properties.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This ruling with proof covers a specific case: a badanah (camel) designated as Hady becomes disabled on the way. If it was voluntary, the owner should slaughter it, mark it with blood (dyeing its necklace and hump) so people know it is Hady, and then only the poor may eat from it; the owner and the rich are prohibited. This is based on the hadith of Najiyyah al-Aslami. The rationale is that the permission to consume the Hady is conditional upon it reaching its destination (the Haram), so it is normally unlawful before that. However, charity to the poor is preferred over letting it become carrion for beasts. If the Hady was obligatory, it must be replaced with another animal, and the disabled one becomes the owner's property to dispose of as he wishes, as it is no longer suitable for the designated purpose.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel or cow brought for sacrifice as Hady, specifically mentioned for its size and value.
نعل (na'l): Here means the necklace (qiladah) of the Hady, not a sandal; it is marked with blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for the required actions on a disabled voluntary Hady?
A) Analogy (qiyas) with obligatory Hady
B) The command of the Prophet to Najiyyah al-Aslami
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) The owner's personal preference

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires specific actions for a disabled voluntary Hady to preserve its sacred status, while an obligatory Hady must be replaced; both rules stem from a Prophetic command and the principle of conditional permission.
